linux-mm Patch Review

2026-03-17 (4)

Minor Issues mm: introduce a new page type for page pool in page type 🔗 Byungchul Park 1p
The patch replaces pp_magic-based page pool page identification with a dedicated PGTY_netpp page type, removes page_pool_page_is_pp() and related APIs, and adds a page_type field to struct net_iov at the same offset as struct page so PageNetpp() works for both. The approach is structurally correct, but the newly introduced net_iov->page_type field is not initialized to UINT_MAX in either net_iov allocation path, causing VM_BUG_ON_PAGE to fire in CONFIG_DEBUG_VM builds on the first net_mp_niov_set_page_pool() call.
drivers include net page_alloc
From: reviewer

[PATCH v5] mm: introduce a new page type for page pool in page type

Overall the approach is clean.  I traced the set/clear symmetry in
page_pool_set_pp_info()/page_pool_clear_pp_info(), verified the
static_assert that pins net_iov->page_type at the same offset as
page->page_type, confirmed the netmem_is_pp() cast is safe under that
guarantee, and checked that the free-path sanity check in
free_page_prepare() is correctly gated by is_check_pages_enabled().
One issue found when cross-referencing the net_iov allocation paths.

> diff --git a/include/net/netmem.h b/include/net/netmem.h

[ ... ]

> +	unsigned int page_type;
>  	enum net_iov_type type;
>  	struct net_iov_area *owner;
>  };
>
> +#define NET_IOV_ASSERT_OFFSET(pg, iov)			\
> +	static_assert(offsetof(struct page, pg) ==	\
> +		      offsetof(struct net_iov, iov))
> +NET_IOV_ASSERT_OFFSET(page_type, page_type);

Good, the compile-time assertion locks in the structural requirement.

> diff --git a/net/core/page_pool.c b/net/core/page_pool.c

[ ... ]

> +	page = (struct page *)((__force unsigned long)netmem & ~NET_IOV);
> +	__SetPageNetpp(page);

PAGE_TYPE_OPS expands __SetPageNetpp() to:

    if (PageNetpp(page))
        return;
    VM_BUG_ON_PAGE(data_race(page->page_type) != UINT_MAX, page);
    page->page_type = (unsigned int)PGTY_netpp << 24;

When netmem wraps a net_iov, 'page' points into the net_iov and
page->page_type aliases net_iov->page_type.  The problem is that
net_iov->page_type is not initialised to UINT_MAX in either allocation
path before the first call to page_pool_set_pp_info():

  io_uring/zcrx.c allocates niovs with __GFP_ZERO so page_type = 0.
  net/core/devmem.c uses plain kvmalloc_objs() without __GFP_ZERO
  so page_type is uninitialised garbage.

In both cases VM_BUG_ON_PAGE(page_type != UINT_MAX) fires in
CONFIG_DEBUG_VM builds on the first net_mp_niov_set_page_pool() call
for a freshly allocated niov.  Production kernels are unaffected (the
assignment to PGTY_netpp << 24 still executes), but debug kernels will
BUG() during io_uring zero-copy receive or dmabuf devmem setup.

Could 'niov->page_type = UINT_MAX' be added to the net_iov
initialisation loops in io_uring/zcrx.c (alongside the niov->type and
niov->owner assignments) and in net/core/devmem.c (alongside the
niov->type and niov->owner assignments)?

> diff --git a/mm/page_alloc.c b/mm/page_alloc.c

[ ... ]

> +	if (unlikely(page_has_type(page))) {
> +		/* networking expects to clear its page type before releasing */
> +		if (is_check_pages_enabled()) {
> +			if (unlikely(PageNetpp(page))) {
> +				bad_page(page, "page_pool leak");
> +				return false;
> +			}
> +		}
> +		/* Reset the page_type (which overlays _mapcount) */
> +		page->page_type = UINT_MAX;
> +	}

The is_check_pages_enabled() gating and the unconditional reset to
UINT_MAX look correct.  Verified that __ClearPageNetpp() in
page_pool_clear_pp_info() also restores UINT_MAX on the normal release
path, so set/clear symmetry is preserved.
Looks Good mm: filemap: fix nr_pages calculation overflow in filemap_map_pages() v2+ 🔗 Baolin Wang 1p
The patch fixes an unsigned integer underflow in filemap_map_pages() where a concurrent truncation between next_uptodate_folio() and the file_end/end_pgoff recalculation can leave xas.xa_index > end_pgoff, causing nr_pages to wrap to a huge value and set_pte_range() to map far beyond the folio boundary. The fix moves the end_pgoff recalculation before next_uptodate_folio() so any returned folio is guaranteed to satisfy xas.xa_index <= end_pgoff.
Newer versions: v1
filemap
From: <reviewer>
Subject: Re: [PATCH] mm: filemap: fix nr_pages calculation overflow in
         filemap_map_pages()

On [date], Baolin Wang wrote:

> diff --git a/mm/filemap.c b/mm/filemap.c
> --- a/mm/filemap.c
> +++ b/mm/filemap.c

[ ... ]

> +	/*
> +	 * Recalculate end_pgoff based on file_end before calling
> +	 * next_uptodate_folio() to avoid races with concurrent
> +	 * truncation.
> +	 */
> +	file_end = DIV_ROUND_UP(i_size_read(mapping->host), PAGE_SIZE) - 1;
> +	end_pgoff = min(end_pgoff, file_end);
> +
>  	rcu_read_lock();
>  	folio = next_uptodate_folio(&xas, mapping, end_pgoff);
>  	if (!folio)
>  		goto out;
>  
> -	file_end = DIV_ROUND_UP(i_size_read(mapping->host), PAGE_SIZE) - 1;
> -	end_pgoff = min(end_pgoff, file_end);

The underflow is confirmed.  xas_next_entry() inside
next_uptodate_folio() limits its scan to end_pgoff, so a returned
folio's head index satisfies xas.xa_index <= end_pgoff only when
end_pgoff is already clamped to the current i_size.  In the old
ordering, end_pgoff was narrowed after the folio was in hand, leaving
the window where a concurrent truncation could shrink i_size enough
that xas.xa_index > end_pgoff, causing

    nr_pages = min(end, end_pgoff) - xas.xa_index + 1

to wrap to a huge unsigned value, passing that into
filemap_map_folio_range() and ultimately triggering the
VM_WARN_ON_FOLIO in __folio_rmap_sanity_checks() at

    VM_WARN_ON_FOLIO(page_folio(page + nr_pages - 1) != folio, folio)

I also checked next_uptodate_folio(): it does re-read i_size_read()
while holding the folio lock and skips folios whose head index is >=
max_idx.  That guard prevents returning a folio whose head is already
past the new EOF, but it does not close the window above: the wrapping
happens in the caller after next_uptodate_folio() returns, using the
stale end_pgoff.  The fix correctly clamps end_pgoff at the call site
before the folio is fetched.

The PMD eligibility check (file_end >= folio_next_index(folio)) and
the file_end argument forwarded to filemap_map_folio_range() both
consume the same file_end variable, which is now computed earlier; the
semantics of both paths are unchanged.

Looks good to me.

Reviewed-by: <reviewer>
Looks Good mm/vmalloc: free unused pages on vrealloc() shrink 🔗 Shivam Kalra via B4 Relay 3p
This series implements partial page freeing in vrealloc() when shrinking across a page boundary, extracting a vm_area_free_pages() helper, adding the shrink logic with correct exclusions for huge-page and VM_FLUSH_RESET_PERMS allocations, and a lib/test_vmalloc test case.
tests vmalloc
Shivam Kalra <shivamkalra98@zohomail.in>

[PATCH v5 0/3] mm/vmalloc: free unused pages on vrealloc() shrink

> diff --git a/mm/vmalloc.c b/mm/vmalloc.c

[Patch 1/3: extract vm_area_free_pages()]

> +static void vm_area_free_pages(struct vm_struct *vm, unsigned int start,
> +			       unsigned int end)
> +{
> +	unsigned int i;
> +
> +	for (i = start; i < end; i++) {
> +		struct page *page = vm->pages[i];
> +
> +		BUG_ON(!page);
> +		if (!(vm->flags & VM_MAP_PUT_PAGES))
> +			mod_lruvec_page_state(page, NR_VMALLOC, -1);
> +		__free_page(page);
> +		vm->pages[i] = NULL;
> +		cond_resched();
> +	}
> +}

Refactoring verified against the original loop in vfree(). The NULLing
of vm->pages[i] is safe: vfree() (after this patch) calls
vm_area_free_pages(vm, 0, vm->nr_pages), and vm->nr_pages is reduced to
new_nr_pages by patch 2 before vfree() sees the allocation. The NULL
slots at [new_nr_pages, original_nr_pages) are never visited.

[ ... ]

[Patch 2/3: free unused pages on vrealloc() shrink]

> +	/* Free tail pages when shrink crosses a page boundary. */
> +	if (new_nr_pages < vm->nr_pages && !vm_area_page_order(vm) &&
> +	    !(vm->flags & VM_FLUSH_RESET_PERMS)) {
> +		unsigned long addr = (unsigned long)p;
> +
> +		vunmap_range(addr + (new_nr_pages << PAGE_SHIFT),
> +			     addr + (vm->nr_pages << PAGE_SHIFT));
> +
> +		vm_area_free_pages(vm, new_nr_pages, vm->nr_pages);
> +		vm->nr_pages = new_nr_pages;
> +	}

Operation ordering verified:
  1. memset [size, old_size) runs while pages are still mapped.
  2. vunmap_range() clears PTEs and flushes TLBs before __free_page().
  3. vm->nr_pages is reduced only after freeing, so BUG_ON(!page) in
     vm_area_free_pages() is safe for the range being freed.

The subsequent vfree() path is safe. remove_vm_area() calls
free_unmap_vmap_area(), which invokes vunmap_range_noflush() over the
full original VA range. Since the tail PTEs are already cleared, the
second vunmap is a no-op. vm_reset_perms() is excluded by the
VM_FLUSH_RESET_PERMS guard above, so set_area_direct_map() only sees
the reduced vm->nr_pages. No double-free, no stale page pointers.

KASAN: __kasan_vrealloc() poisons shadow for [size, old_size) after
pages are unmapped. The KASAN shadow region is not backed by the vmalloc
pages themselves, so writes to shadow for the freed VA range are safe.

> -	if (size <= alloced_size) {
> +	if (size <= (size_t)vm->nr_pages << PAGE_SHIFT) {

Correct fix. get_vm_area_size() reads vm->size, which reflects the
virtual reservation and does not change on shrink. After pages are freed,
vm->nr_pages reflects actual physical backing, so a grow-in-place beyond
vm->nr_pages * PAGE_SIZE would access freed pages without this fix.

The page_order > 0 exclusion is correct: compound huge pages cannot be
partially freed at order-0. The VM_FLUSH_RESET_PERMS exclusion is
correct: vm_reset_perms() in vfree() must see all pages with direct-map
permissions intact, requiring them to remain until final vfree().

[ ... ]

[Patch 3/3: lib/test_vmalloc: add vrealloc test case]

The four-step sequence (grow-realloc, shrink-across-boundary,
shrink-within-page, grow-in-place) exercises all code paths introduced
in patch 2. Data integrity is checked at each step. The bit 12 (id
4096) mask assignment is consistent with the existing scheme.

Overall the series looks correct.

  • [PATCH v5 1/3] mm/vmalloc: extract vm_area_free_pages() helper from vfree()
  • [PATCH v5 2/3] mm/vmalloc: free unused pages on vrealloc() shrink
  • [PATCH v5 3/3] lib/test_vmalloc: add vrealloc test case

Looks Good selftests/mm: skip several tests when thp is not available 🔗 Chunyu Hu 5p
This series adds thp_is_enabled() guard checks across five selftests (guard-regions collapse, soft-dirty hugepage, split_huge_page_test, transhuge-stress) to skip rather than fail on THP-disabled kernels, and consolidates the write_file() helper into vm_util to eliminate duplicate implementations.
tests
Chunyu Hu <chuhu@redhat.com>

selftests/mm: skip several tests when thp is not available

Verified the following across all five patches:

- thp_is_enabled() in thp_settings.c first calls thp_available() which
  does access(THP_SYSFS, F_OK), then reads the "enabled" sysfs knob and
  returns true only for "always" (mode==1) or "madvise" (mode==3). The
  guard correctly identifies THP-disabled kernels.

> diff --git a/tools/testing/selftests/mm/soft-dirty.c b/tools/testing/selftests/mm/soft-dirty.c
> @@ -82,7 +82,9 @@ static void test_hugepage(int pagemap_fd, int pagesize)
>  	if (!thp_is_enabled()) {
> -		ksft_test_result_skip("Transparent Hugepages not available\n");
> +		ksft_print_msg("Transparent Hugepages not available\n");
> +		ksft_test_result_skip("Test %s huge page allocation\n", __func__);
> +		ksft_test_result_skip("Test %s huge page dirty bit\n", __func__);

Correct fix: test_hugepage covers two sub-tests so exactly two
ksft_test_result_skip() calls are needed to keep the count consistent
with the "1..19" plan.

> diff --git a/tools/testing/selftests/mm/vm_util.c b/tools/testing/selftests/mm/vm_util.c
> +unsigned int write_file(const char *path, const char *buf, size_t buflen)
> +{
> +	if (fd == -1)
> +		ksft_exit_fail_msg("%s open failed: %s\n", path, strerror(errno));
> +	numwritten = write(fd, buf, buflen - 1);
> +	close(fd);
> +	if (numwritten < 1)
> +		ksft_exit_fail_msg("Write failed\n");
> +	return (unsigned int) numwritten;
> +}

The new implementation matches the version removed from
split_huge_page_test.c exactly. The old thp_settings.c write_file() used
printf()+exit(EXIT_FAILURE); switching to ksft_exit_fail_msg() is a
compatible change since both exit on failure. The callers in
thp_settings.c (write_num, thp_write_string) keep their "if
(!write_file(...))" checks, which become dead code since write_file()
now exits rather than returning 0 on failure, but this is harmless.

Checked that khugepaged.c includes both vm_util.h and thp_settings.h.
After the patch, thp_settings.h no longer declares write_file() but
vm_util.h does, so khugepaged.c still resolves exactly one declaration
and one definition. No multiple-definition or missing-prototype issues.

The transhuge-stress.c and split_huge_page_test.c THP checks are placed
after ksft_print_header() so ksft_exit_skip() produces well-formed TAP
output matching the expected "1..0 # SKIP" format. The guard-regions
collapse test uses the ksft fixture SKIP() macro correctly inside
TEST_F.

Looks good to me.

Looks Good Docs/mm/damon: Document DAMON actions when TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is off 🔗 <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com> 1p
Pure documentation patch adding a note that the DAMON hugepage and nohugepage actions silently fail when CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is disabled, because do_madvise() returns -EINVAL for those behaviors in that configuration.
docs
From: Asier Gutierrez <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com>
Subject: [PATCH v1 1/1] Docs/mm/damon: Document DAMON actions when
TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is off

I verified the claim against the implementation.  In mm/madvise.c,
MADV_HUGEPAGE and MADV_NOHUGEPAGE are gated by
#ifdef CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE inside madvise_behavior_valid().
When that config is off, is_valid_madvise() returns false, causing
madvise_should_skip() to set *err = -EINVAL and return true.
do_madvise() then returns -EINVAL to damos_madvise() in vaddr.c:

  applied = do_madvise(mm, start, len, behavior) ? 0 : len;

Since the return value is non-zero, applied == 0 and no error is
propagated upward from DAMON.  The documentation addition is accurate.

> diff --git a/Documentation/mm/damon/design.rst b/Documentation/mm/damon/design.rst
> --- a/Documentation/mm/damon/design.rst
> +++ b/Documentation/mm/damon/design.rst
> @@ -460,9 +460,13 @@ that supports each action are as below.
>   - ``hugepage``: Call ``madvise()`` for the region with ``MADV_HUGEPAGE``.
> -   Supported by ``vaddr`` and ``fvaddr`` operations set.
> +   Supported by ``vaddr`` and ``fvaddr`` operations set. When
> +   TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is disabled, the application of the action will just
> +   fail.

The phrase "will just fail" is accurate.  Optionally saying "silently
fail" could be clearer, since the -EINVAL from do_madvise() is
converted to 0 applied bytes internally and no error is reported to
the user via DAMON interfaces.  Either wording works.

Reviewed-by: <reviewer>
Needs Discussion mm/mempolicy: NUMA mempolicy mismatch during remote access 🔗 Lin Ruifeng 1p
RFC (no code change) reporting that SVA IOPF handling via a kworker ignores the faulting process's NUMA mempolicy because get_vma_policy() falls back to get_task_policy(current), where current is the kworker rather than the original process.
Lin Ruifeng <linruifeng4@huawei.com>

[RFC PATCH] mm/mempolicy: NUMA mempolicy mismatch during remote access

The bug is real.  I traced the call chain in the current tree to confirm:

  iommu_sva_handle_iopf() [kworker context]
    -> iommu_sva_handle_mm()
      -> handle_mm_fault(vma, addr, FAULT_FLAG_REMOTE, NULL)
        -> do_anonymous_page()
          -> alloc_anon_folio()
            -> vma_alloc_folio_noprof()
              -> get_vma_policy(vma, addr, order, &ilx)

In get_vma_policy() (mm/mempolicy.c):

> pol = __get_vma_policy(vma, addr, ilx);
> if (!pol)
>         pol = get_task_policy(current);

When no VMA-level policy is set, the fallback is get_task_policy(current),
which returns the kworker's mempolicy (NULL -> system default), not the
original process's mempolicy.  The FAULT_FLAG_REMOTE flag passed to
handle_mm_fault() is only checked by arch_vma_access_permitted(); it
does not influence mempolicy resolution anywhere in the allocation path.

This same issue affects mm/hmm.c, which also drives handle_mm_fault()
with FAULT_FLAG_REMOTE from a non-owner context.

A few design questions worth settling before writing a fix:

1. The mm->owner field tracks the canonical task for the mm_struct.
   One approach is to make get_vma_policy() accept a task_struct*
   argument (or a mempolicy* fallback) so that FAULT_FLAG_REMOTE
   callers can supply the owner's policy.  However, mm->owner is
   maintained under alloc_lock and can change; any dereference needs
   RCU read-side protection.  What locking would the caller hold at
   the point of alloc_anon_folio() when invoked from a kworker?

2. Alternatively, could the policy be snapshotted from the owner task
   at bind time (iommu_sva_bind_device) and stored on the SVA domain?
   That avoids the per-fault owner lookup but means the policy is
   frozen at bind time and won't track subsequent set_mempolicy() calls.

3. The iommufd path (iommufd_fault_iopf_handler -> userspace response
   loop) delegates fault handling to userspace entirely and is not
   affected.  The SVA kernel handler iommu_sva_handle_iopf() is the
   affected path.

No code is changed in this RFC, so there are no correctness or locking
issues to flag yet.  Looking forward to the proposed fix.
Needs Work [LSF/MM/BPF TOPIC] mm/mempolicy: introduce socket-aware weighted interleave 🔗 Rakie Kim 4p
This series introduces socket-aware weighted interleave by grouping NUMA nodes into per-socket memory packages and restricting allocation candidates to the current socket before applying weights. Several correctness issues — a silent empty-mask success return, wrong stub return values, a hot-path locking concern, and a misleading barrier idiom — need to be fixed before this can land.
drivers include memory-tiers mempolicy
From: <reviewer>
Subject: Re: [LSF/MM/BPF TOPIC] [RFC PATCH 0/4] mm/mempolicy: introduce
         socket-aware weighted interleave

Thanks for the series. The benchmark numbers are impressive and the
concept is sound. A few correctness issues need to be addressed.

--- [RFC PATCH 1/4] mm/numa: introduce nearest_nodes_nodemask() ---

> diff --git a/include/linux/numa.h b/include/linux/numa.h
> +static inline int nearest_nodes_nodemask(int node,
> +					 const nodemask_t *mask,
> +					 nodemask_t *out)
> +{
> +	return 0;
> +}

The no-NUMA stub returns 0 (success) without touching *out at all,
leaving it uninitialized. The kdoc for the real implementation says
"Return: 0 on success" and that *out is populated on success. Any
caller that does:

  if (!nearest_nodes_nodemask(n, &mask, &out))
      /* use out */

will read garbage on a CONFIG_NUMA=n build. The stub should clear
*out before returning, matching what the real implementation does at
the top of the function.

--- [RFC PATCH 2/4] mm/memory-tiers: introduce socket-aware topology
                    management ---

> +static inline int mp_next_demotion_node(int nid)
> +{
> +	return 0;
> +}
> +
> +static inline int mp_next_promotion_node(int nid)
> +{
> +	return 0;
> +}

Both stubs return 0, which is a valid node ID. The existing analogous
stub for next_demotion_node() returns NUMA_NO_NODE. Any caller testing
`mp_next_demotion_node(nid) != NUMA_NO_NODE` will misinterpret "no
target" as "node 0" on CONFIG_NUMA=n builds. Both stubs should return
NUMA_NO_NODE.

The same issue applies to the no-CONFIG_MIGRATION stubs inside the
CONFIG_NUMA block (mp_next_demotion_node / mp_next_promotion_node
return 0 there too).

Additionally, the cover letter notes that mp_next_demotion_nodemask(),
mp_next_demotion_node(), mp_next_promotion_nodemask(), and
mp_next_promotion_node() are all exported but have no callers anywhere
in the series. Dead exported symbols are not acceptable for mainline;
please remove them and re-add with their first user.

--- [RFC PATCH 4/4] mm/mempolicy: enhance weighted interleave with
                    socket-aware locality ---

> +static int policy_resolve_package_nodes(struct mempolicy *policy,
> +					nodemask_t *mask)
> +{
> +	unsigned int node, ret = 0;
> +	nodemask_t package_mask;
> +
> +	if (!policy || !mask)
> +		return -EINVAL;
> +
> +	nodes_clear(*mask);
> +
> +	node = numa_node_id();
> +	ret = mp_get_package_nodes(node, &package_mask);
> +	if (!ret) {
> +		nodes_and(*mask, package_mask, policy->nodes);
> +
> +		if (nodes_empty(*mask)) {
> +			node = first_node(policy->nodes);
> +			ret = mp_get_package_nodes(node, &package_mask);
> +			if (ret)
> +				goto out;
> +			nodes_and(*mask, package_mask, policy->nodes);
> +			if (nodes_empty(*mask))
> +				goto out;
> +		}
> +	}
> +
> +out:
> +	return ret;
> +}

There is a correctness bug in the second fallback path. When the
second nodes_and() yields an empty *mask, the function jumps to out
with ret == 0 (the successful return left by the second
mp_get_package_nodes() call). The caller treats ret == 0 as success:

  if (policy_resolve_package_nodes(policy, &mask))
      mask = policy->nodes;

So it proceeds with an empty mask. In weighted_interleave_nodes(),
with il_weight exhausted or node not in the empty mask,
next_node_in() on an empty nodemask returns MAX_NUMNODES, which then
propagates up the call stack even though policy->nodes is fully
populated. The `if (nodes_empty(*mask)) goto out` in the fallback
must set a non-zero ret before jumping, so the caller falls back to
policy->nodes as intended.

> +static unsigned int weighted_interleave_nodes(struct mempolicy *policy)
> +{
>  	unsigned int node;
>  	unsigned int cpuset_mems_cookie;
> +	nodemask_t mask;
>  
>  retry:
>  	cpuset_mems_cookie = read_mems_allowed_begin();
>  	node = current->il_prev;
> +
> +	if (policy_resolve_package_nodes(policy, &mask))
> +		mask = policy->nodes;
> +
> +	if (!current->il_weight || !node_isset(node, mask)) {
> +		node = next_node_in(node, mask);
>  		if (read_mems_allowed_retry(cpuset_mems_cookie))
>  			goto retry;

policy_resolve_package_nodes() is called unconditionally on every
entry to weighted_interleave_nodes(), including the common fast path
where il_weight is still positive and no new node selection is needed.
This means mp_get_package_nodes() runs for every single page
allocation under MPOL_WEIGHTED_INTERLEAVE.

What is the locking discipline inside mp_get_package_nodes()? The
implementation is in patch 2/4 which is truncated, but this matters:
weighted_interleave_nodes() is reached from mempolicy_slab_node(),
which can be called in GFP_ATOMIC or interrupt-disabled contexts. If
mp_get_package_nodes() acquires a mutex or sleeps, this is broken for
those callers.

The call should also be guarded so it is only made when a new node
actually needs to be selected (i.e., inside the il_weight == 0 branch),
both for correctness in atomic contexts and to avoid unnecessary work
on the hot path.

> +static unsigned int read_once_policy_package_nodemask(
> +					struct mempolicy *pol,
> +					nodemask_t *mask)
> +{
> +	nodemask_t package_mask;
> +
> +	barrier();
> +	if (policy_resolve_package_nodes(pol, &package_mask))
> +		memcpy(mask, &pol->nodes, sizeof(nodemask_t));
> +	else
> +		memcpy(mask, &package_mask, sizeof(nodemask_t));
> +	barrier();
> +
> +	return nodes_weight(*mask);
> +}

The barrier() idiom in read_once_policy_nodemask() works because it
wraps a plain memcpy of pol->nodes: the barriers prevent the compiler
from reordering memory accesses around that snapshot. Placing
policy_resolve_package_nodes() -- which may acquire locks and walk
data structures -- between two compiler barriers does not provide the
same guarantee and is misleading. If the intent is to take a stable
snapshot of the filtered nodemask for the weighted_interleave_nid()
path, the approach needs to be reconsidered.

--- [RFC PATCH 3/4] mm/memory-tiers: register CXL nodes to
                    socket-aware packages via initiator ---

> +static int cxl_region_find_nearest_node(struct cxl_region *cxlr)
> +{
> +	for (i = 0; i < p->nr_targets; i++) {
> +		cxled = p->targets[i];
> +		cxlmd = cxled_to_memdev(cxled);
> +		numa_node = dev_to_node(&cxlmd->dev);
> +		if (numa_node != NUMA_NO_NODE)
> +			return numa_node;
> +	}
> +	return NUMA_NO_NODE;
> +}

For a multi-target (interleaved) CXL region whose targets span more
than one CPU socket, this function returns only the initiator node of
the first eligible target. The region then gets registered to a single
package, silently ignoring all other sockets it actually services.
Is this intended? If so it should be documented. If not, an interleaved
region may need separate mp_add_package_node_by_initiator() calls for
each distinct initiator socket."

Looks Good mm/zswap: add missing kunmap_local() 🔗 "Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle)" 1p

From: reviewer

mm/zswap: add missing kunmap_local()

Verified against the current mm/zswap.c implementation.  In
zswap_decompress(), the uncompressed fast path (entry->length ==
PAGE_SIZE) was passing the return value of kmap_local_folio() directly
to memcpy_from_sglist(), discarding the pointer and making it impossible
to call kunmap_local().  The else branch avoids kmap entirely since
sg_set_folio() works directly on the folio, so only this branch is
affected.

> if (entry->length == PAGE_SIZE) {
> +       void *dst;
> +
>         WARN_ON_ONCE(input->length != PAGE_SIZE);
> -       memcpy_from_sglist(kmap_local_folio(folio, 0), input, 0, PAGE_SIZE);
> +
> +       dst = kmap_local_folio(folio, 0);
> +       memcpy_from_sglist(dst, input, 0, PAGE_SIZE);
>         dlen = PAGE_SIZE;
> +       kunmap_local(dst);

Checked: dst is scoped to the if-block, initialized before use, and
kunmap_local() is called before the block exits.  On 64-bit builds
kmap_local_folio() is essentially a no-op so the bug is latent there;
on 32-bit builds with real kmap slots the leaked slot triggers the
BUG_ON() syzbot reported.  The fix is minimal and correct.

Minor Issues mm/vma: convert vm_flags_t to vma_flags_t in vma code 🔗 "Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle)" 23p
The series incrementally converts VMA flag handling from the legacy vm_flags_t (unsigned long) to the new structured vma_flags_t (bitmap wrapper), adding helpers and temporary unions to allow gradual migration. The union aliasing and new helper semantics are correct, but the vm_brk_flags() parameter elimination in patch 09 risks silently dropping VM_EXEC for executable ELF BSS sections on NON_EXEC-default architectures.

From: reviewer
To: Lorenzo Stoakes <ljs@kernel.org>, linux-mm@kvack.org
Subject: Re: [PATCH v2 00/23] mm/vma: convert vm_flags_t to vma_flags_t
 in vma code

Reviewed against mm/vma.c, mm/vma.h, include/linux/mm.h,
include/linux/mm_types.h, mm/mmap.c, and fs/binfmt_elf.c.

--- [PATCH v2 01/23] mm/vma: add vma_flags_empty(), vma_flags_and(),
    vma_flags_diff_pair()

> +/* Are no flags set in the specified VMA flags? */
> +static __always_inline bool vma_flags_empty(vma_flags_t *flags)
> +{
> +	unsigned long *bitmap = flags->__vma_flags;
> +
> +	return bitmap_empty(bitmap, NUM_VMA_FLAG_BITS);
> +}

The pointer should be 'const vma_flags_t *flags'.  Every other query
function in this file (vma_flags_test, vma_flags_test_any_mask,
vma_flags_test_all_mask) takes a const pointer.  Without it, callers
with a const-qualified vma_flags_t cannot use this function without
a cast, and lvalues returned from vma_flags_and_mask() or
vma_flags_diff_pair() cannot be passed directly.

> +static __always_inline vma_flags_t vma_flags_and_mask(const vma_flags_t *flags,
> +						      vma_flags_t to_and)
> +{
> +	vma_flags_t dst;
> +	unsigned long *bitmap_dst = dst.__vma_flags;

dst is uninitialized before bitmap_and().  Since NUM_VMA_FLAG_BITS ==
BITS_PER_LONG, DIV_ROUND_UP(64, 64) = 1 word, so bitmap_and() fully
writes dst.__vma_flags[0].  This is safe as-is.

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v2 03/23] mm/vma: add further vma_flags_t unions

> diff --git a/mm/vma.h b/mm/vma.h
> +	union {
> +		/* Temporary while VMA flags are being converted. */
> +		vm_flags_t vm_flags;
> +		vma_flags_t vma_flags;
> +	};

The union aliasing is safe.  vm_flags_t is unsigned long; vma_flags_t
is 'struct { unsigned long __vma_flags[1]; }' because NUM_VMA_FLAG_BITS
== BITS_PER_LONG, so both sides are exactly sizeof(unsigned long) bytes.
Existing callers that initialise '.vm_flags = ...' via VMG_STATE and
VMG_VMA_STATE continue to write the correct storage location.

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v2 05/23] mm/vma: use new VMA flags for sticky flags logic

I traced the sticky flags path in the current vma_merge_existing_range():

  vm_flags_t sticky_flags = vmg->vm_flags & VM_STICKY;
  ...
  sticky_flags |= (next->vm_flags & VM_STICKY);  /* if merge_right */
  sticky_flags |= (prev->vm_flags & VM_STICKY);  /* if merge_left  */
  ...
  vm_flags_set(vmg->target, sticky_flags);

Converting this to vma_flags_diff_pair() (XOR) + clearing
VMA_STICKY_FLAGS before the empty check in is_mergeable_vma(), and
accumulating sticky flags via vma_flags_and_mask() in the merge path,
is semantically equivalent to the original '(a ^ b) & ~VM_IGNORE_MERGE'
test.  VMA_STICKY_FLAGS is conditionally defined with the same
CONFIG_MEM_SOFT_DIRTY guard as the original VM_STICKY.

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v2 09/23] mm: unexport vm_brk_flags() and eliminate vm_flags
    parameter

This patch is not fully visible, but the title and the fs/binfmt_elf.c
change warrant attention.  The current call site in binfmt_elf.c is:

  /* If the header is requesting these pages to be
   * executable, honour that (ppc32 needs this).  */
  error = vm_brk_flags(zero_start, zero_end - zero_start,
                       prot & PROT_EXEC ? VM_EXEC : 0);

This path is inside 'if (eppnt->p_memsz > eppnt->p_filesz)' and is
reached when prot & PROT_EXEC, so it always passes VM_EXEC.

In do_brk_flags(), vm_flags is ORed with VM_DATA_DEFAULT_FLAGS:

  vm_flags |= VM_DATA_DEFAULT_FLAGS | VM_ACCOUNT | mm->def_flags;

On architectures where VM_DATA_DEFAULT_FLAGS is VM_DATA_FLAGS_NON_EXEC
(arc, nios2, hexagon, riscv, s390) or VM_DATA_FLAGS_TSK_EXEC (arm,
arm64, mips, loongarch, ppc32 -- where TASK_EXEC expands to VM_EXEC
only when READ_IMPLIES_EXEC personality is set), this OR does NOT
unconditionally set VM_EXEC.  The explicit VM_EXEC parameter is the
only mechanism that makes the BSS-padding mapping executable for
PROT_EXEC ELF segments on these architectures.

If the vm_flags parameter is simply dropped from vm_brk_flags() and
nothing replaces it, the vm_get_page_prot() call inside do_brk_flags()
will produce non-executable page protection for the anonymous BSS
region even when the ELF segment protection requires it.  The ppc32
case the comment mentions uses VM_DATA_FLAGS_TSK_EXEC, which only
sets VM_EXEC when READ_IMPLIES_EXEC is active -- not unconditionally.

Could you confirm how the executable BSS case is preserved after the
parameter is removed?  Does the binfmt_elf.c change substitute a
different mechanism -- for example calling do_brk_flags() directly
with VM_EXEC, or a new boolean argument -- to convey exec permission
on non-EXEC-default architectures?

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v2 17/23] mm: convert do_brk_flags() to use vma_flags_t

do_brk_flags() currently passes vm_flags to VMG_STATE, which
initialises '.vm_flags = vm_flags_'.  After the parameter type becomes
vma_flags_t, that designated initialiser assigns a struct value to
an unsigned long member, which is a type error unless VMG_STATE is
also updated in this patch.  Is there a new macro variant (e.g.
VMG_STATE_VMA_FLAGS) introduced here, or is VMG_STATE updated to use
'.vma_flags = ...' instead?

Additionally, do_brk_flags() calls ksm_vma_flags(), vm_flags_init(),
and vm_get_page_prot() -- all of which take vm_flags_t.  Are these
bridged through the vma_flags_to_legacy() helper from patch 11, or
are these callees also converted as part of this patch?

Minor Issues kho: history: track previous kernel version and kexec boot count 🔗 Breno Leitao 6p
This series generalizes the KHO subtree API to handle non-FDT blobs by adding an explicit size parameter and persisting it in the KHO FDT, then uses that infrastructure to carry the previous kernel's version string and kexec boot count across kexec transitions.
docs include kernel memblock tests
Breno Leitao <leitao@debian.org>

kho: history: track previous kernel version and kexec boot count

Patches 1-4 look mechanically correct after cross-checking callers and
the version gating in kho_populate().  Questions on patch 5 below,
where the diff was truncated.

--- [PATCH v9 3/6] kho: persist blob size in KHO FDT ---

> -#define KHO_FDT_COMPATIBLE "kho-v2"
> +#define KHO_FDT_COMPATIBLE "kho-v3"

Verified: kho_populate() gates on this string via
fdt_node_check_compatible() before setting kho_in.fdt_phys, so any
FDT written by a pre-v3 kernel is silently rejected before either
kho_in_debugfs_init() or kho_retrieve_subtree() is reached.  The
version bump is correctly enforced.

> +	err = fdt_setprop(root_fdt, off, KHO_SUB_TREE_PROP_NAME,
> +			  &phys, sizeof(phys));
> +	if (err < 0)
> +		goto out_pack;
> +
> +	err = fdt_setprop(root_fdt, off, KHO_SUB_TREE_SIZE_PROP_NAME,
> +			  &size_u64, sizeof(size_u64));
> +	if (err < 0)
> +		goto out_pack;

If the second fdt_setprop() fails the node is left with
'preserved-data' but no 'blob-size'.  kho_add_subtree() correctly
returns error so the caller knows not to rely on the entry, and patch
4's kho_in_debugfs_init() skips such nodes with a warning.  No
functional regression here, but should kho_retrieve_subtree() also
return -EINVAL in the new size-output path when 'blob-size' is absent,
rather than silently returning only phys with size unset?

--- [PATCH v9 4/6] kho: fix kho_in_debugfs_init() to handle non-FDT blobs ---

> +		blob_size = fdt_getprop(fdt, child,
> +					KHO_SUB_TREE_SIZE_PROP_NAME, &len);
> +		if (!blob_size || len != sizeof(*blob_size)) {
> +			pr_warn("node %s missing or invalid %s property\n",
> +				name, KHO_SUB_TREE_SIZE_PROP_NAME);
> +			continue;
> +		}

The len != sizeof(*blob_size) check is correct (sizeof(u64) == 8).
Since only kho-v3 FDTs reach this point, 'blob-size' will always be
present for well-formed entries.  The continue is the right choice:
failure to show a debugfs entry is non-fatal.  Looks good.

--- [PATCH v9 5/6] kho: kexec-metadata: track previous kernel chain ---

> +struct kho_kexec_metadata {
> +	u32 version;
> +	char previous_release[__NEW_UTS_LEN + 1];
> +	u32 kexec_count;
> +} __packed;

With __packed, kexec_count lands at offset 4 + 65 = 69, which is not
4-byte aligned.  The compiler generates correct code for packed struct
member accesses, so this is not a correctness bug on x86 or arm64.
However, taking &metadata->kexec_count and passing it anywhere
expecting an aligned u32 * would be unsafe.  Is that pointer taken in
the restore path?

The diff for kexec_handover.c in patch 5 was truncated, so I could not
verify the restore-side implementation.  A few questions:

1. When reading back the metadata on the incoming side, is the blob
   size (retrieved via kho_retrieve_subtree() with the new size
   parameter) validated against sizeof(struct kho_kexec_metadata)
   before any field is dereferenced?  A truncated or zero blob-size
   value in the FDT would otherwise let the code walk past valid
   memory.

2. Is previous_release guaranteed to be NUL-terminated before the
   printk?  utsname()->release is always NUL-terminated (it fills a
   __NEW_UTS_LEN + 1 buffer), so a direct strscpy/memcpy of that exact
   size into previous_release is safe -- just confirming the copy uses
   a bounded form and does not rely on the source being shorter.

3. On cold boot (no incoming KHO data) how is kexec_count initialised
   in the outgoing metadata?  The cover letter says "count starts at 0"
   but the example output shows "count 1" for the first kexec.  A
   short comment clarifying the counting convention (e.g. the outgoing
   kernel writes incoming_count + 1, cold boot is treated as count 0)
   would help future readers without having to re-derive it from the
   printk output.

Author: Deepanshu Kartikey <kartikey406@gmail.com>

kernel/fork: validate exit_signal in kernel_clone()

The fix looks correct.  valid_signal() accepts 0 (exit_signal=0 is
used by kernel_thread() for threads that send no signal on exit, and
explicitly by vhost_task.c), so no existing in-kernel caller is
broken.  fork() and vfork() pass SIGCHLD=17.  clone3() is already
validated in copy_clone_args_from_user() before reaching

Two minor issues:

Minor Issues mm: Free contiguous order-0 pages efficiently 🔗 Muhammad Usama Anjum 3p
This series introduces free_prepared_contig_range() to batch-free contiguous order-0 pages as largest possible power-of-2 aligned chunks, then applies the optimization to free_contig_range, vfree, and __free_contig_frozen_range. The approach is correct but vfree loses its cond_resched() which warrants discussion.
include page_alloc vmalloc
Author: Muhammad Usama Anjum <usama.anjum@arm.com>

mm: Free contiguous order-0 pages efficiently (v2 1-3/3)

[ patch 2/3: vmalloc: Optimize vfree ]

> diff --git a/mm/vmalloc.c b/mm/vmalloc.c
> --- a/mm/vmalloc.c
> +++ b/mm/vmalloc.c

[ ... ]

> -	for (i = 0; i < vm->nr_pages; i++) {
> -		struct page *page = vm->pages[i];
> +
> +	if (vm->nr_pages) {
> +		bool account = !(vm->flags & VM_MAP_PUT_PAGES);
> +		unsigned long start_pfn, pfn;
> +		struct page *page = vm->pages[0];
> +		int nr = 1;

Minor: vm->nr_pages is unsigned int; nr is declared as int.  nr grows
up to vm->nr_pages before being passed to __free_contig_range() as
unsigned long.  Could be unsigned int to match the field type.

> -		__free_page(page);
> -		cond_resched();

The original loop called cond_resched() after every __free_page().
The new loop does not have a yield point in the per-page accounting
pass.  For a large vmalloc area backed by non-contiguous physical
pages (worst case: every vm->pages[i] has a different PFN, so every
iteration flushes a batch of size 1 via __free_contig_range()), the
CPU is held for all nr_pages iterations without preemption.  vfree()
runs in sleepable process context (might_sleep() is asserted above),
so latency on GiB-scale frees is a real concern.

Does __free_contig_range() call cond_resched() internally?  If not,
should one be added in the batch-flush path, e.g. after each
__free_contig_range() call?

> +		for (i = 1; i < vm->nr_pages; i++) {
> +			page = vm->pages[i];
> +			BUG_ON(!page);
> +			if (account)
> +				mod_lruvec_page_state(page, NR_VMALLOC, -1);
> +			pfn = page_to_pfn(page);
> +			if (start_pfn + nr == pfn) {
> +				nr++;
> +				continue;
> +			}
> +			__free_contig_range(start_pfn, nr);
> +			start_pfn = pfn;
> +			nr = 1;

[ ... ]

[ patch 3/3: mm/page_alloc: Optimize __free_contig_frozen_range() ]

> diff --git a/mm/page_alloc.c b/mm/page_alloc.c
> --- a/mm/page_alloc.c
> +++ b/mm/page_alloc.c

[ ... ]

> -	for (; nr_pages--; pfn++)
> -		free_frozen_pages(pfn_to_page(pfn), 0);
> +	struct page *page = pfn_to_page(pfn);
> +	struct page *start = NULL;
> +	unsigned long i;
> +
> +	for (i = 0; i < nr_pages; i++, page++) {
> +		if (free_pages_prepare(page, 0)) {
> +			if (!start)
> +				start = page;
> +		} else if (start) {
> +			free_prepared_contig_range(start, page - start);
> +			start = NULL;
> +		}
> +	}
> +
> +	if (start)
> +		free_prepared_contig_range(start, page - start);

I traced the callers of __free_contig_frozen_range(): it is invoked
from alloc_contig_frozen_range_noprof() to free the head and tail
pages of the outer aligned range, and this happens before the call to
undo_isolate_page_range().  That means the pageblocks are still
MIGRATE_ISOLATE at the time these pages are freed.

The old free_frozen_pages() -> __free_frozen_pages() handled that
explicitly: if migratetype is MIGRATE_ISOLATE, it calls free_one_page()
directly, bypassing the PCP list.

The new path calls free_pages_prepare() (same __free_pages_prepare()
with FPI_NONE, identical to the old path) and then delegates to
free_prepared_contig_range(), which from the perf trace calls
__free_frozen_pages() internally.  Since __free_frozen_pages() still
performs the migratetype check and routes MIGRATE_ISOLATE pages to
free_one_page(), the behavior should be preserved -- could you confirm
that free_prepared_contig_range() passes FPI_PREPARED through to
__free_frozen_pages() so that path is still reached after preparation
is skipped?

The batch accumulation logic looks correct.  When free_pages_prepare()
returns false (e.g. HWPoison), the else-if(start) branch correctly
flushes the accumulated run [start, page) and resets start, isolating
the bad page.  The pointer arithmetic page - start is valid because
page is incremented by 1 each iteration over the struct page array.
The tail flush uses page == pfn_to_page(pfn) + nr_pages, so
page - start yields the correct trailing count.

  • [PATCH v2 0/3] mm: Free contiguous order-0 pages efficiently
  • [PATCH v2 1/3] mm/page_alloc: Optimize free_contig_range()
  • [PATCH v2 2/3] vmalloc: Optimize vfree
  • [PATCH v2 3/3] mm/page_alloc: Optimize __free_contig_frozen_range()
Minor Issues mm/userfaultfd: re-validate vma in mfill_atomic() loop under CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK 🔗 Deepanshu Kartikey 1p
The patch re-validates the VMA on each iteration of the mfill_atomic() page-by-page loop to detect when a concurrent __split_vma() has shrunk vma->vm_end past the current dst_addr while only a per-VMA read lock is held. When a stale VMA is detected it drops it and re-acquires a fresh one via mfill_get_vma().
userfaultfd
From: reviewer
Subject: Re: [PATCH] mm/userfaultfd: re-validate vma in mfill_atomic() loop
         under CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK

> --- a/mm/userfaultfd.c
> +++ b/mm/userfaultfd.c
> @@ -910,6 +910,22 @@ static __always_inline ssize_t mfill_atomic(...)
>
>  	while (state.src_addr < src_start + len) {
>  		VM_WARN_ON_ONCE(state.dst_addr >= dst_start + len);
> +	       /*
> +		* Under CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK, a concurrent UFFDIO_UNREGISTER can

The opening '/*' has seven spaces before it instead of a tab.  Should
be a single tab to match kernel coding style.

> +		* Under CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK, a concurrent UFFDIO_UNREGISTER can
> +		* split state.vma while we hold only the per-VMA read lock.

The comment says "Under CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK" but the new code is not
gated by that symbol -- it compiles and runs on both code paths.
Under !CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK, uffd_mfill_lock() holds mmap_read_lock()
which prevents concurrent splits, so the check is always false and
harmless there, but the comment is misleading.  Worth either dropping
the qualifier or adding an #ifdef CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK guard if you
want to make the intent explicit.

> +		if (state.dst_addr < state.vma->vm_start ||
> +		    state.dst_addr >= state.vma->vm_end) {
> +			mfill_put_vma(&state);
> +			state.dst_start = state.dst_addr;
> +			state.len = dst_start + len - state.dst_addr;
> +			err = mfill_get_vma(&state);
> +			if (err)
> +				break;
> +		}

I traced through the logic and the core fix is correct:

- mfill_put_vma() sets state.vma = NULL, so the outer mfill_put_vma()
  after the loop is a safe no-op when mfill_get_vma() fails here.

- mfill_get_vma() calls uffd_mfill_lock(mm, state.dst_start,
  state.len), which calls validate_dst_vma(vma, state.dst_start +
  state.len).  With the patch's assignments this evaluates to
  validate_dst_vma(vma, dst_start + len) -- i.e., the entire
  remaining range must fit within the newly found VMA.  If the split
  broke that invariant (e.g. UFFDIO_UNREGISTER unregistered part of
  the range), validate_dst_vma() returns false and mfill_get_vma()
  returns -ENOENT, which is correct.

- state.src_start is not updated here, but mfill_get_vma() does not
  read it (only dst_start and len are used), so there is no
  inconsistency.  state.src_addr advances in lock-step with
  state.dst_addr, and the loop condition (state.src_addr <
  src_start + len) uses the original local variables and is unaffected
  by the state.len update.

- The mfill_copy_folio_retry() path also calls mfill_put_vma() and
  mfill_get_vma(state).  After the patch updates state.dst_start and
  state.len, any subsequent mfill_copy_folio_retry() invocation would
  use the updated values, which correctly reflect the current position
  in the range.

One small question on the dst_addr < vm_start arm: dst_addr starts at
or above vm_start and only ever advances by PAGE_SIZE, and vm_start is
not modified by __split_vma().  Is there a concrete execution path
where dst_addr could end up below vm_start, or is this arm purely
belt-and-suspenders?
Minor Issues mm/memcontrol: batch memcg charging in __memcg_slab_post_alloc_hook 🔗 Hui Zhu 1p
Batches memcg charging in __memcg_slab_post_alloc_hook() by scanning runs of consecutive objects whose slabs share the same pgdat, issuing one __obj_cgroup_charge()/__consume_obj_stock() call per run instead of one per object. Implements the TODO left in commit bc730030f956.
memcontrol
From: [reviewer]

mm/memcontrol: batch memcg charging in __memcg_slab_post_alloc_hook

> diff --git a/mm/memcontrol.c b/mm/memcontrol.c
> --- a/mm/memcontrol.c
> +++ b/mm/memcontrol.c

[ ... ]

> -	for (i = 0; i < size; i++) {
> +	for (i = 0; i < size; ) {
>  		unsigned long obj_exts;
>  		struct slabobj_ext *obj_ext;
>  		struct obj_stock_pcp *stock;
> +		struct pglist_data *pgdat;
> +		unsigned int batch_bytes;
> +		size_t run_len = 0;
> +		size_t j;
> +		bool skip_next = false;

I traced the skip_next logic carefully: when alloc_slab_obj_exts()
fails for p[j] in the inner scan, run_len == j - i at that point, so
"i = i + run_len + 1" correctly lands on p[j+1], matching the original
behaviour of the per-object "continue".  skip_next is re-initialised
to false on every outer-loop iteration, so a failure in one batch
cannot bleed into the next.

> +		pgdat = slab_pgdat(slab);
> +		run_len = 1;
> +
> +		for (j = i + 1; j < size; j++) {
> +			struct slab *slab_j = virt_to_slab(p[j]);
> +
> +			if (slab_pgdat(slab_j) != pgdat)
> +				break;
> +
> +			if (!slab_obj_exts(slab_j) &&
> +			    alloc_slab_obj_exts(slab_j, s, flags, false)) {
> +				skip_next = true;
> +				break;
> +			}
> +
> +			run_len++;
> +		}

The two break paths are kept separate: a pgdat mismatch breaks without
setting skip_next, so the mismatched object is picked up by the next
outer iteration; an alloc failure sets skip_next=true so that object
is skipped.  Both paths preserve the original per-object semantics.

> +		batch_bytes = obj_size * run_len;
>  		stock = trylock_stock();
> -		if (!stock || !__consume_obj_stock(objcg, stock, obj_size)) {
> +		if (!stock || !__consume_obj_stock(objcg, stock, batch_bytes)) {
>  			size_t remainder;
>
>  			unlock_stock(stock);
> -			if (__obj_cgroup_charge(objcg, flags, obj_size, &remainder))
> +			if (__obj_cgroup_charge(objcg, flags, batch_bytes, &remainder))
>  				return false;

Error-recovery contract is preserved: if __obj_cgroup_charge() fails
we return false before the obj_ext->objcg assignment loop runs, so
kmem_cache_free_bulk() sees NULL objcg for every object in this batch
and skips uncharing them -- exactly as in the original.  I read
__consume_obj_stock(), __refill_obj_stock(), and __account_obj_stock()
to verify the trylock/unlock sequence around the charge path is
identical to the original code.

One minor type concern: batch_bytes is declared as unsigned int, but
it is computed as obj_size * run_len where both operands are size_t.
The multiplication is done in size_t and then truncated on assignment.
__account_obj_stock() takes "int nr", so a large-enough batch_bytes
would be sign-extended into a negative nr and corrupt the vmstat
counter.  In practice the kernel's bulk-alloc sizes and SLAB_ACCOUNT
object sizes keep the product well below UINT_MAX, but using size_t
for batch_bytes (matching obj_size) would close that gap at no cost.
Needs Work Migrate on fault for device pages 🔗 mpenttil@redhat.com 6p
This series adds a single-walk "migrate on fault" capability to HMM, allowing hmm_range_fault() to both fault in non-present pages and install migration entries. Several correctness issues are present in the test driver and in the plumbing between the HMM walk and the existing migrate_vma_pages()/migrate_vma_finalize() infrastructure.
Kconfig hmm include migrate_device tests
Author: Mika Penttilä <mpenttil@redhat.com>

[PATCH v6 0/6] Migrate on fault for device pages

The optimization is real and the approach is clean at a high level.
Several correctness issues need addressing before this is ready.

> diff --git a/lib/test_hmm.c b/lib/test_hmm.c

[ ... ]

> +static int do_fault_and_migrate(struct dmirror *dmirror,
> +                                struct hmm_range *range)
> +{
> +	struct migrate_vma *migrate = range->migrate;
> +	int ret;
> +
> +	mmap_read_lock(dmirror->notifier.mm);
> +
> +	/* Fault-in pages for migration and update device page table */
> +	ret = dmirror_range_fault(dmirror, range);
> +
> +	pr_debug("Migrating from sys mem to device mem\n");
> +	migrate_hmm_range_setup(range);
> +
> +	dmirror_migrate_alloc_and_copy(migrate, dmirror);
> +	migrate_vma_pages(migrate);
> +	dmirror_migrate_finalize_and_map(migrate, dmirror);
> +	migrate_vma_finalize(migrate);

If dmirror_range_fault() returns -EBUSY (mmu_interval_check_retry
fired mid-walk) or any other error, all four migration functions
still execute on a partially-filled src_pfns array.  Entries not
reached by the walk will have MIGRATE_PFN_MIGRATE set but no valid
page PFN -- the anonymous-hole encoding produced by
migrate_hmm_range_setup().  __migrate_device_pages() takes this path
for every such entry:

    if (!page) {
        if (!(src_pfns[i] & MIGRATE_PFN_MIGRATE))
            goto next;
        VM_BUG_ON(!migrate);
        addr = migrate->start + i * PAGE_SIZE;
        if (!notified) {
            mmu_notifier_range_init_owner(&range,
                MMU_NOTIFY_MIGRATE, 0,
                migrate->vma->vm_mm, ...);   /* deref here */

If migrate->vma was not yet populated by the aborted walk this is a
NULL deref.  Migration must be skipped on fault failure:

    ret = dmirror_range_fault(dmirror, range);
    if (ret)
        goto out_mmput;

> +static int dmirror_fault_and_migrate_to_device(struct dmirror *dmirror,
> +                                               struct hmm_dmirror_cmd *cmd)
> +{
> +	unsigned long src_pfns[PFNS_ARRAY_SIZE] = { 0 };
> +	unsigned long dst_pfns[PFNS_ARRAY_SIZE] = { 0 };
> +	struct migrate_vma migrate = { 0 };

migrate.start and migrate.end are zero-initialized and are never
explicitly set in this function.  migrate_hmm_range_setup() computes:

    migrate->npages = (migrate->end - migrate->start) >> PAGE_SHIFT;

With both at zero npages == 0, the loop body never executes and
nothing is migrated.  The cover letter says "migrate_vma.vma gets
populated" by the HMM walk; presumably migrate->start/end are also
set there.  If so, that assignment is not visible in the posted
patches and should be clearly documented.  If it is not done, this
is a silent no-op.

Similarly, migrate_vma_insert_page() and the THP variant both begin
with:

    struct vm_area_struct *vma = migrate->vma;
    struct mm_struct *mm = vma->vm_mm;

If the walk did not populate migrate->vma these crash.  Can the code
add a WARN_ON(!migrate->vma) immediately after migrate_hmm_range_setup()
to make the invariant explicit?

> diff --git a/mm/hmm.c b/mm/hmm.c

[ ... ]

> +#ifdef CONFIG_DEVICE_MIGRATION
> +static int hmm_vma_handle_migrate_prepare(const struct mm_walk *walk,
> +                                          pmd_t *pmdp,
> +                                          pte_t *ptep,
> +                                          unsigned long addr,
> +                                          unsigned long *hmm_pfn,
> +                                          bool *unmapped)

For non-ZONE_DEVICE (system memory) folios being migrated to the
device, the existing migrate_vma_collect_pmd() does three things
beyond just installing the migration PTE:

  1. folio_remove_rmap_pte() -- removes the reverse mapping so
     mapcount drops to zero.
  2. folio_put() -- drops the pinning reference taken with folio_get().
  3. The subsequent migrate_device_unmap() call performs lru_add_drain(),
     folio_isolate_lru(), try_to_migrate() for multiply-mapped folios,
     and migrate_vma_check_page() to verify the page is not pinned.

Without LRU isolation, folio_migrate_mapping() will see:

    (folio_ref_count(folio) - extra) > folio_mapcount(folio)

because the LRU still holds a reference while mapcount is now 0,
causing migration to be silently aborted for every normal anonymous
page.  The new test only passes today because freshly faulted pages
may still be in the per-CPU LRU pagevec (before lru_add_drain()).

Does hmm_vma_handle_migrate_prepare() call folio_remove_rmap_pte()
for PTEs it clears?  And where is the equivalent of
migrate_device_unmap()'s lru_add_drain() + folio_isolate_lru() +
try_to_migrate() in the new path?

> +	if (pmd_trans_huge(*pmdp)) {
> +		if (!(minfo & MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_SYSTEM))
> +			goto out;
> +		...
> +		r = set_pmd_migration_entry(&pvmw, folio_page(folio, 0));
> +		if (r) {
> +			hmm_pfn[0] &= ~(HMM_PFN_MIGRATE | HMM_PFN_COMPOUND);
> +			r = -ENOENT;  // fallback
> +			goto unlock_out;
> +		}

The existing migrate_vma_collect_huge_pmd() sends
MMU_NOTIFY_MIGRATE (carrying pgmap_owner) via
mmu_notifier_range_init_owner() before installing the PMD migration
entry.  This lets device drivers skip flushing their device page
tables for device-private pages they own.  The hmm_vma_walk struct
gains a mmu_notifier_range field, but whether
mmu_notifier_invalidate_range_start() with MMU_NOTIFY_MIGRATE and
pgmap_owner is called before any migration entry is installed is not
visible in the posted diff.  Can you confirm this notification is
sent at the right time, or point to where in the walk it happens?

> diff --git a/lib/test_hmm_uapi.h b/lib/test_hmm_uapi.h

> -#define HMM_DMIRROR_MIGRATE_TO_SYS	_IOWR('H', 0x03, ...)
> -#define HMM_DMIRROR_SNAPSHOT		_IOWR('H', 0x04, ...)
> +#define HMM_DMIRROR_MIGRATE_ON_FAULT_TO_DEV _IOWR('H', 0x03, ...)
> +#define HMM_DMIRROR_MIGRATE_TO_SYS	     _IOWR('H', 0x04, ...)
> +#define HMM_DMIRROR_SNAPSHOT		     _IOWR('H', 0x05, ...)

Renumbering every IOCTL >= 0x03 breaks any existing selftest binary
compiled against the old header: a compiled test issuing 0x03 now
triggers MIGRATE_ON_FAULT_TO_DEV instead of MIGRATE_TO_SYS.  The
IOCTL encoding is part of the kernel-userspace ABI even for test
modules.  The new ioctl should be appended at the end (0x09) rather
than inserted in the middle.

> diff --git a/include/linux/migrate.h b/include/linux/migrate.h

> +enum migrate_vma_info {
> +	MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_NONE = 0,
> +	MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_COMPOUND = MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_NONE,
> +};
> +
> +static inline enum migrate_vma_info
> +hmm_select_migrate(struct hmm_range *range)
> +{
> +	return MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_NONE;
> +}

This is the !CONFIG_MIGRATION stub.  MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_COMPOUND is
aliased to 0 here, but is (1 << 3) in the real enum.  Any code that
tests (minfo & MIGRATE_VMA_SELECT_COMPOUND) would silently get a
different result in stub builds.  Make the stub enum match the real
values, or at minimum do not alias COMPOUND to NONE.

Looks Good userfaultfd: unassigned vma leads to a potential unreleased locks 🔗 Edward Adam Davis 1p
mfill_get_vma() assigned state->vma only on the success path, so mfill_put_vma() — which uses state->vma as a NULL sentinel — returned early on every error path without releasing the VMA read lock or map_changing_lock. The fix moves the assignment to immediately after uffd_mfill_lock() succeeds, before any validation checks, so cleanup is always symmetric.
userfaultfd
Edward Adam Davis <eadavis@qq.com>

userfaultfd: unassigned vma leads to a potential unreleased locks

Verified the fix by tracing lock acquire/release symmetry across
mfill_get_vma() and mfill_put_vma().

> diff --git a/mm/userfaultfd.c b/mm/userfaultfd.c
> --- a/mm/userfaultfd.c
> +++ b/mm/userfaultfd.c
> @@ -218,6 +218,7 @@ static int mfill_get_vma(struct mfill_state *state)
>  	if (IS_ERR(dst_vma))
>  		return PTR_ERR(dst_vma);
>  
> +	state->vma = dst_vma;

The assignment sits after uffd_mfill_lock() succeeds (which holds the
VMA read lock) but before down_read(&ctx->map_changing_lock) and all
validation checks.  Every error path in mfill_get_vma() goes via
out_unlock: -> mfill_put_vma(), which guards on (state->vma != NULL)
before calling up_read(map_changing_lock) + uffd_mfill_unlock().  With
state->vma set early, both locks are now released correctly on every
error path.

> @@ -257,7 +258,6 @@ static int mfill_get_vma(struct mfill_state *state)
>  		goto out_unlock;
>  
>  out:
> -	state->vma = dst_vma;
>  	return 0;

The hugetlb "goto out" path (which bypasses out_unlock entirely) is
also correct: both locks remain intentionally held and the caller drops
them later via mfill_put_vma().  The NULL sentinel is valid on first
entry because the compound-literal initialisation in mfill_atomic()
zero-initialises fields not explicitly named, including vma.

Locking and error-path symmetry look correct.

Reviewed-by: [reviewer]

zram: propagate read_from_bdev_async() errors

Checked the bio chaining, resource cleanup, and error propagation.

> -static void read_from_bdev_async(struct zram *zram, struct page *page,
> -				 u32 index, unsigned long blk_idx,

> +				struct bio *parent)

Verified: bio_inc_remaining(parent) is only reached on the success path,
after both kmalloc_obj() and bio_alloc() succeed, so neither error return
leaves the parent bio with an incremented remaining count that would never
be paired with a bio_endio().

> 	req = kmalloc_obj(*req, GFP_NOIO);
> 	if (!req)
> -		return;
> +		return -ENOMEM;
>
> 	bio = bio_alloc(zram->bdev, 1, parent->bi_opf, GFP_NOIO);

> 		kfree(req);
> -		return;
> +		return -ENOMEM;
> 	}

Cleanup is symmetric: the bio_alloc() failure path correctly frees req
before returning, matching the success-path teardown in

> -	read_from_bdev_async(zram, page, index, blk_idx, parent);
> -	return 0;

Looks Good userfaultfd: fix lock leak in mfill_get_vma() 🔗 Andrei Vagin 1p
Fixes a lock leak in mfill_get_vma() where error paths after acquiring both the per-VMA lock and map_changing_lock would call mfill_put_vma() with state->vma still NULL, causing it to return early without releasing either lock.
userfaultfd
Author: Andrei Vagin <avagin@google.com>

userfaultfd: fix lock leak in mfill_get_vma()

Verified the fix by reading the full mfill_get_vma() implementation,
mfill_put_vma(), both CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK and !CONFIG_PER_VMA_LOCK
variants of uffd_mfill_lock/uffd_mfill_unlock, and the caller
mfill_atomic().

> -	down_read(&ctx->map_changing_lock);
> +	down_read(&ctx->map_changing_lock);
> +	state->vma = dst_vma;
>  	err = -EAGAIN;
>  	if (atomic_read(&ctx->mmap_changing))
>  		goto out_unlock;

Correct. By assigning state->vma immediately after acquiring
map_changing_lock, all subsequent error paths reach out_unlock with
state->vma non-NULL, so mfill_put_vma() correctly calls
up_read(&ctx->map_changing_lock) and uffd_mfill_unlock(state->vma)
instead of returning early. The state struct is initialized via a
compound literal in mfill_atomic(), so vma starts as NULL and the
early IS_ERR(dst_vma) return path (before either lock is acquired)
still correctly leaves state->vma NULL.

> -	if (is_vm_hugetlb_page(dst_vma))
> -		goto out;
> +	if (is_vm_hugetlb_page(dst_vma))
> +		return 0;

The old goto-out path was equivalent to (state->vma = dst_vma; return
0) with both locks held. The new path reaches return 0 with state->vma
already assigned and both locks still held -- identical observable
behavior. The caller in mfill_atomic() then hands state.vma to
mfill_atomic_hugetlb() and returns, which is unchanged.

Looks good to me.
Needs Work mm/mglru: fix cgroup OOM during MGLRU state switching 🔗 Leno Hou via B4 Relay 2p
This two-patch series introduces a 'draining' intermediate state for MGLRU enable/disable transitions to prevent a reclaim vacuum that causes spurious cgroup OOM kills, and adds shadow entry context tracking to correctly dispatch workingset refaults after state transitions. The approach is sound but the visible diff is missing critical pieces that make it impossible to verify correctness.
include rmap swap vmscan workingset
From: Leno Hou <lenohou@gmail.com>
Subject: [PATCH v3 1/2] mm/mglru: fix cgroup OOM during MGLRU state switching

Thanks for the patch.  The problem statement is real and the draining-state
approach is a reasonable way to fix it.  However there are several issues
in the visible diff that need addressing.

> diff --git a/include/linux/mm_inline.h b/include/linux/mm_inline.h
> +static inline bool lru_gen_draining(void)
> +{
> +	DECLARE_STATIC_KEY_FALSE(lru_drain_core);
> +
> +	return static_branch_unlikely(&lru_drain_core);
> +}

DECLARE_STATIC_KEY_FALSE() here is an extern declaration; the key must be
defined somewhere with DEFINE_STATIC_KEY_FALSE(lru_drain_core).  The base
tree (vmscan.c:2629) only defines lru_gen_caps.  The visible portion of
the vmscan.c diff does not show a DEFINE for lru_drain_core.  Is the
definition in the truncated portion of the hunk?  Without it the patch
would not link.

Similarly, the base lru_gen_change_state() never calls
static_branch_enable/disable on lru_drain_core, so the draining window
is never actually opened.  Are those calls in the truncated part of the
vmscan.c diff?  Please post the full diff so reviewers can verify the
complete mechanism end-to-end.

> diff --git a/mm/swap.c b/mm/swap.c
> -	if (lru_gen_enabled()) {
> +	if (folio_lru_gen(folio) != -1) {
>  		lru_gen_inc_refs(folio);
>  		return;
>  	}

This changes behavior for folios not yet added to any LRU list.  A folio
sitting in a per-cpu folio_batch has LRU_GEN_MASK == 0, so
folio_lru_gen() == -1.  Under the old code lru_gen_inc_refs() was called
for all folios while MGLRU is enabled; under the new code it is skipped
for those folios.  The LRU_REFS bits set by lru_gen_inc_refs() affect the
eviction tier in lru_gen_eviction() via lru_tier_from_refs().  For a
folio accessed several times before its folio_batch drains, the tier will
be underestimated.  Is this intentional?  The commit message does not
call it out.

> -	bool active = folio_test_active(folio) || lru_gen_enabled();
> +	bool active = folio_test_active(folio) || (folio_lru_gen(folio) != -1);

This change in lru_deactivate_file() is correct: it uses per-folio state
rather than the global flag, which is the right behaviour during the
draining window when some folios remain on MGLRU lists and others have
already been moved to the traditional LRU.

> diff --git a/mm/vmscan.c b/mm/vmscan.c
> +	/* whether in lru gen scan context */
> +	unsigned int lru_gen:1;

[ ... ]

> +	sc->lru_gen = 0;
>  	nr_reclaimed = shrink_folio_list(&folio_list, pgdat, sc, &stat,

The sc object is stack-allocated by the top-level caller and shared
across the full shrink_lruvec() call chain.  Mutating sc->lru_gen inside
both shrink_inactive_list() and evict_folios() is correct only because
each write immediately precedes its corresponding shrink_folio_list()
call and no downstream caller reads sc->lru_gen outside of
__remove_mapping().  This invariant is non-obvious.  A comment, or
passing lru_gen as a direct parameter to shrink_folio_list(), would make
the intent clearer and less fragile.

> +retry:
> +	sc->lru_gen = 1;
>  	reclaimed = shrink_folio_list(&list, pgdat, sc, &stat, false, memcg);

This is in evict_folios(), so sc->lru_gen=1 is correct.  The retry label
is also jumped to from a later goto after move_folios_to_lru() has run.
sc->lru_gen=1 is right before the label so it is reset on each pass
through retry -- that looks correct, just worth confirming.

> diff --git a/mm/rmap.c b/mm/rmap.c
> -		if (lru_gen_enabled() && pvmw.pte) {
> +		if (lru_gen_enabled() && !lru_gen_draining() && pvmw.pte) {

Suppressing lru_gen_look_around() for the entire draining window is safe
but potentially wide.  On large systems with many memcgs and nodes,
lru_gen_change_state() iterates every lruvec while draining.  During
that whole window look_around is disabled system-wide.  Is this
performance tradeoff acceptable, or should the suppression be scoped more
tightly (e.g., per-lruvec)?

> --- [PATCH v3 2/2] mm/mglru: maintain workingset refault context

Adding WORKINGSET_MGLRU_SHIFT increases EVICTION_SHIFT by 1, shrinking
EVICTION_MASK by 1 bit and reducing eviction timestamp precision for all
shadow entries on all systems.  The BUILD_BUG_ON in lru_gen_eviction()
guards against actual overflow, but the precision loss on 64-bit systems
that don't hit the BUILD_BUG_ON is still a real tradeoff.  Please
document it in the commit message.

The workingset.c diff is truncated.  The modifications to pack_shadow(),
unpack_shadow(), workingset_test_recent(), and workingset_refault() that
carry and dispatch the is_mglru bit are not visible.  Please send the
complete diff for review.

Looks Good mm/damon: support MADV_COLLAPSE via DAMOS_COLLAPSE scheme action 🔗 <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com> 1p
Adds DAMOS_COLLAPSE, a new DAMOS scheme action that calls madvise_collapse() synchronously to collapse a virtual address region into a THP, independent of khugepaged. The implementation routes through the existing damos_madvise() helper with MADV_COLLAPSE.
damon/sysfs-schemes damon/vaddr docs include
Author: Asier Gutierrez <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com>

mm/damon: support MADV_COLLAPSE via DAMOS_COLLAPSE scheme action

Looks good to me.  Checked the following:

> +	case DAMOS_COLLAPSE:
> +		madv_action = MADV_COLLAPSE;
> +		break;

damos_madvise() calls do_madvise() which, for MADV_COLLAPSE, takes
mmap_read_lock internally (get_lock_mode() in madvise.c returns
MADVISE_MMAP_READ_LOCK for MADV_COLLAPSE).  No lock is held by the
caller before entering damos_madvise(), so there is no deadlock or
lock ordering concern.

When CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is disabled, madvise_behavior_valid()
does not include MADV_COLLAPSE (it lives under #ifdef
CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE alongside MADV_HUGEPAGE/MADV_NOHUGEPAGE),
so do_madvise() returns -EINVAL and damos_madvise() returns 0 bytes
applied.  This is identical to how DAMOS_HUGEPAGE and DAMOS_NOHUGEPAGE
behave under the same config; the documentation note about silent
failure is accurate.

The fvaddr operations set shares damon_va_apply_scheme() directly, so
it inherits the new case without any additional change needed.  The
paddr operations set has a default no-op case; DAMOS_COLLAPSE correctly
falls through to it, matching the doc restricting support to
vaddr/fvaddr.

Sysfs action_show/store iterate damos_sysfs_action_names[] by name
string and enum value comparison (not by array index), so inserting
DAMOS_COLLAPSE between DAMOS_NOHUGEPAGE and DAMOS_LRU_PRIO, which
shifts subsequent enum values, does not break the sysfs interface.
NR_DAMOS_ACTIONS is defined but not used as an array bound anywhere
in-tree.
Looks Good mm/damon/stat: monitor all System RAM resources 🔗 SeongJae Park 1p
The patch fixes DAMON_STAT to monitor all System RAM resources instead of only the largest one, by replacing damon_set_region_biggest_system_ram_default() with a new walk that captures the bounding box [first_start, last_end] across all System RAM regions.
damon/stat
SeongJae Park <sj@kernel.org>

mm/damon/stat: monitor all System RAM resources

Verified the walk logic, address conversion, error paths, and how
non-RAM gaps in the bounding box are handled by paddr ops.

> +static int damon_stat_system_ram_walk_fn(struct resource *res, void *arg)
> +{
> +	struct damon_stat_system_ram_range_walk_arg *a = arg;
> +
> +	if (!a->walked) {
> +		a->walked = true;
> +		a->res.start = res->start;
> +	}
> +	a->res.end = res->end;
> +	return 0;
> +}

walk_system_ram_res() iterates in ascending address order (via
walk_res_desc which advances start = res.end + 1 each step).  The
callback correctly records the start of the first region and keeps
overwriting res.end so the last region's end is retained, producing a
correct bounding box.  Returning 0 unconditionally ensures all regions
are visited.

> +	walk_system_ram_res(0, -1, &arg, damon_stat_system_ram_walk_fn);
> +	if (!arg.walked)
> +		return -EINVAL;
> +	addr_range.start = damon_stat_res_to_core_addr(
> +			arg.res.start, addr_unit);
> +	addr_range.end = damon_stat_res_to_core_addr(
> +			arg.res.end + 1, addr_unit);
> +	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, 1, min_region_sz);

damon_stat_res_to_core_addr() is an exact copy of the static
damon_res_to_core_addr() in core.c, including the div_u64() path for
the 64-bit resource_size_t / 32-bit unsigned long combination.  The
+1 on arg.res.end correctly converts the inclusive end to an exclusive
end for DAMON's addr_range convention, matching what
damon_find_biggest_system_ram() did for the single-region case.

ctx->addr_unit is initialised to 1 by damon_new_ctx() and is not
changed by damon_select_ops(), so there is no division-by-zero hazard.

The -EINVAL return propagates to damon_stat_build_ctx()'s goto
free_out, which calls damon_destroy_ctx() -- the same cleanup path
triggered by the old function returning an error.

For non-RAM gaps between System RAM regions that now fall inside the
bounding box: damon_pa_prepare_access_checks() samples a random
address in each region and calls damon_pa_mkold(), which calls
damon_get_folio(); if there is no folio at that physical address the
function returns early without touching anything.  Similarly
damon_pa_young() returns false for addresses with no backing folio.
So gaps are treated as not-accessed, which is harmless.

Looks good.
Looks Good fixup: mm/memory: inline unmap_page_range() into __zap_vma_range() 🔗 SeongJae Park 7p
A 7-patch series containing critical damon_set_regions() argument fixes (addr_unit passed as nr_ranges instead of 1), a 32-bit LPAE address overflow guard in damon/stat, a khugepaged threshold-checking refactoring that centralizes MADV_COLLAPSE vs khugepaged thresholds, a trivial variable rename in mm/memory.c, and a userfaultfd behavior restoration for WP_ASYNC on VMAs without vm_uffd_ops (e.g., SysV shared memory).
damon/core damon/stat docs khugepaged memory userfaultfd
From: reviewer
To: linux-mm@kvack.org

Series: fixup: mm/memory: inline unmap_page_range() into __zap_vma_range()

Reviewed each patch against the actual source in mm/damon/stat.c,
mm/damon/core.c, mm/khugepaged.c, mm/memory.c, and mm/userfaultfd.c.

---

[PATCH] mm/damon/stat: fix wrong argument to damon_set_regions()
[PATCH] mm/damon/core: fix wrong damon_set_regions() argument

> -	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, addr_unit, min_region_sz);
> +	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, 1, min_region_sz);

Clear critical fix in both sites.  Passing addr_unit (e.g. PAGE_SIZE =
4096) as the nr_ranges argument would cause damon_set_regions() to
iterate 4095 ranges past the end of the single-element stack variable
addr_range.  Verified the callers propagate the error return correctly:
damon_stat_build_ctx() uses "goto free_out" -> damon_destroy_ctx(),
which frees the target already added to the context at that point.

---

[PATCH] mm/damon/stat: return error if monitoring target region is invalid

> +	if (addr_range.end <= addr_range.start)
> +		return -EINVAL;
>  	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, 1, min_region_sz);

On 32-bit LPAE, resource_size_t is u64 but unsigned long is 32-bit.
damon_stat_res_to_core_addr() uses div_u64() precisely to handle this;
if the result of dividing (res.end + 1) by addr_unit exceeds ULONG_MAX
the truncation yields 0, making addr_range.end = 0 < addr_range.start.
The check catches that.  The -EINVAL propagates up through
damon_stat_build_ctx() via the existing "goto free_out" path, which is
symmetric with the success path.

---

[PATCH] tmp (khugepaged refactoring)

> +static int collapse_max_ptes_none(struct collapse_control *cc,
> +		struct vm_area_struct *vma)
> +{
> +	if (vma && userfaultfd_armed(vma))
> +		return 0;
> +	if (!cc->is_khugepaged)
> +		return HPAGE_PMD_NR;
> +	return khugepaged_max_ptes_none;
> +}

Verified all three helpers produce semantically equivalent results
for every branch.

__collapse_huge_page_isolate, none_or_zero path:
The old condition
  !userfaultfd_armed(vma) && (!cc->is_khugepaged || count <= limit)
maps exactly to the new count > max_ptes_none check:
- uffd armed:          max=0,           first increment triggers failure
- MADV_COLLAPSE:       max=HPAGE_PMD_NR, loop cap (HPAGE_PMD_NR iters)
                       means count > HPAGE_PMD_NR is never true
- khugepaged, no uffd: max=khugepaged_max_ptes_none, same threshold

The shared-PTE path follows the same logic with collapse_max_ptes_shared.

hpage_collapse_scan_pmd, swap-PTE path:
The restructuring checks the count limit first, then pte_swp_uffd_wp_any().
In the old code pte_swp_uffd_wp_any() was only evaluated when the limit
was not exceeded, which is identical to the new ordering.

hpage_collapse_scan_file (collapse_scan_file in current tree):
max_ptes_none is computed with vma=NULL, correctly skipping the
userfaultfd_armed() check that is only meaningful for anon VMAs.
For the end-of-scan "present < HPAGE_PMD_NR - max_ptes_none" check:
when !cc->is_khugepaged, max_ptes_none = HPAGE_PMD_NR, the threshold
collapses to 0 and present (non-negative) never falls below it,
matching the old "cc->is_khugepaged &&" guard.

One observation worth documenting: the file-scan swap counter uses
  swap += 1 << xas_get_order(&xas);
rather than a per-page increment.  The old code guarded with
!cc->is_khugepaged (unconditional pass for MADV_COLLAPSE); the new code
uses max_ptes_swap = HPAGE_PMD_NR for MADV_COLLAPSE.  A boundary-
spanning large swap folio whose xas order inflates the counter above
HPAGE_PMD_NR would now fail for MADV_COLLAPSE where it previously
succeeded.  In practice the scan window is exactly HPAGE_PMD_NR pages
so the total swap pages within the window cannot exceed HPAGE_PMD_NR,
making this impossible today.  A brief comment noting that
HPAGE_PMD_NR is chosen as "effectively unlimited" would help future
readers.

Also, the patch subject "tmp" should be replaced before merging.

---

[PATCH] fixup: mm/memory: inline unmap_page_range() into __zap_vma_range()

> -		unsigned long next, cur = start;
> +		unsigned long next, addr = start;
>  		...
> -		} while (pgd++, cur = next, cur != end);
> +		} while (pgd++, addr = next, addr != end);

Pure cosmetic rename; loop invariant and termination condition are
unchanged.

---

[PATCH 1/1] userfaultfd: allow registration of WP_ASYNC for any VMA

> -	/* only VMAs that implement vm_uffd_ops are supported */
> -	if (!ops)
> -		return false;
> -
> -	if (vma->vm_flags & VM_DROPPABLE)
> -		return false;
> -
>  	if (wp_async && (vm_flags == VM_UFFD_WP))
>  		return true;
>
> +	/* For any other mode reject VMAs that don't implement vm_uffd_ops */
> +	if (!ops)
> +		return false;
> +
> +	if (vma->vm_flags & VM_DROPPABLE)
> +		return false;

Verified via vma_uffd_ops(): anonymous VMAs always return &anon_uffd_ops
(non-NULL); shmem/SysV-shared VMAs backed by vm_ops that do not set
uffd_ops return NULL, so the old !ops check blocked them.  Moving the
WP_ASYNC+WP-only early return before that check restores the ability to
register those VMAs with WP_ASYNC, which is the stated regression fix.

The VM_DROPPABLE check is also bypassed for the WP_ASYNC+WP-only path.
WP_ASYNC write faults are resolved entirely by the generic fault handler
without any VMA-specific uffd dispatch, so skipping VM_DROPPABLE for
this path appears safe.  SysV shared memory (the primary target) does
not use VM_DROPPABLE today; confirming whether a hypothetical future
DROPPABLE+WP_ASYNC combination needs additional care in the fault path
would be a useful note in the commit message.

Overall the series is correct.  The two nits above (swap-counter comment
and "tmp" subject) are the only non-blocking observations.
