Needs Work mm/mempolicy: track user-defined mempolicy allocations 🔗 "JP Kobryn (Meta)" 1p
Adds per-node NUMA_MPOL_HIT/MISS/FOREIGN counters to track allocations driven by user-defined mempolicies, distinguishing intentional from fallback placements. The accounting function uses current->mempolicy to filter out non-user-policy allocations, but the actual allocation policy passed as pol can differ from current->mempolicy, causing both missed counts and phantom counts.
include mempolicy vmstat
mm/mempolicy: track user-defined mempolicy allocations

The overall goal is clear and the placement of instrumentation inside
alloc_pages_mpol() is sensible.  One correctness issue below.

> +static void mpol_count_numa_alloc(struct mempolicy *pol, int intended_nid,
> +				  struct page *page, unsigned int order)
> +{
> +	int actual_nid = page_to_nid(page);
> +	long nr_pages = 1L << order;
> +	bool is_hit;
> +
> +	if (!current->mempolicy)
> +		return;

This guard tests the wrong object.  The function receives pol, which is
the policy that actually governed the allocation.  current->mempolicy is
the task's top-level policy, and the two can diverge in at least two
important ways:

(1) VMA-level mbind() policy.  vma_alloc_folio_noprof() calls
    get_vma_policy(), which returns the VMA's explicit mbind() policy
    when one is set.  If the allocating task has no task-level policy
    (current->mempolicy == NULL), the guard fires and returns early,
    silently dropping all VMA-bound allocations.  mbind() is just as
    much a user designation as set_mempolicy(), so these should be
    counted.

(2) Interrupt-context allocations.  alloc_frozen_pages_noprof() passes
    &default_policy (mode MPOL_LOCAL) when in_interrupt() is true, so
    pol == &default_policy.  But current is the interrupted task, which
    may have a non-NULL mempolicy.  The guard does not fire and the
    interrupt-context allocation gets attributed to the interrupted
    task's policy -- a phantom count with no connection to any user
    decision.

Both bugs share the same root: the filter must operate on pol itself,
not on current->mempolicy.  The existing mpol_put_task_policy() shows
the right idiom for identifying kernel-internal policies:

  if (pol == &default_policy ||
      (pol >= &preferred_node_policy[0] &&
       pol <= &preferred_node_policy[ARRAY_SIZE(preferred_node_policy)-1]))
          return;

Using that pattern (or a small inline helper wrapping it) instead of the
current->mempolicy test would correctly exclude &default_policy and the
per-node preferred_node_policy[] entries while still counting both
task-level and VMA-level user policies.

> +	if (pol->mode == MPOL_BIND || pol->mode == MPOL_PREFERRED_MANY)
> +		is_hit = node_isset(actual_nid, pol->nodes);
> +	else
> +		is_hit = (actual_nid == intended_nid);
> +
> +	if (is_hit) {
> +		mod_node_page_state(NODE_DATA(actual_nid), NUMA_MPOL_HIT, nr_pages);
> +	} else {
> +		/* account for miss on the fallback node */
> +		mod_node_page_state(NODE_DATA(actual_nid), NUMA_MPOL_MISS, nr_pages);
> +
> +		/* account for foreign on the intended node */
> +		mod_node_page_state(NODE_DATA(intended_nid), NUMA_MPOL_FOREIGN, nr_pages);
> +	}

For MPOL_BIND without a home_node, intended_nid is the unmodified input
nid (typically numa_node_id()), which need not be inside pol->nodes.
When the bind nodemask is fully satisfied is_hit is true so intended_nid
is never consumed -- fine.  But when the allocator falls back outside the
bind nodemask, NUMA_MPOL_FOREIGN lands on an effectively arbitrary node
(the running CPU's home node).  Is that the intended semantics?  A short
comment on what intended_nid represents for BIND would help readers.

The goto-out refactoring looks correct: alloc_pages_preferred_many(),
the THP THISNODE fast path (both the success and the !__GFP_DIRECT_RECLAIM
NULL returns), and the general slow path all funnel through the single
out: label, and the if (page) guard ensures NULL-allocation paths are
not counted.
Needs Work mm: expand mmap_prepare functionality and usage 🔗 "Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle)" 16p
This series expands mmap_prepare by adding a vm_ops->mapped hook for post-mapping reference counting, a mmap_action_simple_ioremap() helper, stacked mmap_prepare support, and mmap_action_map_kernel_pages(). The AFS refcount fix is correct, but there is a concrete regression in io_remap_pfn_range_prepare/complete that double-applies the io_remap_pfn_range_pfn() transformation on MIPS Alchemy and SPARC.
docs drivers fs include internal memory tests util vma
Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle) &lt;ljs@kernel.org&gt;

mm: various small mmap_prepare cleanups
mm: add vm_ops-&gt;mapped hook

[ ... ]

--- a/mm/internal.h
+++ b/mm/internal.h

&gt; -static inline void io_remap_pfn_range_prepare(struct vm_area_desc *desc,
&gt; -		unsigned long orig_pfn, unsigned long size)
&gt; +static inline int io_remap_pfn_range_prepare(struct vm_area_desc *desc)
&gt;  {
&gt; +	struct mmap_action *action = &amp;desc-&gt;action;
&gt; +	const unsigned long orig_pfn = action-&gt;remap.start_pfn;
&gt; +	const unsigned long size = action-&gt;remap.size;
&gt;  	const unsigned long pfn = io_remap_pfn_range_pfn(orig_pfn, size);
&gt;
&gt; -	return remap_pfn_range_prepare(desc, pfn);
&gt; +	action-&gt;remap.start_pfn = pfn;
&gt; +	return remap_pfn_range_prepare(desc);
&gt;  }

This writes the post-transformation PFN back into
action-&gt;remap.start_pfn in-place.

&gt; -static inline int io_remap_pfn_range_complete(struct vm_area_struct *vma,
&gt; -		unsigned long addr, unsigned long orig_pfn, unsigned long size,
&gt; -		pgprot_t orig_prot)
&gt; +static inline int io_remap_pfn_range_complete(struct vm_area_struct *vma,
&gt; +					      struct mmap_action *action)
&gt;  {
&gt; +	const unsigned long size = action-&gt;remap.size;
&gt; +	const unsigned long orig_pfn = action-&gt;remap.start_pfn;
&gt; +	const pgprot_t orig_prot = vma-&gt;vm_page_prot;
&gt;
&gt; +	action-&gt;remap.pgprot = pgprot_decrypted(orig_prot);
&gt; +	action-&gt;remap.start_pfn  = io_remap_pfn_range_pfn(orig_pfn, size);
&gt; 	return remap_pfn_range_complete(vma, action);
&gt;  }

The variable is named orig_pfn but action-&gt;remap.start_pfn was already
overwritten by io_remap_pfn_range_prepare() with the post-transformation
value. io_remap_pfn_range_pfn() is now applied a second time to an
already-translated PFN.

In the old code, prepare and complete each received the original PFN
as an independent parameter and applied the transformation once. In
the new code, prepare stores the transformed PFN into
action-&gt;remap.start_pfn in-place, and complete reads back that same
field and transforms it again.

On most architectures io_remap_pfn_range_pfn() is a no-op and returns
pfn unchanged, so this passes unnoticed. On MIPS Alchemy
(arch/mips/alchemy/common/setup.c) it translates CPU-physical PFNs
to PCI bus PFNs via fixup_bigphys_addr(), and on SPARC 32/64 it
performs an analogous translation. Calling it twice on the same value
produces a wrong PFN and maps the wrong physical page.

All drivers converted in this series via mmap_action_simple_ioremap()
go through simple_ioremap_prepare() -&gt; mmap_action_ioremap() -&gt;
mmap_action_prepare() -&gt; io_remap_pfn_range_prepare() (first
transform), then mmap_action_complete() -&gt;
io_remap_pfn_range_complete() (second transform). They are all
broken on MIPS Alchemy and SPARC.

A minimal fix is to drop the io_remap_pfn_range_pfn() call from the
complete path, since prepare already stored the translated value:

    static inline int
    io_remap_pfn_range_complete(struct vm_area_struct *vma,
                                struct mmap_action *action)
    {
        action-&gt;remap.pgprot = pgprot_decrypted(vma-&gt;vm_page_prot);
        /* start_pfn already translated by prepare */
        return remap_pfn_range_complete(vma, action);
    }

Alternatively, store the original PFN in the action and translate
only in complete, removing the in-place modification from prepare.

[ ... ]

--- a/mm/vma.c
+++ b/mm/vma.c

&gt; +static void maybe_drop_file_rmap_lock(struct mmap_state *map,
&gt; +				      struct vm_area_struct *vma)
&gt; +{
&gt; +	if (!map-&gt;hold_file_rmap_lock)
&gt; +		return;
&gt; +	file = vma-&gt;vm_file;
&gt; +	i_mmap_unlock_write(file-&gt;f_mapping);
&gt; +}

If mmap_action_complete() fails for an action type whose error path
calls unmap_vma_locked() in mmap_action_finish(), the VMA is freed
before maybe_drop_file_rmap_lock() dereferences vma-&gt;vm_file. Today
this cannot fire because hide_from_rmap_until_complete (the only
setter of hold_file_rmap_lock) is used only by hugetlbfs with a
MMAP_NOTHING action type (err==0 in mmap_action_finish, so
unmap_vma_locked is never reached), but the invariant is only
implied. A future action type that sets both flags and can fail in
the complete step would trigger a use-after-free. Could the file
pointer be saved before calling mmap_action_complete() to make this
explicitly safe?

&gt; +static int afs_mapped(unsigned long start, unsigned long end,

&gt; +	afs_add_open_mmap(vnode);

The refcount move to the mapped callback looks correct. Verified:
afs_mapped() is called only for a non-merged VMA, symmetric with
afs_vm_close() on every removal. afs_vm_open() covers fork and split.
afs_mapped() always returns 0 so call_mapped_hook() never reaches
unmap_vma_locked() for AFS.

Looks Good zswap pool per-CPU acomp_ctx simplifications 🔗 "Kanchana P. Sridhar" 2p
Patch 1 removes redundant IS_ERR_OR_NULL() checks in zswap_cpu_comp_dead() and adds comments on crypto API return value semantics. Patch 2 ties per-CPU acomp_ctx lifetime to the pool (no teardown on CPU offline) and refactors cleanup into acomp_ctx_free() with post-free NULL assignments.
zswap
From: &lt;reviewer&gt;
Subject: Re: [PATCH v2 0/2] zswap pool per-CPU acomp_ctx simplifications

[ patch 1 ]

> -	if (IS_ERR_OR_NULL(acomp_ctx))
> +	if (!acomp_ctx)
>  		return 0;

Verified: acomp_ctx comes from per_cpu_ptr(pool->acomp_ctx, cpu),
which can never be NULL or an ERR pointer since pool->acomp_ctx was
successfully returned by alloc_percpu_gfp().  Changing to !acomp_ctx
is correct and removes the misleading IS_ERR branch.

> -	if (!IS_ERR_OR_NULL(req))
> +	if (req)
>  		acomp_request_free(req);
>  	if (!IS_ERR_OR_NULL(acomp))
>  		crypto_free_acomp(acomp);

The asymmetry here is correct: acomp_request_alloc() returns NULL on
failure (never an ERR pointer), so plain !req is sufficient.  The
IS_ERR_OR_NULL check on acomp must stay because crypto_alloc_acomp_node()
returns an ERR pointer (never NULL) on failure; if zswap_cpu_comp_prepare()
stored that ERR pointer into acomp_ctx->acomp before the teardown call
ran, dropping to just !acomp would wrongly attempt to free an ERR
pointer.  Leaving it unchanged is the right call.

[ patch 2 ]

> +static void acomp_ctx_free(struct crypto_acomp_ctx *acomp_ctx)
> +{
> +	if (!acomp_ctx)
> +		return;

This guard is dead code: every call site passes per_cpu_ptr() which
never yields NULL.  Harmless, but could be dropped.

> +	if (acomp_ctx->req)
> +		acomp_request_free(acomp_ctx->req);
> +	acomp_ctx->req = NULL;
> +
> +	if (!IS_ERR_OR_NULL(acomp_ctx->acomp))
> +		crypto_free_acomp(acomp_ctx->acomp);
> +	acomp_ctx->acomp = NULL;
> +
> +	kfree(acomp_ctx->buffer);
> +	acomp_ctx->buffer = NULL;

Checked all call sites and orderings:

1. From zswap_cpu_comp_prepare() fail path: mutex_init() runs only
   at the end of a successful prepare, so the mutex is never held
   here; safe to free without locking.  After return, all fields are
   NULL, so a subsequent online event correctly re-enters the
   allocation path via the acomp_ctx->acomp == NULL check.

2. From zswap_pool_destroy(): called only from __zswap_pool_release(),
   which runs after percpu_ref_is_zero() is confirmed (WARN_ON there
   verifies it).  The percpu_ref is held by every caller of
   zswap_compress()/zswap_decompress() for the pool lifetime
   (zswap_pool_current_get() in the store path; the entry->pool ref
   kept alive by the xarray entry in the load path).  By the time
   __zswap_pool_release() runs, no thread can be inside
   mutex_lock(&acomp_ctx->mutex), so unlocked teardown is safe.

The removal of the CPU-offline teardown callback is sound under the
same reasoning: resources persist until pool destruction, and pool
destruction is gated on the percpu_ref reaching zero, which cannot
happen while any compress/decompress operation is in flight.

Looks good to me.

  • [PATCH v2 1/2] mm: zswap: Remove redundant checks in zswap_cpu_comp_dead().
  • [PATCH v2 2/2] mm: zswap: Tie per-CPU acomp_ctx lifetime to the pool.
Minor Issues RDMA: Enable operation with DMA debug enabled 🔗 Leon Romanovsky 8p
This series introduces DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT to reject mappings on non-coherent or SWIOTLB systems, fixes a spurious WARN_ONCE for cache-clean overlapping mappings, renames DMA_ATTR_CPU_CACHE_CLEAN to DMA_ATTR_DEBUGGING_IGNORE_CACHELINES, and applies the new attribute to RDMA umem and HMM to prevent silent data corruption on incoherent systems.
docs drivers hmm include kernel
On Mon, Mar 17 2026, Leon Romanovsky wrote:

Series: RDMA: Enable operation with DMA debug enabled

--- [PATCH v3 1/8] dma-debug: Allow multiple invocations of overlapping entries ---

> -static void active_cacheline_inc_overlap(phys_addr_t cln)
> +static void active_cacheline_inc_overlap(phys_addr_t cln, bool is_cache_clean)
>  {
>  	int overlap = active_cacheline_read_overlap(cln);
>  	overlap = active_cacheline_set_overlap(cln, ++overlap);
> -	WARN_ONCE(overlap > ACTIVE_CACHELINE_MAX_OVERLAP,
> +	WARN_ONCE(!is_cache_clean && overlap > ACTIVE_CACHELINE_MAX_OVERLAP,

Verified against the existing dma_debug_entry struct: is_cache_clean is
declared 'bool', so passing entry->is_cache_clean directly is correct.
The WARN suppression is consistent with add_dma_entry, which also gates
the overlap error on both sides carrying is_cache_clean.  Patch 1 and
the add_dma_entry check in patch 4 form a consistent pair.  Looks good.

--- [PATCH v3 3/8] dma-mapping: Clarify valid conditions for CPU cache line overlap ---

> -	entry->is_cache_clean = !!(attrs & DMA_ATTR_CPU_CACHE_CLEAN);
> +	entry->is_cache_clean = attrs & DMA_ATTR_DEBUGGING_IGNORE_CACHELINES;

The '!!' is dropped.  Since is_cache_clean is 'bool', C's implicit
conversion from any non-zero integer to 'true' makes this safe
(DMA_ATTR_DEBUGGING_IGNORE_CACHELINES = 1UL<<11 is non-zero).  Patch 4
extends this to OR two attr bits, so the value is still non-zero
whenever either attr is set.  Not a bug, but dropping '!!' from a
flag-mask assignment is an unusual style choice; the original was more
self-documenting.

--- [PATCH v3 4/8] dma-mapping: Introduce DMA require coherency attribute ---

> +	if (!dev_is_dma_coherent(dev) && (attrs & DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT))
> +		return -EOPNOTSUPP;
> +
> +	if (WARN_ON_ONCE(!dev->dma_mask))
> +		return 0;

(in __dma_map_sg_attrs)

In dma_map_phys the coherency check is placed *after* the dma_mask
WARN_ON_ONCE, but here it is placed *before* it.  Neither ordering is
wrong, but a non-coherent device with no dma_mask returns -EOPNOTSUPP
via this path while the phys path would return DMA_MAPPING_ERROR from
the WARN path.  A comment on the ordering choice would help future
readers.

More importantly: dma_map_sgtable() kdoc lists four documented error
codes (-EINVAL, -ENOMEM, -EIO, -EREMOTEIO).  The new early return
adds -EOPNOTSUPP to the set that can reach callers via dma_map_sgtable,
but the kdoc is not updated.  Could you add -EOPNOTSUPP there so that
callers know they may see it on a non-coherent system?

> +It must never be used in an in-kernel driver that only works with
> +kernal memory.
                  ^^^^^^

Tyo: "kernal" -> "kernel".

--- [PATCH v3 5/8] dma-direct: prevent SWIOTLB path ---

> -		if (is_swiotlb_active(dev))
> +		if (is_swiotlb_active(dev) &&
> +		    !(attrs & DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT))
>  			return swiotlb_map(dev, phys, size, dir, attrs);
>
>  		goto err_overflow;

Verified the full dma_direct_map_phys body: when DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT
is set and SWIOTLB would be needed, the code falls through to
err_overflow and returns DMA_MAPPING_ERROR.  Correct.

The symmetric change to dma_direct_unmap_phys (early return skipping
both dma_direct_sync_single_for_cpu and swiotlb_tbl_unmap_single) is
also correct: a successful map with this attribute guarantees no SWIOTLB
bounce was used and the device is coherent, so neither sync nor
swiotlb_tbl_unmap_single has work to do.

--- [PATCH v3 6/8] iommu/dma: add support for DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT ---

> +	if (WARN_ON_ONCE((state->__size & DMA_IOVA_USE_SWIOTLB) &&
> +			 (attrs & DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT)))
> +		return -EOPNOTSUPP;
> +
> +	if (!dev_is_dma_coherent(dev) && (attrs & DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT))
> +		return -EOPNOTSUPP;

The DMA_IOVA_USE_SWIOTLB check is a good defensive assertion: if a
previous dma_iova_link call already took the SWIOTLB path, subsequent
calls with REQUIRE_COHERENT should never reach this function (the map-
level coherency check should have prevented it).  Making it a WARN_ON
that then returns -EOPNOTSUPP rather than continuing is the right call.

--- [PATCH v3 7/8] RDMA/umem: Tell DMA mapping that UMEM requires coherency ---

> -	if (dirty)
>  		ib_dma_unmap_sgtable_attrs(dev, &umem->sgt_append.sgt,
> -					   DMA_BIDIRECTIONAL, 0);
> +					   DMA_BIDIRECTIONAL,
> +					   DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT);

The map path uses 'dma_attr', which may also have DMA_ATTR_WEAK_ORDERING
ORed in (when IB_ACCESS_RELAXED_ORDERING is set).  The unmap path
hardcodes only DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT, so DMA_ATTR_WEAK_ORDERING is
absent at unmap time.  Tracing through dma_unmap_sg_attrs ->
dma_direct_unmap_sg: on a coherent device the sync helpers are no-ops
and DMA_ATTR_WEAK_ORDERING has no effect at unmap time, so this
asymmetry is harmless today.  That said, should the umem struct store
the dma_attr used at map time and replay it at unmap, rather than
hardcoding a subset?  Not a bug, but worth a note.

--- [PATCH v3 8/8] mm/hmm: Indicate that HMM requires DMA coherency ---

> -	unsigned long attrs = 0;
> +	unsigned long attrs = DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT;

(in both hmm_dma_map_pfn and hmm_dma_unmap_pfn)

In hmm_dma_map_pfn the PCI_P2PDMA_MAP_THRU_HOST_BRIDGE case ORs in
DMA_ATTR_MMIO, giving attrs = DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT | DMA_ATTR_MMIO.
On a non-coherent device the early check in dma_map_phys would return
DMA_MAPPING_ERROR.  However, hmm_dma_alloc() already gates entry on
'if (dma_need_sync || dma_addressing_limited(dev)) return -EOPNOTSUPP',
so hmm_dma_map_pfn is only reachable for coherent devices in practice.
For a coherent device with both attrs set, dma_direct_map_phys falls
into the DMA_ATTR_MMIO branch correctly and DMA_ATTR_REQUIRE_COHERENT
only takes effect in the SWIOTLB guard in the else branch, which is not
reached.  No regression here, but it may be worth a comment in
hmm_dma_map_pfn explaining why REQUIRE_COHERENT and MMIO can coexist.

Thanks,

Needs Discussion mm: vmscan: add PID and cgroup ID to vmscan tracepoints 🔗 Thomas Ballasi 3p
This series adds PID, IRQ context, and memcg ID fields to key vmscan tracepoints, and introduces __event_in_irq() helpers that read the existing trace entry header flags. The tracing infrastructure changes look correct, but reordering existing TP_STRUCT__entry fields in patch 2/3 breaks the binary tracepoint ABI, and a cosmetic trailing-space issue exists in the TP_printk format strings.
include shrinker vmscan
Thomas Ballasi <tballasi@linux.microsoft.com>

mm: vmscan: add PID and cgroup ID to vmscan tracepoints

--- [PATCH v8 1/3] tracing: Add __event_in_*irq() helpers ---

Verified: TRACE_FLAG_HARDIRQ=0x08, TRACE_FLAG_SOFTIRQ=0x10 in
enum trace_flag_type (include/linux/trace_events.h). The hardcoded
values in stage7_class_define.h (0x8, 0x10, 0x18) match exactly,
and the comment explaining why the enum names are not used is
helpful. Patch 1 looks good.

> +#define __event_in_hardirq()    (__entry->ent.flags & TRACE_FLAG_HARDIRQ)
> +#define __event_in_softirq()    (__entry->ent.flags & TRACE_FLAG_SOFTIRQ)
> +#define __event_in_irq()        (__entry->ent.flags & (TRACE_FLAG_HARDIRQ | TRACE_FLAG_SOFTIRQ))

Access to __entry->ent.flags is valid in TP_printk context: every
trace event struct embeds struct trace_entry ent as its first member
and __entry is a typed pointer to that struct. __entry->ent.pid in
patch 3 follows the same logic.

--- [PATCH v8 2/3] mm: vmscan: add cgroup IDs to vmscan tracepoints ---

Verified: mem_cgroup_id() handles NULL safely. In the CONFIG_MEMCG=y
path it returns cgroup_id(memcg->css.cgroup) only after the NULL
check; in the CONFIG_MEMCG=n stub it returns 0 unconditionally. Call
sites passing integer 0 for the memcg argument (try_to_free_pages,
node_reclaim) are safe.

However, there is a binary ABI concern. The TP_STRUCT__entry layout
for mm_vmscan_direct_reclaim_begin_template is reordered:

> -	__field(	int,	order		)
> -	__field(	unsigned long,	gfp_flags	)
> +	__field(	unsigned long,	gfp_flags	)
> +	__field(	u64,	memcg_id	)
> +	__field(	int,	order		)

This swaps order and gfp_flags in the binary ring buffer record,
breaking any userspace tool or BPF program that accesses these fields
by compiled-in offset rather than by reading the format file at
runtime.

The same concern applies to mm_shrink_slab_start, where nid moves
from position 3 to position 9 in the struct:

> -	__field(struct shrinker *, shr)
> -	__field(void *, shrink)
> -	__field(int, nid)
> -	__field(long, nr_objects_to_shrink)
> +	__field(struct shrinker *, shr)
> +	__field(void *, shrink)
> +	__field(long, nr_objects_to_shrink)
> +	...
> +	__field(int, nid)
> +	__field(u64, memcg_id)

The existing code in this same file already documents this concern:

    /* classzone is previous name of the highest_zoneidx.
     * Reason not to change it is the ABI requirement of
     * the tracepoint. */

Could the new memcg_id fields simply be appended to the end of
TP_STRUCT__entry instead of being interleaved with existing fields?
Appending preserves the binary layout of all existing fields and
avoids breaking tools that have compiled-in offsets.

--- [PATCH v8 3/3] mm: vmscan: add PIDs to vmscan tracepoints ---

> +	TP_printk("order=%d gfp_flags=%s pid=%d memcg_id=%llu %s",
> +		__entry->order,
> +		show_gfp_flags(__entry->gfp_flags),
> +		__entry->ent.pid,
> +		__entry->memcg_id,
> +		__event_in_irq() ? "(in-irq)" : "")

When the event fires in task context, __event_in_irq() is false and
the last argument is "". The format string still has a space before
%s, so every non-IRQ trace line ends with a trailing space. The same
pattern appears in all four modified TP_printk calls
(direct_reclaim_begin, direct_reclaim_end, mm_shrink_slab_start,
mm_shrink_slab_end). A format like "%s%s" where the first string
is either " (in-irq)" or "" (empty, no leading space) is one way
to avoid the trailing space in the common case.

Needs Work mm/damon: let DAMON be paused and resumed 🔗 SeongJae Park 10p
This series adds a 'pause' field to damon_ctx that causes kdamond_fn() to spin in a sleep-and-damon_call() loop instead of doing monitoring and DAMOS work, preserving DAMON internal state across deliberate pauses; sysfs and selftests are updated accordingly.
damon/core damon/sysfs damon/tests/core-kunit docs include tests
SeongJae Park <sj@kernel.org>

mm/damon: let DAMON be paused and resumed

Thanks for the series.  The overall approach is clean.  Two issues
were found during review.

--- [RFC PATCH 01/10] mm/damon/core: introduce damon_ctx->paused ---

> diff --git a/include/linux/damon.h b/include/linux/damon.h
> --- a/include/linux/damon.h
> +++ b/include/linux/damon.h
> @@ -811,6 +811,8 @@ struct damon_ctx {
>   	 * intervals tuning
>   	 */
>  	unsigned long next_intervals_tune_sis;
> +	/* pause kdamond main loop */
> +	bool pause;
>  	/* for waiting until the execution of the kdamond_fn is started */
>  	struct completion kdamond_started;

This places 'pause' in the '/* private: internal use only */' section
of damon_ctx, between next_intervals_tune_sis and kdamond_started.
But 'pause' is a user-configurable API parameter: callers set it via
damon_commit_ctx() the same way they set ops, addr_unit, and
min_region_sz -- all of which live in the '/* public: */' section.
Should 'pause' be moved to the public section?  The struct kdoc (the
@field list above damon_ctx) also does not document 'pause'.

> diff --git a/mm/damon/core.c b/mm/damon/core.c
> --- a/mm/damon/core.c
> +++ b/mm/damon/core.c
> @@ -2978,6 +2979,13 @@ static int kdamond_fn(void *data)
>  		kdamond_call(ctx, false);
> +		while (ctx->pause) {
> +			if (kdamond_need_stop(ctx))
> +				goto done;
> +			kdamond_usleep(ctx->attrs.sample_interval);
> +			/* allow caller unset pause via damon_call() */
> +			kdamond_call(ctx, false);
> +		}

The pause loop does not call damos_walk_cancel().  Compare with
kdamond_wait_activation(), which calls damos_walk_cancel(ctx) on
every iteration while waiting for watermarks to be satisfied.

If a caller registers a damos_walk() request at the same time 'pause'
is committed -- the walk control is installed but
kdamond_apply_schemes() will not run until the context is resumed --
that caller blocks indefinitely on wait_for_completion().  It is only
unblocked when DAMON is stopped (damos_walk_cancel() at the 'done:'
label) or when 'pause' is cleared.  With a long or permanent pause
this is a deadlock from the walk caller's perspective.

Could a damos_walk_cancel(ctx) call be added inside the pause while
loop, matching the pattern in kdamond_wait_activation()?

The rest of the series looks correct.  Specifically verified:
- damon_new_ctx() uses kzalloc_obj, so pause is zero-initialised to
  false with no separate default needed.
- damon_sysfs_commit_input() runs as a damon_call() callback on the
  kdamond thread, so ctx->pause is written only by the same thread
  that reads it in the while loop; no additional barrier is needed.
- kstrtobool() accepts 'T'/'F' as the first character, so write_file()
  passing Python str(True)=="True" / str(False)=="False" works.
- The pause-before-dump logic in assert_ctxs_committed() correctly
  handles the already-paused case (paused_for_dump stays False) and
  restores ctx.pause for the caller in both branches.

Looks Good Docs/mm/damon: document exclusivity of special-purpose modules 🔗 SeongJae Park 1p
Documentation-only patch adding a cross-referenced note to design.rst and the three DAMON special-purpose module docs (lru_sort, reclaim, stat) explaining that these modules run exclusively and return -EBUSY if another is already active.

Docs/mm: document the OOM killer

Thanks for filling in this stub.  I cross-checked the descriptions
against mm/oom_kill.c.  Two inaccuracies to fix:

> +The reaper gives the victim a short window to exit naturally before

> +``unmap_page_range()`` to release physical pages.

`unmap_page_range()` does not exist in mm/oom_kill.c or mm/memory.c.
The function actually invoked by __oom_reap_task_mm() is
`zap_vma_for_reaping()`, which zaps page table entries per-VMA
without blocking.  Please correct the function name.

> +The ``totalpages`` baseline depends on the allocation constraint:
> +
> +- **Unconstrained**: all RAM plus swap.
> +- **Cpuset**: memory on nodes in the current cpuset.
> +- **Memory policy**: memory on nodes in the current mempolicy.

For CONSTRAINT_CPUSET and CONSTRAINT_MEMORY_POLICY, constrained_alloc()
initialises oc->totalpages to total_swap_pages first, then adds
node_present_pages() for each node in the relevant mask.  Swap is
included in those two cases as well.  The bullets should read something
like:

Kit Dallege <xaum.io@gmail.com>

Docs/mm: document Page Allocation

Good start at filling in this stub.  I spotted two factual issues
while cross-referencing against the source.

> +When a per-CPU list is empty, a batch of pages is taken from the buddy.
> +When it exceeds its high watermark, excess pages are returned.
> +``lru_add_drain()`` and ``drain_all_pages()`` flush per-CPU lists when
> +the system needs an accurate count of free pages, such as during memory
> +hot-remove.

lru_add_drain() drains the LRU addition batches (cpu_fbatches in
mm/swap.c), not the PCP page lists.  The function that drains PCP
lists is drain_all_pages() (and its single-CPU variant
drain_local_pages()).  lru_add_drain() should be removed from this
sentence or given its own separate, accurate description.

> +Each pageblock (typically 2MB on x86) carries a migratetype tag that
> +describes the kind of allocations it serves:
> +
> +- **MIGRATE_UNMOVABLE**: kernel allocations that cannot be relocated
> +  (slab objects, page tables).
> +- **MIGRATE_MOVABLE**: user pages and other content that can be migrated
> +  or reclaimed (used by compaction and memory hot-remove).
> +- **MIGRATE_RECLAIMABLE**: caches that can be dropped under pressure
> +  (page cache, dentries).
> +- **MIGRATE_CMA**: reserved for the contiguous memory allocator;

MIGRATE_HIGHATOMIC (== MIGRATE_PCPTYPES in include/linux/mmzone.h) is
missing from the list.  It sits between MIGRATE_RECLAIMABLE and
MIGRATE_CMA and is used for high-order atomic reserves; it cannot be
requested directly via GFP flags but is part of the migratetype
taxonomy and worth mentioning for completeness.

Author: Kit Dallege <xaum.io@gmail.com>

Docs/mm: document Boot Memory

I checked the main claims against mm/memblock.c and
include/linux/memblock.h.

> +Memblock tracks physical memory as two arrays of regions: ``memory`` (all
> +usable RAM reported by firmware) and ``reserved`` (memory already allocated
> +or otherwise unavailable).  A free page is one that appears in ``memory``
> +but not in ``reserved``.

Correct.  The struct memblock definition in memblock.h confirms both
arrays and the semantics match for_each_free_mem_range().

> +- **NOMAP**: memory that should not be directly mapped by the kernel
> +  (e.g., firmware-reserved ranges that are usable but not mappable).

The kernel header describes MEMBLOCK_NOMAP as "don't add to kernel
direct mapping and treat as reserved in the memory map".  NOMAP regions
are not usable as RAM; the parenthetical "usable but not mappable"
overstates it.  Could this be rephrased closer to "memory excluded from
the kernel direct map and treated as reserved in the memory map"?

> +- ``for_each_mem_range()`` iterates over free ranges (memory minus
> +  reserved).

This is incorrect.  The actual definition in memblock.h is:

  #define for_each_mem_range(i, p_start, p_end) \
      __for_each_mem_range(i, &memblock.memory, NULL, NUMA_NO_NODE, \
                           MEMBLOCK_HOTPLUG | MEMBLOCK_DRIVER_MANAGED, \
                           p_start, p_end, NULL)

The type_b argument is NULL, so reserved regions are never subtracted.
for_each_mem_range() walks the memory array while skipping NOMAP (and
HOTPLUG under movable_node), nothing more.

The macro that subtracts reserved is for_each_free_mem_range(), which
passes &memblock.reserved as type_b.

> +These iterators handle the subtraction of reserved regions from memory
> +regions internally, presenting the caller with a simple sequence of
> +available ranges.

This paragraph reinforces the error above.  Subtraction of reserved
only happens in for_each_free_mem_range() and its reverse variant, not
in for_each_mem_range().

Could the iterator list be corrected to something like:

  - for_each_mem_range() walks the memory array, skipping NOMAP and
    (with movable_node) HOTPLUG regions; it does not subtract reserved.
  - for_each_free_mem_range() iterates truly free ranges (memory minus
    reserved).
  - for_each_reserved_mem_region() iterates reserved regions directly.
  - for_each_mem_pfn_range() iterates by page frame number.

[ ... ]

> +memblock arrays themselves are returned to the page allocator via
> +``memblock_discard()``

Small note: memblock_discard() only frees arrays that were dynamically
resized past their static initial buffers; if no resize occurred it is a
no-op.  Worth a brief qualifier so readers do not assume the static
buffers are always reclaimed.

No other regressions found.  The memblock_add()/memblock_reserve()
descriptions, the top-down/bottom-up allocation direction, the
memblock_free_all() transition, and the named-reservation and
zone-topology sections all look accurate against the source.

Author: Kit Dallege <xaum.io@gmail.com>

Docs/mm: document Virtually Contiguous Memory Allocation

Cross-referenced against mm/vmalloc.c and include/linux/vmalloc.h.
Two factual inaccuracies found below.

> +Guard Pages
> +-----------
> +
> +By default, each vmalloc area is surrounded by a guard page — an unmapped
> +page that causes an immediate fault if code overruns the allocation.  This
> +costs one page of virtual address space (not physical memory) per
> +allocation.

The word "surrounded" implies guard pages on both sides of the
allocation.  Looking at __get_vm_area_node() in mm/vmalloc.c:

    if (!(flags & VM_NO_GUARD))
        size += PAGE_SIZE;

Only one PAGE_SIZE is added to the virtual range, which means there
is a single trailing guard page (after the allocation), not pages on
both sides.  "surrounded" should be "followed by a guard page" or
"has a trailing guard page".

> +Freeing
> +=======
> +
> +``vfree()`` can be called from any context, including interrupt handlers.

This is not quite right.  vfree() explicitly forbids NMI context:

    BUG_ON(in_nmi());

And vfree_atomic(), which vfree() delegates to when in_interrupt(),
carries the same restriction:

    BUG_ON(in_nmi());

The kernel-doc comment for vfree_atomic() already states "except
NMIs".  This sentence should say something like "vfree() can be
called from any context except NMI, including hard interrupt
handlers."

Everything else checked out:
- vmap_area two-tree description (free_vmap_area_root augmented with
  subtree_max_size, vmap_area_root for busy areas) matches the data
  structure definitions.
- vm_struct fields (addr, size, flags, pages array, caller) match
  include/linux/vmalloc.h.
- vmalloc_huge() wrapper exists in include/linux/vmalloc.h.
- arch_vmap_pmd_supported() / arch_vmap_pud_supported() callbacks
  exist and are used in the huge-page mapping path.
- vm_map_ram / vm_unmap_ram descriptions match their implementations.

Docs/mm: document Page Reclaim

Pure documentation patch; no code changes. Verified the key factual
claims against mm/vmscan.c, mm/swap.c, mm/shrinker.c, and
include/linux/mmzone.h.

> +Reclaim Priority
> +================
> +
> +The reclaim path operates at decreasing priority levels (from
> +``DEF_PRIORITY`` down to 0).  At each level, a larger fraction of the
> +LRU lists is scanned.  At the default priority, only 1/4096th of
> +pages are considered; at priority 0, the entire list is scanned.

DEF_PRIORITY is 12 (include/linux/mmzone.h) and scan_control carries
the comment "Scan (total_size >> priority) pages at once", so 2^12 =
4096 -- the 1/4096th claim is correct.

> +- **kswapd**: a per-node kernel thread that runs in the background
> +  when free pages in any zone drop below the low watermark.  It
> +  reclaims until free pages reach the high watermark, then sleeps.

Verified: the slow-path allocator calls wake_all_kswapds() when
ALLOC_WMARK_LOW fails, and kswapd sleeps in kswapd_try_to_sleep()
only when pgdat_balanced() returns true, which checks
high_wmark_pages() -- both halves of this sentence are correct.

> +Each reclaim invocation is parameterized by a ``struct scan_control``
> +that captures the allocation context: which GFP flags were used, how
> +many pages are needed, which node or memory cgroup to reclaim from,
> +and whether writeback or swap are allowed.

Cross-checked against struct scan_control (mm/vmscan.c): gfp_mask,
nr_to_reclaim, nodemask/target_mem_cgroup, may_writepage, may_swap --
all present and match the description.

> +Besides page cache and anonymous pages, kernel caches (dentries,
> +inodes, and driver-specific caches) are reclaimed through the
> +shrinker interface (``mm/shrinker.c``).  A shrinker registers two
> +callbacks:
> +
> +- ``count_objects()``: report how many objects are reclaimable.
> +- ``scan_objects()``: free up to a requested number of objects.

mm/shrinker.c exists; struct shrinker in include/linux/shrinker.h
declares exactly these two function pointers. Correct.

> +``try_to_free_mem_cgroup_pages()`` is the entry point for
> +cgroup-scoped reclaim.

Confirmed in mm/vmscan.c.

No regressions found. Locking, error paths, and refcounts are not
applicable to a documentation-only patch.

Docs/mm: document Swap

Thanks for filling in this stub.  The overall structure is good and the
high-level descriptions are accurate.  One factual error found:

> diff --git a/Documentation/mm/swap.rst b/Documentation/mm/swap.rst

[ ... ]

> +Swap space is allocated in clusters (groups of contiguous slots, typically
> +32 pages).  Each cluster tracks which slots are free and whether it has

The cluster size is not 32 pages.  mm/swap.h defines:

    #ifdef CONFIG_THP_SWAP
    #define SWAPFILE_CLUSTER    HPAGE_PMD_NR   /* 512 on x86-64 */
    #else
    #define SWAPFILE_CLUSTER    256
    #endif

So the cluster size is 256 or 512 pages depending on CONFIG_THP_SWAP,
never 32.  Please correct this to reflect the actual values.

[ ... ]

> +``mm/page_io.c`` maintains a bitmap (``swap_zeromap``) tracking swap slots
> +that contained zero-filled

Minor nit: the bitmap is the zeromap field inside struct swap_info_struct
(include/linux/swap.h).  The functions that read and write it live in
mm/page_io.c, but it is not a standalone object defined there.  Consider
wording it as: "Each swap device tracks zero-filled slots in a bitmap
(the zeromap field of swap_info_struct); mm/page_io.c sets and clears
entries as pages are written out and read back."

Needs Work Docs/mm: document Shared Memory Filesystem 🔗 Kit Dallege 1p
Documentation-only patch filling in the shmfs.rst stub with an overview of tmpfs/shmem internals including page cache integration, swap, huge pages, accounting, and fallocate. Several technical claims do not match the actual kernel implementation.
docs
On Mon, Mar 17 2026, Kit Dallege wrote:

> Fill in the shmfs.rst stub created in commit 481cc97349d6
> ("mm,doc: Add new documentation structure") as part of
> the structured memory management documentation following
> Mel Gorman's book outline.

Thank you for filling out this stub.  A few technical details do not
match the implementation in mm/shmem.c and should be corrected before
merge.

> diff --git a/Documentation/mm/shmfs.rst b/Documentation/mm/shmfs.rst

[ ... ]

> +- ``never``: only base pages (default).
> +- ``always``: attempt huge page allocation for every new page.
> +- ``within_size``: use huge pages only within the file's current size.
> +- ``advise``: use huge pages only for mappings with ``MADV_HUGEPAGE``.

Two issues here.

First, the default is not unconditionally "never".  mm/shmem.c selects
TMPFS_HUGE_DEFAULT based on CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE_TMPFS_HUGE_*.
The fallback when no config option selects a value is SHMEM_HUGE_NEVER,
but this varies by build configuration.  Please qualify: "never (unless
overridden by kernel configuration)" or similar.

Second, the within_size description is incomplete.  The code comment
for SHMEM_HUGE_WITHIN_SIZE in mm/shmem.c says:

  "only allocate huge pages if the page will be fully within i_size,
   also respect madvise() hints;"

The implementation in shmem_allowable_huge_orders() confirms this:
huge_shmem_orders_madvise is OR'd into the result mask when VM_HUGEPAGE
is set, even under the within_size policy.  The description should note
that within_size also honours MADV_HUGEPAGE/MADV_NOHUGEPAGE hints.

[ ... ]

> +When a huge page is allocated but only partially used (e.g., a file is
> +smaller than a huge page), memory is wasted.  To mitigate this, tmpfs
> +registers a shrinker that identifies huge pages where the file has been
> +truncated or punched below the huge page boundary, and splits them back
> +into base pages so the unused portion can be reclaimed.

This is inaccurate.  There is no shmem-specific shrinker in mm/shmem.c.
Grepping for "shrinker" and "split_huge_page" in mm/shmem.c returns no
matches.  The mechanism that reclaims partially-used huge pages is the
generic deferred split shrinker (deferred_split_shrinker) registered in
mm/huge_memory.c, which is not shmem-specific.

Please correct this to describe the actual mechanism -- the THP
deferred split infrastructure -- or remove the paragraph if the detail
cannot be verified accurately.

[ ... ]

> +tmpfs supports ``fallocate()`` to preallocate space for a file.
> +Preallocated pages are allocated and inserted into the page cache
> +immediately, guaranteeing that subsequent writes will not fail with
> +``ENOSPC``.
> +
> +``FALLOC_FL_PUNCH_HOLE`` is also supported: it removes pages from a range
> +of the file and returns them to the filesystem's free pool.

shmem_fallocate() also accepts FALLOC_FL_KEEP_SIZE (the mode validation
is `mode & ~(FALLOC_FL_KEEP_SIZE | FALLOC_FL_PUNCH_HOLE)`).  It is
worth mentioning that preallocating with FALLOC_FL_KEEP_SIZE is
supported and does not extend i_size, which is used by memfd consumers
that want to guarantee space without changing the visible file size.

rust_binder: use AssertSync for BINDER_VM_OPS

2026-03-13 (9)

Needs Discussion lift lookup out of exclive lock for dir ops 🔗 NeilBrown 50p
This RFC series lifts dcache name lookup out of the exclusive directory lock by extending d_alloc_parallel() to be usable without a caller-provided wait queue, making d_splice_alias() handle hashed dentries, and introducing d_alloc_noblock() for readdir cache-priming. The approach is architecturally sound but several critical implementation details in the truncated diff need verification before this can land.
docs fs include shmem
From: NeilBrown <neil@brown.name>
Subject: [PATCH RFC 00/53] lift lookup out of exclusive lock for dir ops

Series-level note: I read patches 01-05 against the kernel tree at
mm-new.  Comments below are ordered by patch.

---

[PATCH 02/53] VFS: enhance d_splice_alias() to handle in-lookup dentries

> -	BUG_ON(!d_unhashed(dentry));
> -
>  	if (!inode)
>  		goto out;

The BUG_ON served two purposes: (1) prevent the re-hash double-insert
bug that would occur if an already-hashed dentry fell through to
__d_rehash(), and (2) catch callers that accidentally passed a
positive (already-instantiated) dentry.  Purpose (1) is now handled
correctly by the conditional __d_rehash() below, so that removal is
fine.  But purpose (2) is lost.  If a positive hashed dentry is
passed, __d_instantiate() is now reached with a non-empty d_u.d_alias,
and hlist_add_head() corrupts the inode alias list silently.  The
doc comment says "@dentry must be negative", but should there be a
WARN_ON(d_inode(dentry)) here to preserve the diagnostic?

> +	if (unlikely(d_in_lookup(dentry))) {
>  		dir = dentry->d_parent->d_inode;
>  		n = start_dir_add(dir);
>  		d_wait = __d_lookup_unhash(dentry);
> +		__d_rehash(dentry);
> +	} else if (d_unhashed(dentry)) {
> +		__d_rehash(dentry);
>  	}
>  	if (unlikely(ops))
>  		d_set_d_op(dentry, ops);
> -	if (inode) {
> -		unsigned add_flags = d_flags_for_inode(inode);
> -		hlist_add_head(&dentry->d_u.d_alias, &inode->i_dentry);
> -		raw_write_seqcount_begin(&dentry->d_seq);
> -		__d_set_inode_and_type(dentry, inode, add_flags);
> -		raw_write_seqcount_end(&dentry->d_seq);
> -		fsnotify_update_flags(dentry);
> -	}
> -	__d_rehash(dentry);
> +	if (inode)
> +		__d_instantiate(dentry, inode);

The conditional __d_rehash() is correct: already-hashed dentries must
not be rehashed (that would insert them twice in the bucket list).

The switch to __d_instantiate() picks up the this_cpu_dec(nr_dentry_
negative) decrement that was previously absent from the __d_add() path.
For d_add() callers this is benign because freshly allocated dentries
have DCACHE_LRU_LIST clear, so the decrement is skipped.  For the new
hashed-dentry path through d_splice_alias_ops(), the dentry may be on
the LRU, and the decrement is now correctly applied.  Verified this
matches the accounting in d_lru_add() / d_lru_del().

__d_instantiate() has WARN_ON(d_in_lookup(dentry)).  For the d_in_lookup
branch above, __d_lookup_unhash() clears DCACHE_PAR_LOOKUP before
__d_instantiate() is reached, so the WARN_ON is safe.

[ ... ]

---

[PATCH 04/53] VFS: use global wait-queue table for d_alloc_parallel()

> +#define PAR_LOOKUP_WQ_BITS	8
> +#define PAR_LOOKUP_WQS (1 << PAR_LOOKUP_WQ_BITS)
> +static wait_queue_head_t par_wait_table[PAR_LOOKUP_WQS] __cacheline_aligned;

> +static int d_wait_wake_fn(struct wait_queue_entry *wq_entry,
> +			  unsigned mode, int sync, void *key)
> +{
> +	struct par_wait_key *pwk = container_of(wq_entry,
> +						 struct par_wait_key, wqe);
> +	if (pwk->de == key)
> +		return default_wake_function(wq_entry, mode, sync, key);
> +	return 0;
> +}

This is the right approach: waiters filter on dentry pointer so
unrelated in-lookup dentries that land in the same global bucket do
not cause spurious wakeups.

> +static inline void d_wake_waiters(struct wait_queue_head *d_wait,
> +				  struct dentry *dentry)
> +{
> +	if (d_wait)
> +		__wake_up(d_wait, TASK_NORMAL, 0, dentry);
> +}

The NULL-guard optimises the common (uncontended) case.  Correct.

Now, __d_lookup_unhash_wake() in the current tree does:

    wake_up_all(__d_lookup_unhash(dentry));

wake_up_all() passes key=NULL to each wake function.  After this
patch, d_wait_wake_fn() tests "pwk->de == key", i.e. "pwk->de ==
NULL", which is false for every real waiter.  If __d_lookup_unhash_wake
is not changed to call d_wake_waiters(wq, dentry), no waiter will ever
be woken through that path.  The diff header lists fs/dcache.c as
modified and the description says the function is updated, but the
shown hunk is truncated.  Can you confirm __d_lookup_unhash_wake() is
changed to d_wake_waiters(wq, dentry)?

> +		if (!dentry->d_wait)

The d_wait_lookup hunk is truncated here.  The key question is: does
the assignment of dentry->d_wait happen under dentry->d_lock?
Both the assignment path (d_wait_lookup, called while d_lock is held)
and the read path (__d_lookup_unhash, called while d_lock is held from
__d_add or __d_lookup_unhash_wake) must be serialised by the same lock.
If d_wait_lookup sets d_wait only under d_lock, and __d_lookup_unhash
reads it only under d_lock, the ordering is correct and no hbl_lock is
required for d_wait itself.  Please confirm this is the case.

> -	new->d_wait = wq;
>  	hlist_bl_add_head(&new->d_u.d_in_lookup_hash, b);
>  	hlist_bl_unlock(b);

(Reconstructed from context; this hunk is also truncated.)

In __d_alloc(), INIT_LIST_HEAD(&dentry->d_lru) sets d_lru.next to
&dentry->d_lru (self-referential, non-NULL).  Since d_wait and d_lru
share a union, d_wait starts out non-NULL with the self-referential
list-head address.  d_wake_waiters() checks "if (d_wait)" -- so if the
new code does not explicitly write new->d_wait = NULL before inserting
the dentry into the in-lookup hash, every uncontended completion will
call __wake_up() with a garbage wait_queue_head pointer and crash.  The
old code wrote "new->d_wait = wq" unconditionally here; the replacement
must write "new->d_wait = NULL".  Is that done in the full diff?

> -static inline void end_dir_add(struct inode *dir, unsigned int n,
> -			       wait_queue_head_t *d_wait)
> +static inline void end_dir_add(struct inode *dir, unsigned int n,
> +			       wait_queue_head_t *d_wait, struct dentry *de)

__d_move() also calls end_dir_add(dir, n, d_wait) (at line 2955 in the
current tree) when target is d_in_lookup().  After this signature
change, __d_move() must pass target (the dentry that waiters registered
their par_wait_key.de against) as the de argument.  If it passes
dentry (the source), d_wait_wake_fn() will compare pwk->de == dentry
instead of pwk->de == target and no waiter will be woken.  The full
diff for __d_move() is not shown -- please verify the correct dentry
is passed there.

[ ... ]

[PATCH 05/53] VFS: introduce d_alloc_noblock()

> +		case ALLOC_PARA_FAIL:
> +			spin_unlock(&dentry->d_lock);
> +			dput(new);
> +			dput(dentry);
> +			return ERR_PTR(-EWOULDBLOCK);

Verified the cleanup path: rcu_read_unlock() is called before
spin_lock(&dentry->d_lock), so the RCU section is properly closed
before the early return.  new was inserted into parent->d_children
(d_sib) but never into the in-lookup hash, so dput(new) reaches
__dentry_kill() which calls __d_drop() (skipped, d_unhashed() is true),
then dentry_unlist() to remove from d_sib.  No leak, no list corruption.

The enum alloc_para / __d_alloc_parallel refactoring is clean.

d_lock serialises the lazy d_wait assignment (waiter side) against the
d_wait read-and-clear (__d_lookup_unhash, waker side).  The three open
questions above all concern truncated hunks and should be straightforward
to verify in the full series: (1) __d_lookup_unhash_wake must use
d_wake_waiters(); (2) new->d_wait must be explicitly NULL-initialised

Looks Good mm: filemap: fix nr_pages calculation overflow in filemap_map_pages() 🔗 Baolin Wang 1p
The patch fixes an unsigned integer underflow in filemap_map_pages() where a concurrent file truncation could shrink end_pgoff below xas.xa_index after a folio was already retrieved, causing nr_pages to wrap to a huge value and filemap_map_folio_range() to map far beyond the folio boundary. The fix moves the i_size read and end_pgoff clamping before next_uptodate_folio(), guaranteeing xas.xa_index <= end_pgoff at the point of the nr_pages calculation.
filemap
Author: Baolin Wang <baolin.wang@linux.alibaba.com>

mm: filemap: fix nr_pages calculation overflow in filemap_map_pages()

The race and fix are correctly identified. Here is what I verified.

> diff --git a/mm/filemap.c b/mm/filemap.c
> --- a/mm/filemap.c
> +++ b/mm/filemap.c
> @@ -3879,14 +3879,14 @@ vm_fault_t filemap_map_pages(struct vm_fault *vmf,
>  	unsigned int nr_pages = 0, folio_type;
>  	unsigned short mmap_miss = 0, mmap_miss_saved;
>  
> +	file_end = DIV_ROUND_UP(i_size_read(mapping->host), PAGE_SIZE) - 1;
> +	end_pgoff = min(end_pgoff, file_end);
> +
>  	rcu_read_lock();
>  	folio = next_uptodate_folio(&xas, mapping, end_pgoff);
>  	if (!folio)
>  		goto out;
>  
> -	file_end = DIV_ROUND_UP(i_size_read(mapping->host), PAGE_SIZE) - 1;
> -	end_pgoff = min(end_pgoff, file_end);

The underflow is here in the loop body:

    nr_pages = min(end, end_pgoff) - xas.xa_index + 1;

All three operands are unsigned (pgoff_t / unsigned long), so when
xas.xa_index > end_pgoff the subtraction wraps to a huge value.
filemap_map_folio_range() then iterates that many pages, walking far
beyond the folio and corrupting _mapcount on unrelated pages - matching
the reported "Bad page state" and the VM_WARN_ON_FOLIO in
folio_add_file_rmap_ptes() that fires when page + nr_pages - 1 falls
outside the folio.

The fix establishes the invariant xas.xa_index <= end_pgoff before the
loop. next_uptodate_folio() advances xas via xas_next_entry(xas,
end_pgoff), which caps the returned xa_index at end_pgoff, so a
successful return always satisfies xas.xa_index <= end_pgoff. By
clamping end_pgoff first, that cap is tight enough to prevent the
underflow.

I also read next_uptodate_folio() and confirmed it has its own internal
i_size re-check (max_idx guard at the xas_next_entry loop): it rejects
any folio whose xa_index >= DIV_ROUND_UP(i_size_read(), PAGE_SIZE). This
is an additional safety net but does not close the original window on its
own, since it and the caller's i_size_read() are separate reads that can
straddle the truncation. The patch eliminates the problematic second
i_size_read() in the caller entirely.

The loop's continuation call

    } while ((folio = next_uptodate_folio(&xas, mapping, end_pgoff))
                                                          ^^^^^^^^

also uses the now-fixed end_pgoff, so all subsequent iterations are
equally protected.

Moving i_size_read() outside rcu_read_lock() is correct: the rcu section
protects the xarray walk, not the inode size, and i_size_read() is safe
on its own (seqlock on 32-bit, atomic on 64-bit).

The file_end value is still consumed correctly by the PMD condition and
as an argument to filemap_map_folio_range(). Both uses tolerate the same
degree of staleness they always could, since file_end was never inside
a critical section with respect to i_size.

Verified: unsigned arithmetic underflow path, xas cap semantics,
next_uptodate_folio internal max_idx guard, loop continuation, file_end
secondary uses. No regressions found.

Reviewed-by: &lt;reviewer&gt;
Needs Discussion elf: align ET_DYN base to exec folio order for contpte mapping 🔗 WANG Rui 1p
The patch adds exec_folio_order()-based alignment to the ET_DYN load-bias calculation in load_elf_binary(), bumping minimum alignment to 64K on arm64 with 4K pages so contiguous-PTE (contpte) mappings can be used for PIE and static-PIE executables. WANG Rui raises a valid question about whether the alignment bump should be gated on the segment already being huge-aligned, to avoid ASLR entropy reduction and unnecessary probe-mmap overhead for binaries that cannot benefit.
WANG Rui <r@hev.cc>

elf: align ET_DYN base to exec folio order for contpte mapping

> +			if (exec_folio_order())
> +				alignment = max(alignment,
> +					(unsigned long)PAGE_SIZE << exec_folio_order());

Your concern about ASLR entropy is well-founded, and I think the
situation is actually worse than just entropy loss: for a binary whose
first PT_LOAD has a p_vaddr that is not huge-aligned (e.g. a typical
4K-aligned binary), forcing load_bias to 64K alignment does not make
the actual mapping huge-aligned.  The real mapping starts at

  load_bias + p_vaddr

and if p_vaddr is 0x1000 while load_bias is masked to 64K, the result
is still only 4K-aligned, so contpte will not engage.  We pay the
ASLR entropy cost for all PIE binaries (4 bits lost on arm64 with 4K
pages) with no benefit for binaries not linked with huge-page
alignment.

Note also that on the static-PIE path (ET_DYN without PT_INTERP) in
load_elf_binary():

[ ... ]

> 			if (alignment > ELF_MIN_ALIGN) {
> 				load_bias = elf_load(bprm->file, 0, elf_ppnt,
> 					     elf_prot, elf_flags, total_size);

With the new alignment (64K) always exceeding ELF_MIN_ALIGN (PAGE_SIZE
= 4K on arm64/4K), this branch is taken for every static-PIE binary,
not just those linked with a large p_align.  Every ld.so or static-PIE
executable now incurs a probe mmap at address 0 followed by
vm_munmap(), with the subsequent remap using MAP_FIXED_NOREPLACE.  For
a binary not linked with 64K alignment, load_bias + p_vaddr is still
not 64K-aligned after masking, so no contpte benefit accrues and the
extra probe overhead is pure waste.

For binaries that ARE linked with 64K-aligned segments -- p_align >=
64K, with p_vaddr and p_offset both 64K-aligned -- maximum_alignment()
already returns 64K, so the existing code in load_elf_binary() already
handles the beneficial case correctly without this addition.

Minor: exec_folio_order() is evaluated twice in the snippet.  Storing
the result in a local avoids the double call.

Your suggested constraint -- only bumping alignment when the segment
vaddr, filesz/memsz, and file offset are all huge-aligned -- is
exactly what is needed to avoid both the ASLR regression and the
spurious probe-mmap regression while still benefiting binaries that
can actually use contpte.
Looks Good pid_namespace: make init creation more flexible 🔗 Pavel Tikhomirov 4p
This series annotates pid_namespace->child_reaper accesses with READ/WRITE_ONCE, hardens the "init must be pid 1" invariant by moving the check to after IDR allocation (still under pidmap_lock), and then exploits that invariant to allow setns(pid_for_children) before the namespace's init process is created.
kernel tests
Pavel Tikhomirov <ptikhomirov@virtuozzo.com>

pid_namespace: make init creation more flexible (v5)

I read the full implementations of alloc_pid(), free_pid(),
copy_process(), find_child_reaper(), pidns_for_children_get(), and
traced the pid_allocated state machine.  Everything checks out.

--- [PATCH v5 1/4] pid_namespace: avoid optimization of accesses to ->child_reaper ---

> diff --git a/kernel/pid.c b/kernel/pid.c
> @@ -128,7 +128,7 @@ void free_pid(struct pid *pid)
>  			 * is the reaper wake up the reaper.  The reaper
>  			 * may be sleeping in zap_pid_ns_processes().
>  			 */
> -			wake_up_process(ns->child_reaper);
> +			wake_up_process(READ_ONCE(ns->child_reaper));

Verified: free_pid holds pidmap_lock (a spinlock), not tasklist_lock.
The WRITE_ONCE sites in copy_process() and find_child_reaper() both
run under write_lock_irq(&tasklist_lock) -- a different lock.
READ_ONCE is the correct pairing to prevent compiler tearing.

A NULL dereference here is impossible: cases 1 and 2 in the switch
are only reachable after disable_pid_allocation() clears the
PIDNS_ADDING bit (called only from zap_pid_ns_processes(), which
runs when init is dying), at which point child_reaper is set.

> @@ -218,7 +218,7 @@ struct pid *alloc_pid(...)
> -			if (tid != 1 && !tmp->child_reaper)
> +			if (tid != 1 && !READ_ONCE(tmp->child_reaper))

This loop runs before idr_preload/spin_lock(&pidmap_lock), so no
lock stabilises child_reaper here.  READ_ONCE is correct.

The ASSERT_EXCLUSIVE_WRITER annotations in fork.c and exit.c are
also correct: both write sites hold write_lock_irq(&tasklist_lock),
so they are mutually exclusive by construction.

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v5 2/4] pid: check init is created first after idr alloc ---

> diff --git a/kernel/pid.c b/kernel/pid.c
> -			if (tid != 1 && !READ_ONCE(tmp->child_reaper))
> -				goto out_abort;
>
> +		/*
> +		 * PID 1 (init) must be created first.
> +		 */
> +		if (!READ_ONCE(tmp->child_reaper) && nr != 1) {
> +			retval = -EINVAL;
> +			goto out_free;
> +		}

The new check runs inside spin_lock(&pidmap_lock), after storing
nr into pid->numbers[i] and decrementing i.  The out_free cleanup
loop starts at ++i (recovering the just-decremented value) and
walks back to ns->level, correctly removing every IDR entry that
was allocated before the check fired.

The cursor reset "if (ns->pid_allocated == PIDNS_ADDING)" fires
correctly here because pid_allocated has not yet been incremented
when we branch to out_free -- the next caller can start from PID 1.

For the non-set_tid path on a fresh namespace: idr_get_cursor is 0,
pid_min is set to 1, so idr_alloc_cyclic returns 1 on the first
call.  nr=1 means the check never triggers.  No regression.

For set_tid with tid != 1 and no init: the IDR entry is allocated
then immediately freed via out_free, returning EINVAL.  The old
code avoided the allocation entirely, but the caller sees the same
error either way.

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH v5 3/4] pid_namespace: allow opening pid_for_children before init was created ---

> diff --git a/kernel/pid_namespace.c b/kernel/pid_namespace.c
> -	if (ns) {
> -		read_lock(&tasklist_lock);
> -		if (!ns->child_reaper) {
> -			put_pid_ns(ns);
> -			ns = NULL;
> -		}
> -		read_unlock(&tasklist_lock);
> -	}

Safe to remove.  The invariant is now enforced inside alloc_pid():
the first PID allocated in any namespace must have nr=1 (checked
post-IDR under pidmap_lock).  idr_alloc serialises the race between
multiple callers trying to become init: only one gets nr=1; all
others receive EEXIST and fail.  A caller that races and observes
child_reaper==NULL with nr>1 gets EINVAL and can retry.

Checked wake_up_process(READ_ONCE(ns->child_reaper)) in free_pid:
values 1 and 2 (with PIDNS_ADDING bit clear) are only reachable
after disable_pid_allocation() runs from zap_pid_ns_processes(),
which only runs when init is exiting -- child_reaper is non-NULL
at that point.  No NULL dereference is possible.

Looks good overall.

Looks Good binfmt_elf: Align eligible read-only PT_LOAD segments to PMD_SIZE for THP 🔗 WANG Rui 1p
The patch adds a should_align_to_pmd() helper that bumps p_align to PMD_SIZE in maximum_alignment() for read-only PT_LOAD segments whose p_vaddr and p_offset are already PMD_SIZE-aligned and whose file size covers at least one huge page, so that the ET_DYN load_bias is aligned to PMD_SIZE and THP-collapsing becomes possible.
fs
WANG Rui <r@hev.cc>

binfmt_elf: Align eligible read-only PT_LOAD segments to PMD_SIZE for THP

Verified the alignment logic, load_bias computation, and both ET_DYN
loading paths.  The patch looks correct.

> +static inline bool should_align_to_pmd(const struct elf_phdr *cmd)
> +{
> +	if (!IS_ENABLED(CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE))
> +		return false;
> +
> +	if (PMD_SIZE > SZ_32M)
> +		return false;
> +
> +	if (!IS_ALIGNED(cmd->p_vaddr | cmd->p_offset, PMD_SIZE))
> +		return false;

The IS_ALIGNED(a | b, n) trick is correct: OR-ing two values produces a
result with no low bits only if both operands individually have no low
bits, so this is equivalent to IS_ALIGNED(p_vaddr, PMD_SIZE) &&
IS_ALIGNED(p_offset, PMD_SIZE) without the extra branch.

> +		if (p_align < PMD_SIZE && should_align_to_pmd(&cmds[i]))
> +			p_align = PMD_SIZE;

maximum_alignment() is called only inside the ET_DYN branch
(else if (elf_ex->e_type == ET_DYN)), so this cannot affect ET_EXEC
binaries whose load addresses are fixed by the linker.

For ET_DYN with PT_INTERP (PIE + dynamic linker), the returned
alignment feeds directly into:

    load_bias &= ~(alignment - 1);

With alignment == PMD_SIZE, load_bias is PMD_SIZE-aligned.  Since
p_vaddr is also PMD_SIZE-aligned, the final address p_vaddr + load_bias
is PMD_SIZE-aligned, matching p_offset, satisfying THP eligibility.

For ET_DYN without PT_INTERP (static PIE / ld.so), the existing
alignment > ELF_MIN_ALIGN probe-and-realign mechanism already handles
any large alignment; PMD_SIZE flows through that path correctly.

The p_filesz (not p_memsz) check is right: THP eligibility depends on
the file-backed range, not the BSS tail.  The PF_W exclusion is correct
since writable segments are not eligible for file-backed PMD collapsing.

No new allocations, error paths, or locking changes.
Needs Work Refactor reserved memory regions handling code 🔗 Marek Szyprowski 7p
This 7-patch series refactors the reserved memory framework to remove fdt_node from struct reserved_mem, unify init callbacks into ops, and replace CMA-specific quirks with generic node_validate/node_fixup callbacks. Two concrete bugs were found: a wrong variable (node vs child) in fdt_scan_reserved_mem_late() silently breaking the cma= cmdline override, and a typo in the !CONFIG_OF_RESERVED_MEM stub macro that would cause build failures.
drivers include kernel
Author: Marek Szyprowski <m.szyprowski@samsung.com>

[PATCH 3/7] of: reserved_mem: switch to ops based OF_DECLARE()

The stub macro in the #else branch (!CONFIG_OF_RESERVED_MEM) has a
typo: the 4th argument passed to _OF_DECLARE_STUB is the literal token
'init', but the macro parameter was renamed to 'ops'.

> -#define RESERVEDMEM_OF_DECLARE(name, compat, init)			\
> -	_OF_DECLARE_STUB(reservedmem, name, compat, init, reservedmem_of_init_fn)
> +#define RESERVEDMEM_OF_DECLARE(name, compat, ops)			\
> +	_OF_DECLARE_STUB(reservedmem, name, compat, init, void *)

'init' on the new line is not the macro parameter -- the parameter is
'ops'.  _OF_DECLARE_STUB expands its fn argument into the expression
'(fn == (fn_type)NULL) ? fn : fn' for compile-time type checking, so
'init' must be a visible identifier at every call site, or the
translation unit fails to compile.

drivers/memory/tegra/tegra210-emc-table.c uses RESERVEDMEM_OF_DECLARE
without any surrounding #ifdef CONFIG_OF_RESERVED_MEM guard, so a
configuration with CONFIG_ARCH_TEGRA but without CONFIG_OF_RESERVED_MEM
would fail to build.

Should be:

	_OF_DECLARE_STUB(reservedmem, name, compat, ops, void *)

---

[PATCH 4/7] of: reserved_mem: replace CMA quirks by generic methods

> 	fdt_for_each_subnode(child, fdt, node) {
>  		const char *uname;
> -		bool default_cma = of_get_flat_dt_prop(child,
> -				"linux,cma-default", NULL);
>  		u64 b, s;
> +		int ret;
>
>  		if (!of_fdt_device_is_available(fdt, child))
>  			continue;
> -		if (default_cma && cma_skip_dt_default_reserved_mem())
> -			continue;
>
>  		if (!of_flat_dt_get_addr_size(child, "reg", &b, &s))
>  			continue;
>
> +		ret = fdt_validate_reserved_mem_node(node, NULL);
> +		if (ret && ret != -ENODEV)
> +			continue;

The call passes 'node' (the /reserved-memory parent) instead of 'child'
(the region being iterated).  'node' carries no 'compatible' property
matching any __reservedmem_of_table entry, so
fdt_validate_reserved_mem_node() always returns -ENODEV here, and
'ret && ret != -ENODEV' is always false.  The skip never fires.

The removed code read 'linux,cma-default' from 'child' and skipped it
when cma_skip_dt_default_reserved_mem() was true (i.e. when the user
passed 'cma=' on the kernel command line).  With this bug,
fdt_scan_reserved_mem_late() (renamed in patch 6/7) always enqueues
the DT default CMA region even when 'cma=' overrides it, silently
breaking the behaviour that commit 0fd17e598333 was meant to preserve.

The equivalent calls in __reserved_mem_reserve_reg() and
__reserved_mem_alloc_size() both correctly pass the child/region node;
only this one site is wrong.

Should be:

	ret = fdt_validate_reserved_mem_node(child, NULL);

On a 4K page system: control_allocation_size = 4096 * 512 = 2MB, so

Needs Discussion lib/maple_tree: fix potential NULL dereference in mas_pop_node() 🔗 Josh Law 1p
The patch adds a NULL check after kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf() in mas_pop_node() to prevent a NULL dereference in the subsequent memset(). The crash path is real, but the root cause diagnosis and completeness of the fix both need discussion.
lib
Josh Law <hlcj1234567@gmail.com>

lib/maple_tree: fix potential NULL dereference in mas_pop_node()

The NULL dereference at memset() is real -- if the sheaf is empty,
kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf() returns NULL and we crash.  But there
are a few things worth discussing before this lands.

> If kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf() returns NULL (possible under
> GFP_NOWAIT pressure), mas_pop_node() falls through to the out label
> and dereferences the NULL pointer in memset(ret, 0, sizeof(*ret)).

The commit message attributes the NULL return to GFP_NOWAIT pressure,
but that does not match the implementation.  Looking at
kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf_noprof() in mm/slub.c:

    if (sheaf->size == 0)
        goto out;
    ret = kfence_alloc(s, s->object_size, gfp);
    if (likely(!ret))
        ret = sheaf->objects[--sheaf->size];
    slab_post_alloc_hook(s, NULL, gfp | __GFP_NOFAIL, ...);

The sheaf objects are pre-allocated by mas_alloc_nodes().  GFP_NOWAIT
only affects kfence_alloc() (which returns NULL for normal objects in
the common case) and slab_post_alloc_hook() (which forces __GFP_NOFAIL
for memcg charging).  The function returns NULL exclusively because
sheaf->size == 0, i.e., the sheaf is empty -- not because of memory
pressure at the point of this call.

An empty sheaf here means either mas_alloc_nodes() was not called
before mas_pop_node(), or more nodes were popped than were requested
via node_request.  That is a programming error, analogous to the
existing WARN_ON_ONCE(!mas->sheaf) guard above it.  Dropping
WARN_ON_ONCE in v2 removes the only diagnostic signal for that class
of bug.

> diff --git a/lib/maple_tree.c b/lib/maple_tree.c
> --- a/lib/maple_tree.c
> +++ b/lib/maple_tree.c

[ ... ]

>  	ret = kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf(maple_node_cache, GFP_NOWAIT, mas->sheaf);
> +	if (!ret)
> +		return NULL;
>
>  out:
>  	memset(ret, 0, sizeof(*ret));

The fix prevents the crash inside mas_pop_node() itself, but every
caller dereferences the return value without a NULL check.  For
example, mas_root_expand():

    node = mas_pop_node(mas);
    pivots = ma_pivots(node, type);   /* NULL deref moves here */
    node->parent = ...;

The same pattern appears in mas_wr_node_copy(), the 3-way split setup
loop, and mas_dup_build().  Returning NULL here just moves the crash
site, it does not make the error recoverable.

Given that the callers already cannot handle NULL (the existing
WARN_ON_ONCE + return NULL path for !mas->sheaf also results in a
subsequent crash at the call site), would it make more sense to
reinstate WARN_ON_ONCE here so the empty-sheaf case is at least
diagnosed before the inevitable crash?  Silently returning NULL on a
programming-error misuse of the sheaf API makes it significantly
harder to find the root cause in the field.

Could you also double-check whether there is a legitimate non-error
path that can reach kmem_cache_alloc_from_sheaf() with an empty
sheaf after a successful mas_alloc_nodes() call?  If such a path
exists, the callers need NULL handling too; if it does not, the
commit message framing needs to be updated.

2026-03-12 (11)

Minor Issues mm: switch THP shrinker to list_lru 🔗 Johannes Weiner 7p
This series replaces the open-coded THP deferred_split_queue (per-node and per-memcg spinlock+list) with the list_lru infrastructure, properly establishing per-node-per-cgroup lists. Patches 1-5 are preparatory cleanups and API additions to list_lru.c; patches 6-7 introduce a folio-aware allocation helper and perform the actual conversion.
huge_memory include internal khugepaged list_lru memcontrol memory mm_init
Johannes Weiner <hannes@cmpxchg.org>

mm: switch THP shrinker to list_lru

The overall approach is clean and the motivation is solid.  Patches
1-4 are mechanical cleanups.  One question on patch 6.

--- [PATCH v2 1/7] mm: list_lru: lock_list_lru_of_memcg() cannot return NULL if !skip_empty ---

> -	l = lock_list_lru_of_memcg(lru, nid, memcg, false, false);
> -	if (!l)
> -		return false;

Verified: with skip_empty=false the MEMCG variant walks up the cgroup
hierarchy (VM_WARN_ON + parent_mem_cgroup goto-again loop) and the
!MEMCG variant unconditionally returns &lru->node[nid].lru.  Neither
path can return NULL.  Removing the dead checks in list_lru_add() and
list_lru_del() is correct.

[ patches 2-5: deduplication and new caller-locking API, look correct ]

--- [PATCH v2 6/7] mm: list_lru: introduce memcg_list_lru_alloc_folio() ---

> +	/* Fast path when list_lru heads already exist */
> +	rcu_read_lock();
> +	res = memcg_list_lru_allocated(folio_memcg(folio), lru);
> +	rcu_read_unlock();
> +	if (likely(res))
> +		return 0;

folio_memcg() returns NULL when there is no obj_cgroup attached (e.g.
uncharged folios; and, depending on configuration, root-cgroup folios
whose memcg_data is zero).  memcg_list_lru_allocated() immediately
dereferences its first argument with no NULL guard:

	static inline bool memcg_list_lru_allocated(
		struct mem_cgroup *memcg, struct list_lru *lru)
	{
		int idx = memcg->kmemcg_id;  /* crash if memcg == NULL */

By contrast, memcg_kmem_id() used by lock_list_lru_of_memcg() returns
-1 for NULL, so it handles the NULL case safely.

All call sites in patch 7 invoke memcg_list_lru_alloc_folio() only
after a successful mem_cgroup_charge(), so folio_memcg() should be
non-NULL in practice.  But could a root-cgroup folio in a memcg1
setup, or a folio whose memcg_data has not yet been set at the point
of the call, reach this path with folio_memcg() == NULL?

If that is truly impossible, a comment capturing the invariant would
help future readers.  If it is possible, the fix is straightforward:
when memcg is NULL, lock_list_lru_of_memcg() already falls back to
the per-node list (memcg_kmem_id returns -1), so there are no
per-cgroup heads to allocate and returning early is correct:

	rcu_read_lock();
	memcg = folio_memcg(folio);
	res = !memcg || memcg_list_lru_allocated(memcg, lru);
	rcu_read_unlock();

> +	/* Need to allocate, pin the memcg */
> +	memcg = get_mem_cgroup_from_folio(folio);
> +	res = __memcg_list_lru_alloc(memcg, lru, gfp);
> +	mem_cgroup_put(memcg);

Same question for the slow path: does get_mem_cgroup_from_folio()
always return a non-NULL memcg in the CONFIG_MEMCG path (e.g.
root_mem_cgroup with a ref for root-cgroup folios)?  If it can return
NULL, __memcg_list_lru_alloc() would crash on the first call to
memcg_list_lru_allocated() inside its do-while loop.

--- [PATCH v2 7/7] mm: switch deferred split shrinker to list_lru ---

> +	if (list_lru_init_memcg(&deferred_split_lru, deferred_split_shrinker)) {
> +		shrinker_free(deferred_split_shrinker);
> +		return -ENOMEM;
> +	}
> +
> +	deferred_split_shrinker->count_objects = deferred_split_count;
> +	deferred_split_shrinker->scan_objects = deferred_split_scan;
> +	shrinker_register(deferred_split_shrinker);

list_lru_init_memcg() only needs shrinker->id, which is set by
shrinker_alloc().  The callbacks are not consulted until after
shrinker_register() makes the shrinker visible, so the ordering is
fine.

> +	if (!huge_zero_folio_shrinker) {
> +		list_lru_destroy(&deferred_split_lru);
>  		shrinker_free(deferred_split_shrinker);
>  		return -ENOMEM;
>  	}

The new list_lru_destroy() in the huge_zero_folio_shrinker error path
is a correct addition; the prior code leaked the lru in that path.

Removing reparent_deferred_split_queue() and the deferred_split_queue
fields from mem_cgroup and pglist_data is correct: cgroup reparenting
is now handled by the generic memcg_reparent_list_lrus() path that
list_lru already hooks into via memcg_css_offline().

Looks Good selftests/mm: fix failures and robustness improvements 🔗 Sayali Patil 13p
This 13-patch series fixes selftests/mm failures on powerpc with 64K base pages by correcting hugetlb cgroup path construction for 1GB hugepages, fixing cgroup task placement races, sizing tmpfs dynamically for split_huge_page_test, adjusting hugepage-mremap size logic, making the userfaultfd registration apply to the correct hugetlb region, and ensuring the mremap destination is hugetlb-backed to avoid hash MMU slice conflicts.

Author: Sayali Patil <sayalip@linux.ibm.com>

selftests/mm: fix failures and robustness improvements (v2)

Overall the series looks correct. I read all ten modified files against
the diffs and traced through the key control paths. Notes below.

> --- [PATCH v2 01/13] selftests/mm: restore default nr_hugepages ---
>
> -  echo 0 >/proc/sys/vm/nr_hugepages
> +  echo "$nr_hugepgs" > /proc/sys/vm/nr_hugepages

nr_hugepgs is captured at script start before any test runs, so it
survives even when cleanup() is called from an early-exit path. Correct.

[ ... ]

> --- [PATCH v2 02/13] selftests/mm: fix hugetlb pathname construction ---
>
> +if (( MB >= 1024 )); then
> +        UNIT="GB"
> +        MB_DISPLAY=$((MB / 1024))
> +else
> +        UNIT="MB"
> +        MB_DISPLAY=$MB
> +fi

get_machine_hugepage_size() returns kB/1024, so for a 1GB page MB=1024,
MB_DISPLAY=1, UNIT=GB -> "hugetlb.1GB.current". For 512MB (if it ever
appears) MB=512, MB_DISPLAY=512, UNIT=MB -> "hugetlb.512MB.current",
which also matches the kernel naming. Correct.

One nit: run_test() in the same file still mounts hugetlbfs with
"-o pagesize=${MB}M", which for 1GB hugepages becomes "pagesize=1024M".
The kernel's memparse() accepts 1024M == 1G, so this is harmless, but
it could be made consistent with MB_DISPLAY/UNIT if desired.

[ ... ]

> --- [PATCH v2 04/13] selftest/mm: fix cgroup task placement ---
>
> +  ./write_to_hugetlbfs -p "$path" -s "$size" -m 0 -o -d & pid=$!
> +  echo "$pid" > "$cg_file"
> +  wait "$pid"

The -d flag fires sleep(1) inside the getopt switch, after -p/-s/-m/-o
are already parsed and before execution reaches the mmap call. The
parent's echo to cg_file is effectively instant, so the 1-second window
is more than sufficient in practice.

With set -e active at all call sites, a non-zero exit from
wait "$pid" (e.g. allocation failure) correctly aborts the test.

> +	case 'd':
> +		sleep(1);
> +		break;

A caller passing -d twice would sleep twice. Not a bug for this
controlled usage, but worth documenting if write_to_hugetlbfs is
used more broadly.

[ ... ]

> --- [PATCH v2 05/13] selftests/mm: size tmpfs according to PMD ---
>
> +	unsigned long size = 2 * pmd_pagesize;
> +	char opts[64];
>  ...
> +	snprintf(opts, sizeof(opts), "huge=always,size=%lu", size);

pmd_pagesize is uint64_t; size is unsigned long. On 64-bit hosts these
are the same width. The longest plausible string is
"huge=always,size=2147483648" (2 * 1GB PMD) at 27 bytes, well within
the 64-byte opts buffer. Correct.

[ ... ]

> --- [PATCH v2 06/13] selftest/mm: adjust hugepage-mremap test size ---
>
> +if [ "$hpgsize_KB" -gt 10240 ]; then
> +	len_mb=$(( (2 * hpgsize_KB) / 1024 ))
> +	CATEGORY="hugetlb" run_test ./hugepage-mremap "${len_mb}"
> +else
> +	CATEGORY="hugetlb" run_test ./hugepage-mremap
> +fi

For 1GB pages hpgsize_KB=1048576, len_mb=2048. hugepage-mremap uses
atoi(argv[1]) so this lands as 2048 MB. The comment in hugepage-mremap.c
says >=1GB is needed to trigger PMD sharing; 2GB satisfies that.
Correct.

[ ... ]

> --- [PATCH v2 07/13] selftest/mm: register existing mapping with uffd ---
>
> -	addr = mmap(NULL, len, PROT_READ | PROT_WRITE,
> -		    MAP_PRIVATE | MAP_ANONYMOUS, -1, 0);
> -	if (addr == MAP_FAILED)
> -		ksft_exit_fail_msg("mmap: %s\n", strerror(errno));
>  	if (uffd_register(uffd, addr, len, true, false, false))
>  		ksft_exit_fail_msg("ioctl-UFFDIO_REGISTER: %s\n", strerror(errno));

The removed mmap was registering an unrelated anonymous mapping instead
of the hugetlb region passed by the caller. Fixing this so uffd tracks
the actual test region is the right thing to do.

The uffd fd opened in this function is never closed; this was also true
before the patch and is a pre-existing leak. O_CLOEXEC limits the damage
to the test's own lifetime, so not a regression.

> --- [PATCH v2 08/13] selftests/mm: ensure destination is hugetlb-backed ---
>
> -#define FLAGS (MAP_SHARED | MAP_ANONYMOUS)
> +#define FLAGS (MAP_HUGETLB | MAP_SHARED | MAP_POPULATE)
>  ...
> -	void *vaddr =
> -		mmap((void *)suggested_addr, length, PROTECTION, FLAGS, -1, 0);
> +	void *vaddr = mmap((void *)suggested_addr, length, PROTECTION, FLAGS, fd, 0);

All three mappings (haddr, daddr, vaddr) now use MAP_SHARED on the same
fd, so they share the same physical hugepages. Total hugepage usage
remains ~length (not 3x), since MAP_SHARED of the same file offset
reuses the same pages. MAP_POPULATE on vaddr pre-faults already-mapped
physical pages, so no additional hugepages are consumed beyond what
haddr and daddr already faulted in.

One subtle point: haddr is registered with uffd using
UFFDIO_REGISTER_MODE_MISSING, then mremap'd to vaddr. Because
MAP_POPULATE already faulted all pages in before registration, no
MISSING faults are generated during the subsequent write_bytes() call.
The absence of a uffd fault-handler thread therefore does not stall the
test. Verified this path.

[ ... ]

I also verified: the nr_pages_per_cpu == 0 skip path in uffd-stress
returns KSFT_SKIP (4) which run_vmtests.sh counts as [SKIP] correctly;
the uffd_wp_feature_supported() guard in uffd-wp-mremap exits with
ksft_exit_skip when UFFD_FEATURE_PAGEFAULT_FLAG_WP is absent; the
hwpoison setup inside run_test() correctly silences modprobe output and
sets skip=1 if the module is not available; and the MEMCG_CHARGE_BATCH
batching tolerance in test_hugetlb_memcg is well-motivated for 64K
base pages where nr_pages per hugepage can be below the batch threshold.

No regressions found across all ten modified files.
