Looks Good mm: migrate: requeue destination folio on deferred split queue 🔗 Usama Arif 1p
The patch fixes NUMA migration of THPs by re-queueing the destination folio on the deferred split list when the source was on it, since __folio_migrate_mapping() unqueues the source but never re-queues the destination. The state (partially_mapped or just underused) is recorded before move_to_new_folio() removes the source and then forwarded to deferred_split_folio() on the destination.
migrate
Usama Arif <usama.arif@linux.dev>

mm: migrate: requeue destination folio on deferred split queue

Verified the following:

> +	if (folio_order(src) > 1 &&
> +	    !data_race(list_empty(&src->_deferred_list))) {
> +		src_deferred_split = true;
> +		src_partially_mapped = folio_test_partially_mapped(src);
> +	}

The data_race() annotation here mirrors the identical idiom in the
folio_unqueue_deferred_split() inline wrapper in mm/internal.h,
which also reads _deferred_list racily as a fast-path guard before
calling __folio_unqueue_deferred_split().  Both the _deferred_list
membership and PG_partially_mapped are read without the
split_queue_lock, but the race consequences are bounded: a false
positive re-queues dst unnecessarily (harmless, shrinker will try
to split or skip), and a false negative leaves dst off the queue in
a tiny window no worse than the pre-existing bug.  The
folio_order > 1 guard matches deferred_split_folio()'s own
early-return for order <= 1.

The removed folio_test_large_rmappable() guard (v2->v3) is correct:
only large_rmappable folios are ever added to the deferred list, so
a non-empty _deferred_list already implies rmappability.

> +	if (src_deferred_split)
> +		deferred_split_folio(dst, src_partially_mapped);

Placement is correct: success path only, after folio_add_lru(dst)
and remove_migration_ptes(), before dst is unlocked.
folio_migrate_flags() does not copy PG_partially_mapped to dst, so
deferred_split_folio() is the right place to set it on dst.
deferred_split_folio() guards against double-queueing via its own
list_empty() check under split_queue_lock, and dst is freshly
allocated so VM_WARN_ON_FOLIO(folio_test_partially_mapped(dst))
cannot fire on the partially_mapped=false arm.

Looks good to me.
Looks Good slub: clarify kmem_cache_refill_sheaf() failure behavior 🔗 Hao Li 1p
Documentation-only patch that rewrites the comment for kmem_cache_refill_sheaf() to distinguish its two failure modes more precisely, and softens "always" to "usually" for the refill-to-capacity claim.
slub
Hao Li <hao.li@linux.dev>

slub: clarify kmem_cache_refill_sheaf() failure behavior

Comment-only change; no functional delta. I traced both failure paths
to verify the new description is accurate.

> +++ b/mm/slub.c

[ ... ]

> + *     1. If the requested size fits within the current sheaf's capacity, the
> + *     refill is done in place. In that case, a failed refill may still fill
> + *     some additional objects into the existing sheaf before returning -ENOMEM.

Verified: the in-place path goes through __prefill_sheaf_pfmemalloc()
-> refill_sheaf(), which does 'sheaf->size += filled' before checking
'filled < to_fill', so partial progress is committed to the sheaf
before -ENOMEM is returned. Accurate.

> + *     2. If the requested size exceeds the current sheaf's capacity, a new
> + *     larger sheaf may be allocated to replace the original one. In that case,
> + *     if allocation of the replacement sheaf fails, the original sheaf is left
> + *     unchanged.

Verified: the oversize path calls kmem_cache_prefill_sheaf() and
returns -ENOMEM immediately on failure, before kmem_cache_return_sheaf()
or the *sheafp update, so the caller's sheaf pointer is untouched.
Accurate.

> - * In practice we always refill to full sheaf's capacity.
> + * In practice we usually refill to the sheaf's full capacity.

'usually' is appropriate: the API accepts an arbitrary size argument,
even if primary callers pass s->sheaf_capacity.

Looks good to me.
Needs Work mm/mempolicy: add sysfs interface to override NUMA node bandwidth 🔗 YeeLi 1p
This patch adds an optional CONFIG_NUMA_BW_MANUAL_OVERRIDE sysfs interface under weighted_interleave/ to let userspace override per-node bandwidth values fed into mempolicy_set_node_perf(). Several correctness bugs are present in the new code.
Kconfig mempolicy
From: <reviewer>

mm/mempolicy: add sysfs interface to override NUMA node bandwidth

Thanks for the patch.  A few issues found by cross-referencing the new
code against the existing sysfs_wi_node_delete() pattern and the
wi_state_lock comment at the node_bw_table declaration.

> +static ssize_t bw_node_show(struct kobject *kobj,
> +			    struct kobj_attribute *attr,
> +			    char *buf)
> +{
> +	/*A Node without CDAT or HMAT*/
> +	if (!node_bw_table)
> +		return sprintf(buf, "N/A\n");
> +
> +	if (!node_bw_table[node_attr->nid])
> +		return sprintf(buf, "0\n");
> +
> +	return sprintf(buf, "%u(MB/s)\n", node_bw_table[node_attr->nid]);
> +}

Two problems here.

First, node_bw_table is protected by wi_state_lock per its declaration
comment:

  /* wi_state_lock protects both wi_state and node_bw_table. */

mempolicy_set_node_perf() assigns a fresh array to node_bw_table under
wi_state_lock, then frees the old one after dropping the lock (the
kfree(old_bw) at the bottom of that function runs unlocked).
bw_node_show() reads node_bw_table without holding wi_state_lock, so a
concurrent mempolicy_set_node_perf() can free the old table between the
!node_bw_table check and the node_bw_table[node_attr->nid] dereference.
This is a use-after-free.  The show handler needs to acquire
wi_state_lock (or snapshot the value under the lock) before
dereferencing node_bw_table.

Second, sysfs show callbacks must use sysfs_emit() instead of
sprintf().  sprintf() has no bounds check against the PAGE_SIZE sysfs
buffer.  Every other show function in this file uses sysfs_emit().

> +static ssize_t bw_node_store(struct kobject *kobj,
> +			     struct kobj_attribute *attr,
> +			     const char *buf, size_t count)
> +{
[ ... ]
> +	ret = kstrtoul(buf, 0, &val);
> +
> +	coords.read_bandwidth = val;
> +	coords.write_bandwidth = val;
> +
> +	if (ret)
> +		return ret;

coords is populated from val before the kstrtoul() return value is
checked.  If kstrtoul() fails, val is indeterminate.  The assignments
to coords.read_bandwidth and coords.write_bandwidth should move to
after the 'if (ret)' early-return check.

> +static void sysfs_bw_node_delete(int nid)
> +{
> +	mutex_lock(&wi_group->kobj_lock);
> +	attr = wi_group->bw_attrs[nid];
> +
> +	if (attr) {
> +		sysfs_remove_file(&wi_group->wi_kobj, &attr->kobj_attr.attr);
> +		kfree(attr->kobj_attr.attr.name);
> +		kfree(attr);
> +		wi_group->nattrs[nid] = NULL;
> +	}
> +	mutex_unlock(&wi_group->kobj_lock);
> +}

Two problems here.

First, the wrong slot is cleared on delete.  The function reads
wi_group->bw_attrs[nid] but then clears wi_group->nattrs[nid].  After
the delete, bw_attrs[nid] still holds the freed pointer.  A subsequent
sysfs_bw_node_add() for the same nid finds bw_attrs[nid] non-NULL and
returns -EEXIST without creating the file.  A subsequent
sysfs_bw_node_delete() passes the stale pointer to sysfs_remove_file()
and kfree().  The assignment should be:

    wi_group->bw_attrs[nid] = NULL;

Second, the locking pattern is inconsistent with sysfs_wi_node_delete().
That function nulls nattrs[nid] under the lock, drops the lock, and
only then calls sysfs_remove_file().  sysfs_remove_file() may block
waiting for an in-progress show/store callback to complete; holding
kobj_lock across that wait diverges from the established pattern.
Please follow sysfs_wi_node_delete(): null bw_attrs[nid] under the
lock, unlock, then call sysfs_remove_file() and kfree().
Needs Work lib/idr: Fixes for infinite loop and memory leak 🔗 Josh Law 2p
Two patches for lib/idr: the first sets *nextid=INT_MAX in idr_get_next() when an out-of-range ID is found; the second claims to fix a real memory leak in ida_alloc_range() but the actual lib/idr.c change is entirely absent from the diff.
lib tests
Josh Law <hlcj1234567@gmail.com>

lib/idr: Fixes for infinite loop and memory leak (v3 0/2)

Thanks for the series.  I have concerns with both patches.

--- Patch 1/2: fix infinite loop in idr_get_next() ---

> +	if (WARN_ON_ONCE(id > INT_MAX)) {
> +		*nextid = INT_MAX;
>  		return NULL;
> +	}

The commit message says this fixes a soft lockup for callers using
idr_for_each_entry().  Looking at the macro:

  #define idr_for_each_entry(idr, entry, id)                      \
          for (id = 0; ((entry) = idr_get_next(idr, &(id))) != NULL; id += 1U)

The increment `id += 1U` is only reached when entry is non-NULL.  When
idr_get_next() returns NULL on the WARN path, the loop condition fails
immediately and the loop exits.  The same is true for
idr_for_each_entry_continue() and idr_for_each_entry_continue_ul() --
all terminate on a NULL return.  What concrete caller and call sequence
produces the claimed soft lockup?

Setting *nextid = INT_MAX when the actual found ID is e.g. 0x80000001
is also questionable.  A caller resuming from *nextid = INT_MAX would
call idr_get_next_ul() from INT_MAX, find the same out-of-range entry
(since 0x80000001 > INT_MAX), WARN again, and return NULL again.  It
does not advance past the bad entry.

> -		BUG_ON(sid != 0);
> +		BUG_ON(sid != INT_MAX);

The original assertion documented the prior contract: *nextid is
unchanged on the error path.  If that contract is changing, please
explain in the commit message why INT_MAX is the right sentinel and
why changing it is safe for all existing callers.

--- Patch 2/2: fix memory leak in ida_alloc_range() error path ---

The commit message says:

  Reorder the error handling to ensure `alloc` is properly freed
  when an XArray error occurs.

But the diff is:

  diff --git a/tools/testing/radix-tree/idr-test.c ...

Only idr-test.c is modified.  The change to lib/idr.c is missing.

To confirm the leak is real: in ida_alloc_range(), the path is

  alloc: kzalloc_obj()  -->  retry  -->  xa_is_value branch:
    bitmap = alloc;
    xas_store(&xas, bitmap);   /* can fail if xarray needs to grow */
    if (xas_error(&xas)) {
        bitmap->bitmap[0] = 0;
        goto out;              /* bitmap == alloc here */
    }

  out:
    if (bitmap != alloc)       /* FALSE -- kfree() is skipped */
        kfree(alloc);
    if (xas_error(&xas))
        return xas_error(&xas); /* alloc leaked */

The same issue exists in the else-branch when bit >= BITS_PER_XA_VALUE
and xas_store() fails after setting bitmap = alloc.  The lib/idr.c fix
must be included in this patch.

> +static void ida_check_leak(void)
> +{
> +	DEFINE_IDA(ida);
> +
> +	/* Allocate up to 128 to ensure we need a new bitmap */
> +	ida_alloc_range(&ida, 0, 128, GFP_KERNEL);
> +	
> +	/* Force a failure by providing an invalid range */
> +	ida_alloc_range(&ida, 0, 0, GFP_KERNEL);

This does not exercise the described error path.  With ID 0 already
allocated, the second call finds the existing bitmap, sees bit 0 set,
searches for the next zero bit, finds it exceeds max=0, and jumps to
nospc -- which correctly calls kfree(alloc).  No XArray insertion
failure occurs.  A test covering the actual leak would need to fail
xas_store() during the xa_is_value-to-bitmap conversion, which this
test does not do.

> +	ida_destroy(&ida);
> +}
> +
>  static void *ida_leak_fn(void *arg)

ida_check_leak() is declared static and defined here, after
user_ida_checks() which calls it.  In C11 there is no implicit
function declaration; calling an undeclared static function is a
constraint violation.  This will not compile.  Either add a forward
declaration before user_ida_checks(), or move ida_check_leak() above
it.

Please respin with:
  1. A concrete reproduction scenario for the Patch 1 infinite loop
     claim, or a revised commit message that accurately describes
     what is being fixed.
  2. The missing lib/idr.c change in Patch 2.
  3. A test that actually triggers the xas_store() failure in the
     xa_is_value conversion path.
  4. The forward declaration or reordering of ida_check_leak().

  • [PATCH v3 2/2] lib/idr: fix memory leak in ida_alloc_range() error path

Needs Discussion lib/idr: fix infinite loop in idr_get_next() 🔗 Josh Law 1p
Adds `*nextid = INT_MAX` to the WARN_ON_ONCE branch of idr_get_next() so callers have a defined cursor value when an out-of-range ID is detected. The commit message incorrectly describes the impact as a soft lockup/infinite loop.
lib
From: Josh Law <objecting@objecting.org>
Subject: [PATCH v2] lib/idr: fix infinite loop in idr_get_next()

The commit message claims that not updating *nextid causes a soft lockup
because the caller's index fails to advance and the loop repeats
forever.  I traced the iteration macros in idr.h and cannot reproduce
that scenario.

> diff --git a/lib/idr.c b/lib/idr.c
> @@ -268,8 +268,10 @@ void *idr_get_next(struct idr *idr, int *nextid)
>  	unsigned long id = *nextid;
>  	void *entry = idr_get_next_ul(idr, &id);
>  
> -	if (WARN_ON_ONCE(id > INT_MAX))
> +	if (WARN_ON_ONCE(id > INT_MAX)) {
> +		*nextid = INT_MAX;
>  		return NULL;
> +	}

The standard iteration macro is:

    for (id = 0; ((entry) = idr_get_next(idr, &(id))) != NULL; id += 1U)

The `id += 1U` increment lives in the for-loop's third clause: it runs
only when the condition was true in the previous iteration.  When
idr_get_next() returns NULL -- which it does in both the old and new
code -- the condition evaluates to false and the loop exits immediately;
`id += 1U` is never reached.  The same holds for
idr_for_each_entry_continue() and idr_for_each_entry_ul(), both of
which break on a NULL return.  Could you point to a concrete call site
where the old code actually loops forever?

Beyond the commit message concern, there is a correctness question about
which execution path triggers the WARN.  There are two distinct cases:

(a) idr_get_next_ul() finds a real entry at id > INT_MAX and returns it;
    idr_get_next() discards the entry and returns NULL.  Setting
    *nextid = INT_MAX here is reasonable as a sentinel.

(b) idr_get_next_ul() returns NULL (no entry found) and leaves the
    local `id` unchanged.  If the caller passed a negative int -- which
    idr_for_each_entry does after INT_MAX + 1U wraps to INT_MIN on a
    two's-complement system -- the unsigned long conversion of *nextid
    produces a value far above INT_MAX, WARN fires, and the function
    returns NULL even though no out-of-range entry exists.

    In case (b) the patch sets *nextid = INT_MAX even though
    idr_get_next_ul() returned NULL.  A caller that saves *nextid and
    resumes from it would then re-visit the entry at INT_MAX that was
    already processed.

Finally, note that if there were a loop that did not exit on NULL,
setting *nextid = INT_MAX would not prevent it from spinning: the next
`id += 1U` would wrap to INT_MIN again, sign-extend to a value above
INT_MAX, and re-trigger the WARN on every subsequent iteration.

Could the commit message be updated to describe the actual observable
behaviour (WARN fires, entry is silently dropped, cursor is left
unchanged), and could case (b) above be addressed or ruled out?
Looks Good lib/idr: fix memory leak in ida_alloc_range() error path 🔗 Josh Law 1p
ida_alloc_range() leaks the 'alloc' bitmap when xas_store() fails and bitmap==alloc, because the original 'if (bitmap != alloc) kfree(alloc)' guard evaluates false in that case. The patch reorders the checks so xas_error is tested first, freeing alloc unconditionally on failure.
lib
Josh Law <hlcj1234567@gmail.com>

lib/idr: fix memory leak in ida_alloc_range() error path

Verified against lib/idr.c.  The leak is real and the fix is correct.

> diff --git a/lib/idr.c b/lib/idr.c
> --- a/lib/idr.c
> +++ b/lib/idr.c

[ ... ]

>  	if (xas_nomem(&xas, gfp)) {
>  		xas.xa_index = min / IDA_BITMAP_BITS;
>  		bit = min % IDA_BITMAP_BITS;
>  		goto retry;
>  	}
> -	if (bitmap != alloc)
> +	if (xas_error(&xas)) {
>  		kfree(alloc);
> -	if (xas_error(&xas))
>  		return xas_error(&xas);
> +	}
> +	if (bitmap != alloc)
> +		kfree(alloc);

I traced two paths that trigger the original leak:

1. xa_is_value overflow path: bitmap is set to alloc (line 418 in the
   source); xas_store() fails; bitmap->bitmap[0] is reset to 0 and we
   goto out.  Since bitmap == alloc, the original guard evaluates false
   and alloc is never freed before returning the error.

2. NULL-bitmap / high-bit path: bitmap is set to alloc (line 445);
   xas_store() can fail with no inline xas_error check, falling through
   to out.  Same bitmap == alloc condition, same leak.

The fix is correct on both paths.  xas_nomem() is still checked first,
so the retry path that needs alloc intact is unaffected.  In the success
case, 'if (bitmap != alloc) kfree(alloc)' correctly avoids freeing a
bitmap now owned by the XArray.

When alloc is NULL (first pass before any alloc: detour), kfree(alloc)
in the patched error branch is kfree(NULL) -- a no-op -- so no
regression there either.

Looks good to me.
Needs Work Fix race condition in the memory management system 🔗 Hubert Mazur 1p
The patch fixes a real race in execmem_cache_alloc() where a concurrent thread can consume the freshly-populated free block between execmem_cache_populate() and the second __execmem_cache_alloc() call, by allocating directly into busy_areas. However, it introduces a memory leak: only 'size' bytes are recorded in busy_areas while the actual vmalloc allocation is 'alloc_size' (round_up(size, PMD_SIZE)) bytes, causing the tail to be permanently untracked.
execmem
Author: Hubert Mazur &lt;hmazur@google.com&gt;

mm: fix race condition in the memory management

The race being fixed is real -- execmem_cache_populate() releases the
mutex after adding to free_areas, and a concurrent thread can consume
that block before the second __execmem_cache_alloc() call.  The
overall approach of going straight to busy_areas is sound, but there
is a memory leak in the implementation.

&gt; diff --git a/mm/execmem.c b/mm/execmem.c

[ ... ]

&gt; +static void *__execmem_cache_alloc(struct execmem_range *range, size_t size)
&gt;  {
&gt; +	struct maple_tree *busy_areas = &amp;execmem_cache.busy_areas;
&gt;  	unsigned long vm_flags = VM_ALLOW_HUGE_VMAP;
&gt;  	struct vm_struct *vm;
&gt; +	unsigned long addr;
&gt;  	size_t alloc_size;
&gt;  	int err = -ENOMEM;
&gt;  	void *p;

[ ... ]

&gt; +	/* Set new allocation as an already busy fragment */
&gt; +	addr = (unsigned long)p;
&gt; +	MA_STATE(mas, busy_areas, addr - 1, addr + 1);
&gt; +	mas_set_range(&amp;mas, addr, addr+size - 1);

The busy_areas entry covers [addr, addr+size-1], but the vmalloc
allocation above is alloc_size bytes (round_up(size, PMD_SIZE)), not
size bytes.  When the PMD-aligned allocation succeeds, alloc_size &gt;
size, and the tail [addr+size, addr+alloc_size-1] is never stored in
either busy_areas or free_areas.

In the original execmem_cache_populate(), the full alloc_size was
passed to execmem_cache_add(), and then __execmem_cache_alloc() split
it: size bytes into busy_areas, the remainder back into free_areas.
That split is now missing.

On the free path, __execmem_cache_free() calls mas_range_len() to
learn the size of the busy entry, gets back only size bytes, and
passes that to execmem_cache_add_locked().  The tail bytes never
reach free_areas.  execmem_cache_clean() then checks
IS_ALIGNED(size, PMD_SIZE) and IS_ALIGNED(mas.index, PMD_SIZE)
before calling vfree(); since only the sub-PMD slice is ever visible
in free_areas, vfree() is never called on the original vmalloc region
and those pages leak permanently.

To fix this, the code should either:
  (a) store alloc_size in busy_areas so the free path can reconstruct
      the full allocation extent, or
  (b) keep the split: under the same mutex hold, insert size bytes
      into busy_areas and the remainder [addr+size, addr+alloc_size-1]
      into free_areas.

&gt; +	mutex_lock(&amp;execmem_cache.mutex);
&gt; +	err = mas_store_gfp(&amp;mas, (void *)addr, GFP_KERNEL);
&gt; +	mutex_unlock(&amp;execmem_cache.mutex);

The locking here is correct: MA_STATE initialisation before the lock
is fine (it is just a struct init), and mas_store_gfp() on the
MT_FLAGS_LOCK_EXTERN tree is called under the mutex.

&gt; +	if (err)
&gt; +		goto err_reset_direct_map;
&gt; +
&gt; +	return p;

The error path (execmem_set_direct_map_valid + vfree) correctly
covers the entire vmalloc region on mas_store_gfp failure.

&gt; -	p = __execmem_cache_alloc(range, size);
&gt; +	p = __execmem_cache_lookup(range, size);
&gt;  	if (p)
&gt;  		return p;
&gt;  
&gt; -	err = execmem_cache_populate(range, size);
&gt; -	if (err)
&gt; -		return NULL;
&gt; -
&gt;  	return __execmem_cache_alloc(range, size);

The new execmem_cache_alloc() is cleaner and the rename of the
lookup helper is an improvement.  Two concurrent callers racing
into __execmem_cache_alloc() get distinct vmalloc VAs, so no
additional synchronisation is needed outside of the mas_store_gfp
insertion itself.  The correctness concern is purely the alloc_size
vs size mismatch described above.

  • [PATCH v1 0/1] Fix race condition in the memory management system
  • [PATCH v1 1/1] mm: fix race condition in the memory management
Looks Good mm/swap: strengthen locking assertions and invariants in cluster allocation 🔗 Hui Zhu 1p
The patch strengthens locking assertions in swap_cluster_alloc_table() and adds a VM_WARN_ON_ONCE() in isolate_lock_cluster() to formalize the invariant that table allocation only occurs for free clusters isolated from the allocator path, not from the reclaim path.

From: Hui Zhu <zhuhui@kylinos.cn>

mm/swap: strengthen locking assertions and invariants in cluster allocation

Verified the three changes against the actual call paths in swapfile.c.

> diff --git a/mm/swapfile.c b/mm/swapfile.c

[ ... ]

> -	lockdep_assert_held(&ci->lock);
>  	lockdep_assert_held(&this_cpu_ptr(&percpu_swap_cluster)->lock);
> +	if (!(si->flags & SWP_SOLIDSTATE))
> +		lockdep_assert_held(&si->global_cluster_lock);
> +	lockdep_assert_held(&ci->lock);

The reordering and new global_cluster_lock assertion look correct.
cluster_alloc_swap_entry() acquires global_cluster_lock for non-SSD
at the top of the function (before any alloc_swap_scan_list() calls),
so the lock is always held when isolate_lock_cluster() ->
swap_cluster_alloc_table() is reached from that path.

For swap_reclaim_work() -> swap_reclaim_full_clusters() ->
isolate_lock_cluster(), neither global_cluster_lock nor the percpu
lock is held. But full_clusters entries always have their tables
already allocated, so cluster_table_is_alloced() returns true and
swap_cluster_alloc_table() is never reached from that path. The
VM_WARN_ON_ONCE additions below guard this invariant explicitly.

> +		flags = ci->flags;
>  		ci->flags = CLUSTER_FLAG_NONE;

[ ... ]

> +		VM_WARN_ON_ONCE(flags != CLUSTER_FLAG_FREE);
>  		VM_WARN_ON_ONCE(list != &si->free_clusters);

The new check fires before the existing list-pointer check and gives
a more specific diagnostic; both guard the same invariant from
different angles. The u8 flags = CLUSTER_FLAG_NONE initializer
ensures a defined value before the loop body runs; it is always
overwritten before use inside the if (found && ...) block.

Looks good to me.

Needs Work mm: thp: reduce unnecessary start_stop_khugepaged() calls 🔗 Breno Leitao 4p
This series reduces unnecessary start_stop_khugepaged() calls by only invoking it when THP settings actually change, and rate-limits the resulting pr_info/pr_warn messages. The approach is sound but Patch 3 introduces a data race by replacing atomic bit operations with non-atomic ones in set_global_enabled_mode() without adding a protecting lock.
huge_memory internal khugepaged page_alloc
Breno Leitao <leitao@debian.org>

mm: thp: reduce unnecessary start_stop_khugepaged() calls

The overall goal is good: skip start_stop_khugepaged() when nothing
changed, and rate-limit the log messages.  Patches 1, 2, and 4 look
correct to me.  There is a locking regression in Patch 3.

--- [PATCH v6 2/4] mm: huge_memory: refactor anon_enabled_store() ---

> +static bool set_anon_enabled_mode(int order, enum anon_enabled_mode mode)
> +{
> +	static unsigned long *enabled_orders[] = {
> +		&huge_anon_orders_always,
> +		&huge_anon_orders_inherit,
> +		&huge_anon_orders_madvise,
> +	};
> +	enum anon_enabled_mode m;
> +	bool changed = false;
> +
> +	spin_lock(&huge_anon_orders_lock);
> +	for (m = 0; m < ARRAY_SIZE(enabled_orders); m++) {
> +		if (m == mode)
> +			changed |= !__test_and_set_bit(order, enabled_orders[m]);
> +		else
> +			changed |= __test_and_clear_bit(order, enabled_orders[m]);
> +	}
> +	spin_unlock(&huge_anon_orders_lock);

Correct: non-atomic __test_and_set_bit / __test_and_clear_bit are used
under huge_anon_orders_lock, which is the right pattern.

--- [PATCH v6 3/4] mm: huge_memory: refactor enabled_store() ---

> +static bool set_global_enabled_mode(enum global_enabled_mode mode)
> +{
> +	static const unsigned long thp_flags[] = {
> +		TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE_FLAG,
> +		TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE_REQ_MADV_FLAG,
> +	};
> +	enum global_enabled_mode m;
> +	bool changed = false;
> +
> +	for (m = 0; m < ARRAY_SIZE(thp_flags); m++) {
> +		if (m == mode)
> +			changed |= !__test_and_set_bit(thp_flags[m],
> +						       &transparent_hugepage_flags);
> +		else
> +			changed |= __test_and_clear_bit(thp_flags[m],
> +							&transparent_hugepage_flags);
> +	}
> +
> +	return changed;
> +}

This is a data-race regression.  The original enabled_store() used
atomic set_bit() / clear_bit() on transparent_hugepage_flags, which
are safe for concurrent callers (multiple sysfs writers, or writers
racing with the lockless readers such as hugepage_global_enabled()
and hugepage_pmd_enabled()).  The new code replaces those with
non-atomic __test_and_set_bit() / __test_and_clear_bit() without
holding any lock.

Compare set_anon_enabled_mode() in the previous patch, which wraps
the identical pattern with spin_lock(&huge_anon_orders_lock).  The
global helper needs the same treatment: either add a spinlock around
the bit operations, or switch to the atomic test_and_set_bit() /
test_and_clear_bit() variants, which also return the old bit value so
the 'changed' tracking still works correctly.

KCSAN will flag __test_and_set_bit() racing with the plain word-load
in hugepage_global_enabled() even on a uniprocessor build with
CONFIG_KCSAN=y.

--- [PATCH v6 4/4] mm: ratelimit min_free_kbytes adjustment messages ---

> -		pr_info("raising min_free_kbytes from %d to %lu to help"...);
> +		pr_info_ratelimited("raising min_free_kbytes from %d to %lu"...);

Rate-limiting looks correct.  Both message sites in
set_recommended_min_free_kbytes() and calculate_min_free_kbytes()
are switched to their _ratelimited variants.  No other callers
affected.

mm: khugepaged cleanups and mTHP prerequisites (v3, 5-patch series)

Patch 1 (consolidate anonymous folio PTE mapping)
--------------------------------------------------

> +void map_anon_folio_pte_nopf(struct folio *folio, pte_t *pte,
> +		struct vm_area_struct *vma, unsigned long addr,
> +		bool uffd_wp)
> +{
> +	unsigned int nr_pages = folio_nr_pages(folio);
> +	pte_t entry = folio_mk_pte(folio, vma->vm_page_prot);
> +
[ ... ]
> +	set_ptes(vma->vm_mm, addr, pte, entry, nr_pages);
> +	update_mmu_cache_range(NULL, vma, addr, pte, nr_pages);
> +}

Passing NULL for vmf is correct.  Checked every in-tree
update_mmu_cache_range() implementation (x86, arm64, arc, xtensa,
csky, parisc, nios2): none dereference the vmf pointer.  arm64
defines update_mmu_cache as update_mmu_cache_range(NULL, ...) already.

> +static void map_anon_folio_pte_pf(struct folio *folio, pte_t *pte,
> +		struct vm_area_struct *vma, unsigned long addr, bool uffd_wp)
> +{
> +	unsigned int order = folio_order(folio);
> +
> +	map_anon_folio_pte_nopf(folio, pte, vma, addr, uffd_wp);
> +	add_mm_counter(vma->vm_mm, MM_ANONPAGES, 1 << order);
> +	count_mthp_stat(order, MTHP_STAT_ANON_FAULT_ALLOC);
> +}

The MM_ANONPAGES delta is equivalent to the removed nr_pages:
folio_nr_pages(folio) == 1 << folio_order(folio).  Moving
add_mm_counter after set_ptes is fine; the counter is per-mm
accounting and is not observed under the PTE spinlock.

Verified: the PTE spinlock is held by the caller at the
map_anon_folio_pte_pf call site (after pte_offset_map_lock, after
vmf_pte_changed and userfaultfd_missing checks).  folio_ref_add,
folio_add_new_anon_rmap, folio_add_lru_vma, and set_ptes order all
match the original sequence.  The uffd_wp handling is preserved
identically in the helper.

Zero-page path: addr is still vmf->address at that point (before the
ALIGN_DOWN reassignment for the write path), and set_pte_at is
equivalent to set_ptes with nr=1 on all architectures.  The
update_mmu_cache_range in the zero-page path correctly continues to
pass vmf (not NULL) matching the original.

Patch 5 (collapse_single_pmd unification)
-----------------------------------------

> +	if (result == SCAN_PTE_MAPPED_HUGEPAGE) {
> +		mmap_read_lock(mm);
> +		if (collapse_test_exit_or_disable(mm))
> +			result = SCAN_ANY_PROCESS;
> +		else
> +			result = try_collapse_pte_mapped_thp(mm, addr,
> +							     !cc->is_khugepaged);
> +		if (result == SCAN_PMD_MAPPED)
> +			result = SCAN_SUCCEED;
> +		mmap_read_unlock(mm);
> +	}
> +end:
> +	if (cc->is_khugepaged && result == SCAN_SUCCEED)
> +		++khugepaged_pages_collapsed;

mmap_lock state and khugepaged_pages_collapsed accounting checked
against the pre-patch code:

For collapse_scan_mm_slot: when collapse_test_exit_or_disable is true
in the old SCAN_PTE_MAPPED_HUGEPAGE branch, the old code went to
breakouterloop (mmap_read_unlock + skip counter).  New code returns
SCAN_ANY_PROCESS with mmap already unlocked inside the helper, so
mmap_locked=false causes collapse_scan_mm_slot to jump to
breakouterloop_mmap_lock (no double-unlock).  Correct.

For madvise_collapse: SCAN_ANY_PROCESS falls to the default case,
sets last_fail, and goes to out_maybelock which re-acquires mmap_lock
if needed.  Correct.

khugepaged_pages_collapsed: only incremented for is_khugepaged &&
SCAN_SUCCEED.  The SCAN_PMD_MAPPED -> SCAN_SUCCEED conversion inside
the helper preserves the original increment path.  Correct.

lock_dropped semantics: the file path always releases mmap before
collapse_scan_file, so *mmap_locked is false on return from
collapse_single_pmd in all file cases; the !mmap_locked check in
madvise_collapse is equivalent to the original unconditional set.
For the anonymous path, *mmap_locked is false only when
collapse_huge_page was called, matching the original.

The noted behavioral change (skipping VMA revalidation on writeback
retry) is safe: collapse_scan_file does not require mmap_lock, pgoff
was captured before the lock was released, and if the mapping changed
the scan will fail on page state independently.  The commit message
explicitly documents this.

Patches 2-4 are mechanical renames and constant introductions with
no behavioral change.  No issues found across the series.

Needs Work Introduce meminspect 🔗 Mukesh Ojha 25p
This series introduces meminspect, a mechanism that registers kernel memory regions into a static table for later inspection by drivers (e.g., crash dump, minidump). Patches 02-16 annotate existing kernel variables into that table using compile-time section macros or init-time API calls.
docs drivers include init init-mm kernel mm_init numa page_alloc percpu show_mem sparse swapfile
Author: Eugen Hristev <eugen.hristev@linaro.org>
         Mukesh Ojha <mukesh.ojha@oss.qualcomm.com>

[PATCH v2 00/25] Introduce meminspect

A few observations on the mm-touching patches follow.

--- [PATCH v2 03/25] mm/percpu: Annotate static information into
    meminspect ---

> diff --git a/mm/percpu.c b/mm/percpu.c
> --- a/mm/percpu.c
> +++ b/mm/percpu.c

[ ... ]

> +#endif	/* CONFIG_SMP */
>  
> +MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY(__per_cpu_offset);
>  /*
>   * pcpu_nr_pages - calculate total number of populated backing pages

The array __per_cpu_offset[NR_CPUS] is declared and defined inside the
#ifdef CONFIG_SMP block that ends at that exact #endif on the line just
above.  The MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY is placed after the #endif, meaning
it is compiled unconditionally.  On a UP (non-SMP) build __per_cpu_offset
does not exist, so this will produce a compile error.

The entry must be moved inside the CONFIG_SMP guard, e.g. placed directly
after the EXPORT_SYMBOL(__per_cpu_offset) line.

Furthermore, asm-generic/percpu.h guards the extern declaration with
#ifndef __per_cpu_offset, because some architectures define that symbol
as a preprocessor macro instead (arm64 does this for the KVM nVHE case).
To be safe the annotation should mirror that guard:

    #ifdef CONFIG_SMP
    #ifndef __per_cpu_offset
    MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY(__per_cpu_offset);
    #endif
    #endif

--- [PATCH v2 15/25] kallsyms: Annotate static information into
    meminspect ---

> diff --git a/kernel/kallsyms.c b/kernel/kallsyms.c
> --- a/kernel/kallsyms.c
> +++ b/kernel/kallsyms.c
> +MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY(kallsyms_num_syms);
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_offsets, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_names, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_token_table, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_token_index, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_markers, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(kallsyms_seqs_of_names, sizeof(void *));

The documentation for MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY describes the size argument
as the actual size of the region, "useful for arrays which do not have a
fixed size at compile time."  Using sizeof(void *) (8 bytes on 64-bit)
for tables like kallsyms_offsets, kallsyms_names, and kallsyms_token_table
-- which can be megabytes in size -- only registers the first 8 bytes of
each array.

If the intent is to record the runtime virtual address of each symbol so
a crash tool can apply KASLR correction against vmlinux, that should be
documented explicitly and the macro ought to be named something distinct
(e.g., MEMINSPECT_ADDR_ENTRY) to avoid confusion with uses like patch 08
where MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY(node_states) correctly captures the full
array via sizeof(node_states).

The same question applies to MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(swapper_pg_dir,
sizeof(void *)) in patch 13: is capturing 8 bytes of the PGD intentional,
or should the full page directory (one page, 4 KiB on most arches) be
registered?

Similarly for the text-section boundary symbols in patch 13:

> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(_sinittext, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(_einittext, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(_end, sizeof(void *));
> +MEMINSPECT_AREA_ENTRY(_text, sizeof(void *));

If these are meant solely to convey the address of each boundary (so a
crash tool can compute section ranges), sizeof(void *) bytes starting at
&_text is the first 8 bytes of kernel .text, not a pointer to it.
Please clarify the intended semantics, perhaps with a comment, so that
users of the API understand when sizeof(void *) is the right size to
pass.

--- [PATCH v2 12/25] kernel/configs: Register dynamic information
    into meminspect ---

> +	/* Register 8 bytes before and after, to catch the marker too */
> +	meminspect_lock_register_id_va(MEMINSPECT_ID_CONFIG,
> +				       (void *)&kernel_config_data - 8,
> +				       &kernel_config_data_end -
> +				       &kernel_config_data + 16);

The size arithmetic is correct: 8 bytes for "IKCFG_ST", the gz payload,
and 8 bytes for "IKCFG_ED", verified against the asm block in configs.c.

Two minor points:

1. ikconfig_init() is compiled only under #ifdef CONFIG_IKCONFIG_PROC,
   so the config data goes unregistered when CONFIG_IKCONFIG=y but
   CONFIG_IKCONFIG_PROC=n, even though the embedded data is present.
   Is that intentional?

2. The expression "(void *)&kernel_config_data - 8" relies on GCC's
   void* arithmetic extension (not standard C).  Prefer
   "(void *)((char *)&kernel_config_data - 8)" for clarity.

--- [PATCH v2 08/25] mm/page_alloc, [PATCH v2 09/25] mm/show_mem,
    [PATCH v2 10/25] mm/swapfile, [PATCH v2 13/25] mm/init-mm ---

The remaining mm/ patches (node_states, _totalram_pages, nr_swapfiles,
init_mm) are straightforward compile-time annotations that do not touch
any execution path.  Verified that:
- All annotated symbols exist at the point of annotation.
- MEMINSPECT_SIMPLE_ENTRY uses sizeof() of the actual object, which is
  correct for node_states (full nodemask_t array), _totalram_pages
  (atomic_long_t), nr_swapfiles (unsigned int), and init_mm (full
  struct mm_struct).
- No locking, control-flow, or refcount changes are introduced.

These hunks look fine modulo the sizeof(void *) design question raised
above for swapper_pg_dir.

Minor Issues ACPI: Add support for ACPI RAS2 feature table 🔗 <shiju.jose@huawei.com> 2p
This series adds a new ACPI RAS2 feature table driver and an auxiliary driver for RAS2 hardware-based memory scrubbing, including an extension to the EDAC scrub interface with a new 'enable_demand' attribute for on-demand scrub control.

Author: Shiju Jose <shiju.jose@huawei.com>

[PATCH v17 1/2] ACPI:RAS2: Add driver for the ACPI RAS2 feature table
[PATCH v17 2/2] ras: mem: Add ACPI RAS2 memory driver

Verified: bus.c placement is consistent with the void-return pattern
of acpi_viot_init(), acpi_hest_init(), acpi_debugger_init() and other
optional ACPI init calls in acpi_init().  The EDAC scrub enum extension
with SCRUB_ENABLE_DEMAND uses designated initializers throughout
scrub_create_desc() and scrub_attr_visible(), so the index shift is
automatically correct.  PCC_STATUS_CMD_COMPLETE (BIT(0) from pcc.h)
matches ACPI_RAS2_COMMAND_COMPLETE (1) from actbl2.h.  The ras2_sspcc
fields pcc_mrtt, pcc_mpar, deadline_us, last_cmd_cmpl_time,
last_mpar_reset, mpar_count mirror the CPPC driver's proven design.

> diff --git a/drivers/acpi/ras2.c b/drivers/acpi/ras2.c
> new file mode 100644
> +static int check_pcc_chan(struct ras2_sspcc *sspcc)
> +{
> +	struct acpi_ras2_shmem __iomem *gen_comm_base = sspcc->comm_addr;
> +	u32 cap_status;
> +	u16 status;
> +	int rc;
> +
> +	rc = readw_relaxed_poll_timeout(&gen_comm_base->status, status,
> +					status & PCC_STATUS_CMD_COMPLETE,
> +					PCC_MIN_POLL_USECS, sspcc->deadline_us);
> +	if (rc) {
> +		pr_warn("PCC ID: 0x%x: PCC check channel timeout for last command: 0x%x rc=%d\n",
> +			sspcc->pcc_id, sspcc->last_cmd, rc);
> +		return rc;
> +	}
> +
> +	if (status &
[... truncated ...]

The cap_status variable is declared as u32, which matches the
set_caps_status field (u32 at offset 44) in struct acpi_ras2_shmem
from actbl2.h.  The v7 changelog says "add read, clear and check
RAS2 set_cap_status outside if (status & PCC_STATUS_ERROR) check".
Can you confirm that set_caps_status is both read AND written back
to zero in the non-error path?  If the register is not cleared after
reading, firmware may see stale capability status on the next command.

Separately: actbl2.h defines ACPI_RAS2_STATUS as (0x1F<<3), covering
bits [7:3] of the status field, which carries the command completion
code (SUCCESS, NOT_VALID, BUSY, FAILED, INVALID_DATA, etc.).  Does
check_pcc_chan() decode these bits and return an error for non-SUCCESS
values, or is that left to per-command callers reading the parameter
block directly?

> +struct ras2_sspcc {
> +	struct mbox_client		mbox_client;
> +	struct pcc_mbox_chan		*pcc_chan;

[ ... ]

> +	bool				pcc_chnl_acq;
> +};

Does the mbox_client initializer set knows_txdone = true?  The CPPC
driver relies on this flag to signal that the client itself will call
mbox_client_txdone() after polling completion, rather than having the
mailbox framework do it autonomously.  Without knows_txdone = true on
a polled PCC channel the TX-done accounting can misfire.

> +#define RAS2_MAX_NUM_PCC_DESCS 100

The acpi_table_ras2.num_pcc_descs field is u16 (0..65535).  If the
table advertises more than 100 descriptors, is there a pr_warn() so
that admins on oversized platforms know descriptors are being skipped?

> diff --git a/drivers/acpi/bus.c b/drivers/acpi/bus.c
> +	acpi_ras2_init();
> +
>  	return 0;

Verified: acpi_init_pcc() is called at the top of acpi_init() before
acpi_bus_init(), so PCC is fully set up before acpi_ras2_init()
attempts pcc_mbox_request_channel().  Ordering is correct.

> diff --git a/drivers/edac/scrub.c b/drivers/edac/scrub.c

[ ... ]

Verified: scrub_dev_attr[], scrub_attrs[], and the loop bound in
scrub_create_desc() all use SCRUB_MAX_ATTRS symbolically, so adding
SCRUB_ENABLE_DEMAND to the enum automatically resizes all three.
The designated initializer syntax in dev_attr[] (e.g.
[SCRUB_ENABLE_BACKGROUND] = ...) guarantees the correct slot is
filled regardless of the enum value shift.  The scrub_attr_visible()
switch default returns 0 for unknown attr_id, so a missing case for
SCRUB_ENABLE_DEMAND would hide the attribute; please double-check the
switch is updated.

  • [PATCH v17 1/2] ACPI:RAS2: Add driver for the ACPI RAS2 feature table
  • [PATCH v17 2/2] ras: mem: Add ACPI RAS2 memory driver
Minor Issues slab: support memoryless nodes with sheaves 🔗 "Vlastimil Babka (SUSE)" 3p
Three-patch series decoupling barn storage from kmem_cache_node, extending barn allocation to all online nodes including memoryless ones, and adapting the free-path locality check so CPUs on memoryless nodes can use the percpu-sheaf fast path instead of always falling to the slowpath.
slab slub
From: reviewer
Subject: Re: [PATCH 0/3] slab: support memoryless nodes with sheaves

Overall the series is logically sound and addresses a real performance
problem.  A few questions and observations below.

--- [PATCH 1/3] slab: decouple pointer to barn from kmem_cache_node ---

> +struct kmem_cache_per_node_ptrs {
> +	struct node_barn *barn;
> +	struct kmem_cache_node *node;
> +};

> -	struct kmem_cache_node *node[MAX_NUMNODES];
> +	struct kmem_cache_per_node_ptrs per_node[MAX_NUMNODES];

The diff was truncated before reaching kmem_cache_init(), so I cannot
verify the create_boot_cache() call for kmem_cache was updated.  Today
it reads:

  create_boot_cache(kmem_cache, "kmem_cache",
          offsetof(struct kmem_cache, node) +
                  nr_node_ids * sizeof(struct kmem_cache_node *), ...)

After the rename the field is per_node and each element is
struct kmem_cache_per_node_ptrs (two pointers, not one), so the size
calculation must become:

  offsetof(struct kmem_cache, per_node) +
          nr_node_ids * sizeof(struct kmem_cache_per_node_ptrs)

Did that update land in the truncated portion?  An undersized boot
cache for kmem_cache would be a serious boot-time corruption.

Similarly, slab_mem_going_online_callback() calls
init_kmem_cache_node(n, barn) and assigns s->node[nid]; both must be
converted.  The compile would catch the wrong signature, but can you
confirm the barn allocation path in that function still works after
the restructuring?

> -static void
> -init_kmem_cache_node(struct kmem_cache_node *n, struct node_barn *barn)
> +init_kmem_cache_node(struct kmem_cache_node *n)
>  {
> -	n->barn = barn;
> -	if (barn)
> -		barn_init(barn);
>  }

Verified: every visible barn_init() call site in the diff is followed
immediately by s->per_node[node].barn = barn before any consumer can
race with it.  The error paths in init_kmem_cache_nodes() kfree the
barn before returning 0, symmetric with the allocation.

> -	for_each_kmem_cache_node(s, node, n) {
> -		if (n->barn) {
> +	for_each_node(node) {
> +		struct node_barn *barn = get_barn_node(s, node);
>  		...
> +	for_each_kmem_cache_node(s, node, n) {
> +		s->per_node[node].node = NULL;

The two-pass approach (barns first, then kmem_cache_nodes) is correct
since barns are now independent of kmem_cache_node lifetime.  No use-
after-free: barn pointers are NULLed before the kmem_cache_node is
freed, and nothing reads per_node[].barn after free_kmem_cache_nodes()
returns.

--- [PATCH 2/3] slab: create barns for online memoryless nodes ---

> +static int slub_cpu_setup(unsigned int cpu)
> +{
> +	int nid = cpu_to_node(cpu);
> +	...
> +	if (node_isset(nid, slab_barn_nodes))
> +		return 0;
> +
> +	mutex_lock(&slab_mutex);
> +
> +	if (node_isset(nid, slab_barn_nodes))
> +		goto out;

The lockless pre-check is justified by the comment that nid bits are
never cleared from slab_barn_nodes.  I checked the entire file and
confirmed there is no node_clear() on slab_barn_nodes anywhere, so
the double-check pattern is safe.

> +		if (!cache_has_sheaves(s) || get_barn_node(s, nid))
> +			continue;

If a previous slub_cpu_setup() for the same nid failed partway through
slab_caches, some caches already have barns but slab_barn_nodes is not
set.  The next CPU hotplug event for the same nid will correctly skip
those already-allocated barns and allocate only the remaining ones.
No barn leak on partial failure: free_kmem_cache_nodes() iterates
for_each_node() and frees all per_node[].barn entries.

> -		rcu_sheaf->node = numa_mem_id();
> +		rcu_sheaf->node = numa_node_id();

Consistent with get_barn() switching from numa_mem_id() to
numa_node_id() in patch 1: the sheaf is returned to the barn of the
cpu's actual node rather than the nearest memory node.  Correct.

> +	for_each_online_node(node)
> +		node_set(node, slab_barn_nodes);

> -	for_each_node_mask(node, slab_nodes) {
> +	for_each_node_mask(node, slab_barn_nodes) {
>  		struct node_barn *barn;
>  		barn = kmalloc_node(sizeof(*barn), GFP_KERNEL, node);

bootstrap_cache_sheaves() now allocates barns for all online nodes
(not just memory nodes) during init.  slab_barn_nodes is fully
populated before this call, so no barns are missed.

--- [PATCH 3/3] slab: free remote objects to sheaves on memoryless nodes ---

> +static __always_inline bool can_free_to_pcs(struct slab *slab)
> +{
> +	...
> +#else
> +	numa_node = numa_node_id();
> +
> +	if (likely(slab_node == numa_node))
> +		goto check_pfmemalloc;
> +
> +	if (unlikely(!node_isset(numa_node, slab_nodes)))
> +		goto check_pfmemalloc;
> +#endif

The !CONFIG_HAVE_MEMORYLESS_NODES branch reads slab_nodes locklessly
in the hot free path.  slab_nodes is only ever grown (bits are set on
node-online, never cleared), so a stale read can at worst cause a
transient missed optimization, not a correctness problem.

One incidental behavior change worth noting: kfree_nolock() previously
did NOT check slab_test_pfmemalloc() before calling free_to_pcs(),
while slab_free() did.  can_free_to_pcs() adds that check uniformly
via the check_pfmemalloc label, so pfmemalloc objects in kfree_nolock()
now go to defer_free() instead of the percpu sheaves.  This closes a
pre-existing asymmetry and looks like a welcome fix, but it is worth
calling out explicitly in the commit message.

> -	int node = numa_mem_id();
>  next_remote_batch:
>  	while (i < size) {
>  		...
> -		if (unlikely((IS_ENABLED(CONFIG_NUMA) && slab_nid(slab) != node)
> -			     || slab_test_pfmemalloc(slab))) {
> +		if (unlikely(!can_free_to_pcs(slab))) {

The old code cached node = numa_mem_id() once per invocation of
free_to_pcs_bulk().  The new code calls numa_node_id() per object.
If the thread migrates between iterations the routing decision changes
per object; that is harmless since each object ends up in the barn for
the current cpu's node.  The next_remote_batch re-entry is correct
because i retains its last value and can_free_to_pcs() is stateless.

Minor Issues mm/zswap, zsmalloc: Per-memcg-lruvec zswap accounting 🔗 Joshua Hahn 11p
This series moves per-memcg zswap accounting from the consumer layer (zswap/zram) into zsmalloc by adding a per-zspage array of obj_cgroup pointers, redirecting zswap_entry to look up the objcg from the zspage, and finally migrating charging and lifetime management entirely into zsmalloc. mm/zswap, zsmalloc: Per-memcg-lruvec zswap accounting

I verified: the locking pattern in zs_lookup_objcg (read_lock
pool->lock, acquire zspage_read_lock, then release pool->lock) is
consistent with zs_obj_write, zs_obj_read_begin, and zs_obj_read_sg_begin,
so migration cannot move pages under a reader.  alloc_zspage's goto-err
path in patch 4 correctly frees objcgs before cache_free_zspage.
migrate_zspage in patch 5 correctly clears the source slot via
zs_migrate_objcg before obj_free runs, so patch 7's uncharge-on-free
does not fire for migrated objects.  A few things to discuss:

> diff --git a/mm/zsmalloc.c b/mm/zsmalloc.c
> +struct obj_cgroup *zs_lookup_objcg(struct zs_pool *pool,
> +				     unsigned long handle)
> +{
> +	read_lock(&pool->lock);
> +	obj = handle_to_obj(handle);
> +	obj_to_location(obj, &zpdesc, &obj_idx);
> +	zspage = get_zspage(zpdesc);
> +	zspage_read_lock(zspage);
> +	read_unlock(&pool->lock);
> +	objcg = zspage->objcgs[obj_idx];
> +	zspage_read_unlock(zspage);
> +	return objcg;
> +}

The function is declared in zsmalloc.h as part of the public API, but
the diff does not show EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(zs_lookup_objcg).  Every other
zs_* public function in this file has one.  CONFIG_ZSWAP is bool so
there is no immediate link failure, but zsmalloc is used by module
consumers (zram) and the convention should be consistent.  Is the
export intentionally absent?

> diff --git a/mm/zswap.c b/mm/zswap.c

[ ... ]

> +	objcg = zs_lookup_objcg(entry->pool->zs_pool, entry->handle);
> +	if (objcg)
> +		count_objcg_events(objcg, ZSWPWB, 1);
>  	zswap_entry_free(entry);

zswap_entry_free calls zs_lookup_objcg again for the same handle to
pass the objcg into zswap_lru_del.  That is two round trips through
read_lock(pool->lock) and zspage_read_lock for the same entry in the
writeback path.  Could the objcg resolved here be threaded into
zswap_entry_free (or a __zswap_entry_free variant that accepts a
pre-resolved objcg) to avoid the redundant lookup?  The same pattern
appears in zswap_load, where the ZSWPIN event is counted using
entry->objcg (patch 6 converts this to a zs_lookup_objcg call) and
then zswap_entry_free is called immediately after, triggering a
second lookup.

> diff --git a/mm/zsmalloc.c b/mm/zsmalloc.c
> +	if (zspage->pool->memcg_aware)
> +		zspage->objcgs[f_objidx] = NULL;

This is in obj_free (patch 5).  In the migrate_zspage path,
zs_migrate_objcg already sets src_zspage->objcgs[s_idx] = NULL before
obj_free is called on the source slot, so this write is redundant
during migration.  It is harmless, but a comment noting that the slot
is already NULL in the migration caller, and that the NULL here is
what prevents patch 7's uncharge-on-free from firing for the moved
object, would help future readers.

[ patch 7: obj_cgroup charging and lifetime move to zsmalloc ]

Patch 7 changes the charge unit from entry->length (actual compressed
bytes) to class->size (the slot size).  The commit message calls this
out as intentional -- the slot is exclusively consumed by the object
regardless of how much of it is used.  That said, class->size can be
noticeably larger than entry->length due to size-class rounding, which
inflates MEMCG_ZSWAP_B compared to the pre-series value and could push
a cgroup over its zswap limit sooner on workloads with good compression
ratios.  Could you quantify the worst-case inflation in the commit
message, or at minimum spell out the new semantic explicitly so that
users monitoring per-cgroup zswap stats know what changed?

> diff --git a/include/linux/zsmalloc.h b/include/linux/zsmalloc.h
> +struct obj_cgroup *zs_lookup_objcg(struct zs_pool *pool,
> +				    unsigned long handle);

The function returns a bare pointer with no reference taken.  Its
safety depends on the caller holding an external reference to the
objcg -- in patches 5+6 via the obj_cgroup_get in zswap_store_page,
and after patch 7 via zsmalloc's internal get in zs_obj_write.  A
brief kerneldoc comment stating that the pointer is only valid while
the caller's reference is live (i.e. before zs_free is called for the
same handle) would prevent a future caller from accidentally using the
return value after zs_free drops the last ref.

Minor Issues kho: add support for deferred struct page init 🔗 Michal Clapinski 2p
This two-patch series makes KHO compatible with CONFIG_DEFERRED_STRUCT_PAGE_INIT by initializing kho scratch and preserved struct pages early (before any code writes metadata to them) and guarding the deferred-init paths from re-initializing or clobbering the migratetype of pages that KHO already set up.
include kernel memblock mm_init
On [PATCH v6 1/2] kho: fix deferred init of kho scratch
On [PATCH v6 2/2] kho: make preserved pages compatible with deferred
struct page init

The overall design is correct.  A few things worth double-checking
below.

> +bool pfn_is_kho_scratch(unsigned long pfn)
> +{
> +	unsigned int i;
> +	phys_addr_t scratch_start, scratch_end, phys = __pfn_to_phys(pfn);
> +
> +	for (i = 0; i < kho_scratch_cnt; i++) {
> +		scratch_start = kho_scratch[i].addr;
> +		scratch_end = kho_scratch[i].addr + kho_scratch[i].size;
> +
> +		if (scratch_start <= phys && phys < scratch_end)
> +			return true;
> +	}
> +
> +	return false;
> +}
> +EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL(pfn_is_kho_scratch);

The only in-tree caller is mm/mm_init.c, which is built into vmlinux;
EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL is not needed for that linkage.  Loadable modules
only run after page_alloc_init_late() completes and the deferred-pages
static branch is permanently disabled, so there is no realistic module
use case for this symbol.  Is the export intentional?

I verified the call-site ordering: kho_memory_init() populates
kho_scratch[] and kho_scratch_cnt before memblock_free_all() →
memmap_init_reserved_pages() → reserve_bootmem_region(), so
kho_scratch[] is valid when pfn_is_kho_scratch() is first called.

> +static void __init kho_init_scratch_pages(void)
> +{
> +	if (!IS_ENABLED(CONFIG_DEFERRED_STRUCT_PAGE_INIT))
> +		return;
> +
> +	for (int i = 0; i < kho_scratch_cnt; i++) {
> +		unsigned long pfn = PFN_DOWN(kho_scratch[i].addr);
> +		unsigned long end_pfn = PFN_UP(kho_scratch[i].addr +
> +					       kho_scratch[i].size);
> +		int nid = early_pfn_to_nid(pfn);
> +
> +		for (; pfn < end_pfn; pfn++)
> +			init_deferred_page(pfn, nid);
> +	}
> +}

nid is derived once from the first PFN of each kho_scratch entry and
reused for the entire region.  The per-node entries are fine because
memblock_alloc_range_nid() constrains them to a single node.  But the
global scratch uses memblock_phys_alloc() without a node constraint.
If that allocation straddles a NUMA node boundary, pages belonging to
the second node are passed the wrong nid.

__init_page_from_nid() walks node_zones[] of the supplied pgdat looking
for a zone that spans pfn.  If no zone matches (because pfn belongs to
a different node), zid exits the loop at MAX_NR_ZONES and
__init_single_page() is called with an out-of-range zone index.

The old memmap_init_kho_scratch_pages() used __for_each_mem_range()
with a per-region &nid output, which handled this correctly.  Could
you either call early_pfn_to_nid() per PFN inside the inner loop, or
iterate memblock regions within each kho_scratch entry and obtain nid
per sub-region?

[ ... ]

Same single-nid issue as in kho_init_scratch_pages(): nid is derived

Needs Work Demotion cleanup and fixes 🔗 Alexandre Ghiti 4p
Four-patch series that moves demotion helpers into memory-tiers.c, renames node_get_allowed_targets(), and fixes two GFP flag bugs (wrong order of GFP_TRANSHUGE vs ~__GFP_RECLAIM, and htlb_modify_alloc_mask discarding the caller's reclaim policy). Patches 2-4 are correct; patch 1 introduces a regression in alloc_demote_folio that was already fixed in vmscan.c.
include memory-tiers migrate vmscan
Alexandre Ghiti &lt;alex@ghiti.fr&gt;

mm: Move demotion related functions in memory-tiers.c

On this mm-new base, vmscan.c already carries a different
implementation of alloc_demote_folio that makes a full struct copy
to avoid mutating the shared mtc:

    target_nid_mtc = *mtc;
    target_nid_mtc.nmask = NULL;
    target_nid_mtc.gfp_mask |= __GFP_THISNODE;
    dst = alloc_migration_target(src, (unsigned long)&target_nid_mtc);
    if (dst)
        return dst;

    return alloc_migration_target(src, (unsigned long)mtc);

The new alloc_demote_folio added to memory-tiers.c, however, reverts
to the old in-place save/restore pattern:

> +static struct folio *alloc_demote_folio(struct folio *src,
> +					unsigned long private)
> +{
> +	struct folio *dst;
> +	nodemask_t *allowed_mask;
> +	struct migration_target_control *mtc;
> +
> +	mtc = (struct migration_target_control *)private;
> +
> +	allowed_mask = mtc->nmask;
> +	mtc->nmask = NULL;
> +	mtc->gfp_mask |= __GFP_THISNODE;
> +	dst = alloc_migration_target(src, (unsigned long)mtc);
> +	if (dst)
> +		return dst;
> +
> +	mtc->gfp_mask &= ~__GFP_THISNODE;
> +	mtc->nmask = allowed_mask;
> +
> +	return alloc_migration_target(src, (unsigned long)mtc);
> +}

The mtc struct is allocated in mt_demote_folios() and the same
pointer is passed as `private` to every get_new_folio callback
invocation inside migrate_pages(). When the THISNODE allocation
succeeds on the first try for a folio, the function returns early
without restoring mtc->nmask or clearing __GFP_THISNODE. For every
subsequent folio in the list:

  - allowed_mask is saved as NULL (mtc->nmask was not restored
    after the previous successful call)
  - if THISNODE then fails for that folio, the fallback path sets
    mtc->nmask back to that saved NULL, so the second
    alloc_migration_target() call runs with nmask==NULL

A NULL nmask means no node restriction at all, so allocation can
go to any NUMA node including the source node, violating the
demotion invariant. The copy approach already in vmscan.c avoids
this because each callback operates on its own local copy and the
shared mtc is never modified. Can the new code adopt the same
struct-copy pattern?

Separately: this patch does not appear to apply cleanly to the
mm-new tree used as the base. vmscan.c already has the copy
implementation above, not the save/restore form shown in the
diff's removal hunks. Is the series based on a different mm-new
tip?

[ ... ]

--- [PATCH 3/4] mm: Fix demotion gfp by clearing GFP_RECLAIM
--- after setting GFP_TRANSHUGE ---

GFP_TRANSHUGE == GFP_TRANSHUGE_LIGHT | __GFP_DIRECT_RECLAIM, so
ORing GFP_TRANSHUGE after clearing __GFP_RECLAIM re-enables direct
reclaim. Reordering fixes this correctly.

> +		gfp_mask |= GFP_TRANSHUGE;
>  		gfp_mask &= ~__GFP_RECLAIM;

Fix is correct.

--- [PATCH 4/4] mm: Fix demotion gfp by preserving initial gfp
--- reclaim policy ---

htlb_modify_alloc_mask() starts from htlb_alloc_mask() which
includes GFP_HIGHUSER_MOVABLE (and thus __GFP_RECLAIM), forwarding
only __GFP_THISNODE and __GFP_NOWARN from the caller. The demotion
mtc.gfp_mask has __GFP_RECLAIM cleared, but htlb_modify_alloc_mask
silently re-enables it.

> +		gfp_mask = (gfp_mask & ~__GFP_RECLAIM) | (gfp_entry & __GFP_RECLAIM);

Since gfp_entry carries the original mtc->gfp_mask with
__GFP_RECLAIM cleared, gfp_entry & __GFP_RECLAIM == 0, so this
correctly strips reclaim bits from the htlb mask. Fix is correct.

Needs Discussion mm: switch deferred split shrinker to list_lru 🔗 Johannes Weiner 1p
Switches the deferred split THP shrinker from a custom per-memcg linked list (struct deferred_split embedded in mem_cgroup and pglist_data) to a generic list_lru, gaining proper per-node per-cgroup intersection tracking and eliminating the shrinker-bit imprecision that caused cross-node splitting. New caller-side locking helpers (list_lru_lock/unlock, __list_lru_add/del) allow atomically coupling the folio_test_partially_mapped() flag with list membership.
huge_memory include internal khugepaged list_lru memcontrol memory mm_init
Johannes Weiner <hannes@cmpxchg.org>

mm: switch deferred split shrinker to list_lru

The overall design is sound and addresses a real problem.  I have one
concrete question about the dying-memcg race, and a smaller question
about node-level accounting in the new caller-locked path.

> diff --git a/include/linux/list_lru.h b/include/linux/list_lru.h

[ ... ]

> +struct list_lru_one *list_lru_lock(struct list_lru *lru, int nid,
> +				   struct mem_cgroup *memcg);
> +void list_lru_unlock(struct list_lru_one *l);
> +struct list_lru_one *list_lru_lock_irqsave(struct list_lru *lru, int nid,
> +					   struct mem_cgroup *memcg,
> +					   unsigned long *irq_flags);
> + * Return: the locked list_lru_one, or NULL on failure

The existing lock_list_lru_of_memcg() has two modes.  With
skip_empty=false it falls back to the parent memcg (and fires
VM_WARN_ON if the cgroup is not dying).  With skip_empty=true it
returns NULL.  The "or NULL on failure" wording implies list_lru_lock()
and list_lru_lock_irqsave() use skip_empty=true.

The old folio_split_queue_lock_irqsave() had an explicit dying-memcg
retry loop that guaranteed callers always landed on a live queue:

  retry:
    queue = memcg_split_queue(nid, memcg);
    spin_lock_irqsave(&queue->split_queue_lock, *flags);
    if (unlikely(memcg_is_dying(memcg))) {
        spin_unlock_irqrestore(...);
        memcg = parent_mem_cgroup(memcg);
        goto retry;
    }

In the new code, after memcg_reparent_list_lrus() runs:
  1. The mlru is removed from the XArray (xas_store NULL).
  2. memcg_reparent_list_lru_one() splices every per-node
     src->list into the parent dst->list and sets
     src->nr_items = LONG_MIN.
  3. kvfree_rcu(mlru, rcu) schedules the free.

At that point folio->_deferred_list is non-empty (it now lives on
the parent's list), but folio_memcg() still points at the dying
cgroup -- the charge is released only after unqueue, per the existing
comment above __folio_unqueue_deferred_split().

If __folio_unqueue_deferred_split() calls list_lru_lock_irqsave()
with that dying memcg, xa_load() will return NULL (once the RCU
grace period passes) or lock_list_lru() will return false
(nr_items == LONG_MIN), so list_lru_lock_irqsave() returns NULL.
If the caller treats NULL as "nothing to do", the folio is freed
with _deferred_list still linked into the parent's list_lru_one.
A subsequent deferred_split_scan() walk of the parent list then
reaches freed memory.

The same concern applies to split_huge_page_to_list_to_order(),
which acquires the deferred queue lock before folio_ref_freeze() to
exclude the scan from touching _refcount.  If list_lru_lock_irqsave()
returns NULL there (dying memcg, slot already reparented), the split
proceeds while the folio remains linked in the parent's list with
stale pointers.

How does the new code handle this case?  Does list_lru_lock_irqsave()
fall back to the parent when the slot is dead (skip_empty=false),
matching the old retry loop?  Or does the unqueue path use
list_lru_del() directly (which uses skip_empty=false) and handle
the flag separately?

> +bool __list_lru_add(struct list_lru *lru, struct list_lru_one *l,
> +		    struct list_head *item, int nid,
> +		    struct mem_cgroup *memcg);
> +bool __list_lru_del(struct list_lru *lru, struct list_lru_one *l,
> +		    struct list_head *item, int nid);

The standard list_lru_del() decrements both l->nr_items (under the
sublist spinlock) and nlru->nr_items (atomic, outside the lock).
__list_lru_del() is called with the lock already held by the caller.
Does it also perform atomic_long_dec on nlru->nr_items, or is the
caller expected to do it?  If neither does, list_lru_count_node() --
used by deferred_split_count() -- will undercount after every
caller-locked removal.

[ ... ]

Checked:
- memcg_init_list_lru_one() allocates space for all nr_node_ids
  nodes in one allocation, confirming the commit message claim that
  migration between nodes needs no special care.
- list_lru_add() calls set_shrinker_bit when nr_items goes 0->1,
  replacing the open-coded set_shrinker_bit in the old
  deferred_split_folio().  Correct.
- memcg_reparent_list_lrus() in mem_cgroup_css_offline() subsumes
  the explicit reparent_deferred_split_queue() call.  The ordering
  relative to memcg_reparent_objcgs() is preserved per the comment.
- The folio_order <= 1 early return and swapcache exclusion in
  deferred_split_folio() are orthogonal to the queue change and
  carry over correctly.
Looks Good slab: remove alloc_full_sheaf() 🔗 "Vlastimil Babka (SUSE)" 1p
The patch removes alloc_full_sheaf() by inlining its alloc_empty_sheaf()+refill_sheaf() sequence directly into __pcs_replace_empty_main(), unifying the two previously separate code paths (empty!=NULL and empty==NULL) into one. No functional change.

> [PATCH] slab: remove alloc_full_sheaf()

Reviewed-by: <reviewer>

I traced all four combinations of (empty/!empty) x (refill
succeeds/fails) through both the old and new code.

alloc_full_sheaf() appeared before its definition in the file. With

after sheaf_flush_unused(), so no forward declaration is required.

> -	if (empty) {
> -		if (!refill_sheaf(s, empty, gfp | __GFP_NOMEMALLOC | __GFP_NOWARN)) {

> -		} else {

> -			free_empty_sheaf(s, empty);

> +		if (!empty)
> +			return NULL;
> +	}
> +
> +	if (refill_sheaf(s, empty, gfp | __GFP_NOMEMALLOC | __GFP_NOWARN)) {
> +		sheaf_flush_unused(s, empty);
> +		free_empty_sheaf(s, empty);
> +		return NULL;
> +	}
> +

> +	empty = NULL;

Verified equivalence for all four paths:

1. empty != NULL, refill succeeds: old sets full=empty, new sets
   full=empty. Identical.

2. empty != NULL, refill fails: both call sheaf_flush_unused() +
   free_empty_sheaf() and return NULL. Whether empty came from
   pcs->spare (already detached before this point) or from
   barn_get_empty_sheaf(), the cleanup is correct in both cases.

3. empty == NULL, refill of freshly allocated sheaf succeeds: GFP
   flags are preserved -- alloc_empty_sheaf(s, gfp) without
   __GFP_NOMEMALLOC, refill_sheaf(..., gfp|__GFP_NOMEMALLOC|
   __GFP_NOWARN) -- identical to what alloc_full_sheaf() did
   internally.

4. empty == NULL, refill fails: both call sheaf_flush_unused() +
   free_empty_sheaf() and return NULL. Identical cleanup.

The barn_put label and subsequent pcs->main/spare placement logic are
untouched and operate on `full` as before.

The updated comment is accurate: after this refactor there is no case
where an empty sheaf is returned to the barn from this function; only
full sheaves or nothing reach barn_put_full_sheaf().

Looks good to me.

Looks Good slab: fix memory leak when refill_sheaf() fails 🔗 Qing Wang 1p
refill_sheaf() can return -ENOMEM after partially filling a sheaf (sheaf->size > 0), but alloc_full_sheaf() and __pcs_replace_empty_main() called free_empty_sheaf() directly on failure, which only kfree()s the sheaf struct without releasing the objects in sheaf->objects[], leaking them. The patch fixes this by calling sheaf_flush_unused() before free_empty_sheaf() in both failure paths, matching the pattern already used in all other error paths in the file.
slub
Author: Qing Wang <wangqing7171@gmail.com>

slab: fix memory leak when refill_sheaf() fails

Verified the bug: refill_sheaf() updates sheaf->size with however many
objects it managed to allocate before returning -ENOMEM, so sheaf->size
can be > 0 on failure. free_empty_sheaf() only does kfree(sheaf), so
the partially allocated objects were lost.

> diff --git a/mm/slub.c b/mm/slub.c

> +static void sheaf_flush_unused(struct kmem_cache *s, struct slab_sheaf *sheaf);

Forward declaration is necessary: alloc_full_sheaf() is defined before
sheaf_flush_unused() in the file. This is the right approach.

> @@ -2837,6 +2839,7 @@ static struct slab_sheaf *alloc_full_sheaf(...

Checked: alloc_full_sheaf() holds no lock itself. sheaf_flush_unused()
calls __kmem_cache_free_bulk(), consistent with every other error path

>  			free_empty_sheaf(s, empty);

Checked: local_unlock(&s->cpu_sheaves->lock) is called before this
branch, so no lock is held here. Correct.

Also checked that the new WARN_ON(sheaf->size > 0) in free_empty_sheaf()
does not trigger on any pre-existing caller:
- The empty_list loop in the barn flush iterates barn->sheaves_empty,
  which holds sheaves with size == 0 by construction.

  if (!WARN_ON(pcs->main->size)), reaching free_empty_sheaf() only
  when size == 0.
- All other callers already precede free_empty_sheaf() with

The fix is correct and complete.

Needs Work record non-slab shrinkers for non-root memcgs when kmem is disabled 🔗 Haifeng Xu 4p
This series optimizes memcg shrinker_info allocation under cgroup_memory_nokmem by introducing a second IDR (shrinker_nonslab_idr) so non-root memcgs only track non-slab shrinkers; however the diff is truncated and the most critical path -- the shrinker IDR lookup in shrink_slab_memcg() -- cannot be verified, and reparent_shrinker_deferred() has an id-scheme mismatch that would corrupt deferred work accounting when reparenting to root.
huge_memory include shrinker
Haifeng Xu <haifeng.xu@shopee.com>

mm: shrinker: record non-slab shrinkers for non-root memcgs when kmem
is disabled (V3, 4 patches)

The optimization goal is clear and the performance win is substantial.
The two-IDR design is conceptually reasonable.  Issues below.


--- [PATCH V3 3/4] mm: shrinker: optimize the allocation of
    shrinker_info when setting cgroup_memory_nokmem ---

> diff --git a/mm/shrinker.c b/mm/shrinker.c

[ ... ]

> +static DEFINE_IDR(shrinker_nonslab_idr);
> +
>  static int shrinker_memcg_alloc(struct shrinker *shrinker)
>  {
>  	int id, ret = -ENOMEM;
> +	bool kmem_online;
>
>  	if (mem_cgroup_disabled())
>  		return -ENOSYS;
>
> +	kmem_online = memcg_kmem_online();
>  	mutex_lock(&shrinker_mutex);

The V3 changelog says "read shrinker_nonslab_nr_max and shrinker_nr_max
after acquiring shrinker_mutex", but kmem_online is sampled before the
lock.  If cgroup_memory_nokmem transitions between the read and the
lock, expand_shrinker_info() gets stale full/root flags and expands all
non-root memcgs for a shrinker that should only expand root.  In
practice this is likely a one-time boot decision, but a comment
explaining the assumption would help.

The base code has:

    if (mem_cgroup_kmem_disabled() && !(shrinker->flags & SHRINKER_NONSLAB))
        return -ENOSYS;

This early return is removed by the patch, so non-NONSLAB slab
shrinkers now succeed through shrinker_memcg_alloc() and become
SHRINKER_MEMCG_AWARE even when kmem is disabled.  Previously they fell
through to non_memcg: in shrinker_alloc() and used shrinker->nr_deferred
for all accounting.  After the patch the global shrink path for root
memcg calls xchg_nr_deferred_memcg() with root_mem_cgroup instead of
the per-shrinker nr_deferred[].  Is this behavioural change intentional
and tested?

[ ... ]

> +	shrinker->nonslab_id = -1;
> +	if (!kmem_online && shrinker->flags & SHRINKER_NONSLAB) {
> +		int nonslab_id;
> +
> +		nonslab_id = idr_alloc(&shrinker_nonslab_idr, shrinker,
> +				       0, 0, GFP_KERNEL);

This introduces two independent ID spaces: shrinker_idr (shrinker->id)
for all memcgs and shrinker_nonslab_idr (shrinker->nonslab_id) for
non-root memcgs when kmem is disabled.  The non-root memcg bitmap then
stores nonslab_id as the bit position via shrinker_id(memcg, shrinker).

For this scheme to be correct, shrink_slab_memcg() must use
shrinker_nonslab_idr when doing the shrinker lookup for non-root memcgs
with kmem disabled.  The base code at the lookup site reads:

    shrinker_id = calc_shrinker_id(index, offset);
    ...
    shrinker = idr_find(&shrinker_idr, shrinker_id);

When kmem is disabled, shrinker_id here is actually a nonslab_id from
shrinker_nonslab_idr.  Passing it to shrinker_idr finds the wrong
shrinker (or NULL if the slot is empty), which would either invoke the
wrong ->scan_objects callback or silently clear the bit and skip
shrinking.

The diff is truncated and the body of shrink_slab_memcg() after patch 3
is not visible.  Could you resend with the full hunk, or at least
explain whether shrink_slab_memcg() switches to shrinker_nonslab_idr
when !memcg_kmem_online()?

[ ... ]

> +static int expand_shrinker_info(int new_id, bool full, bool root)

The bool pair (full, root) encodes three states and the fourth
combination (full=true, root=true) is invalid but not guarded.  Could
this be replaced with an enum to make the three cases explicit and
prevent a future caller from passing an ill-formed combination?

[ ... ]

reparent_shrinker_deferred() concern:

The current (unpatched) reparent_shrinker_deferred() copies nr_deferred
values from child to parent by raw index/offset, assuming both use the
same ID scheme.  After this patch:

  - non-root child: unit[index][offset] encodes nonslab_id
  - root parent:    unit[index][offset] encodes shrinker->id

When a non-root memcg is destroyed and reparented to root_mem_cgroup,
the deferred count at nonslab_id position is added into root's slot at
the same index/offset.  That slot in root's shrinker_info corresponds
to shrinker_id == nonslab_id, which is a completely different shrinker.
This matters because the global shrink path calls xchg_nr_deferred_memcg()
with root_mem_cgroup for MEMCG_AWARE shrinkers, so the corrupted slot
will affect deferred work accounting for whichever unrelated shrinker
occupies shrinker_id == nonslab_id in shrinker_idr.

Does the truncated portion of patch 3 modify reparent_shrinker_deferred()
to translate between the two ID schemes when parent is root_mem_cgroup?


--- [PATCH V3 4/4] mm: shrinker: remove unnecessary check in
    shrink_slab_memcg() ---

> -			/* Call non-slab shrinkers even though kmem is disabled */
> -			if (!memcg_kmem_online() &&
> -			    !(shrinker->flags & SHRINKER_NONSLAB))
> -				continue;

This removal is correct IF the non-root memcg bitmap exclusively holds
nonslab_id-indexed bits for SHRINKER_NONSLAB shrinkers, so that a slab
shrinker bit can never appear there.  That invariant holds if the IDR
lookup in shrink_slab_memcg() is switched to shrinker_nonslab_idr for
the nokmem path.  Patch 4 is therefore correct conditional on patch 3
being complete -- which cannot be verified from the truncated diff.
