Minor Issues selftest: memcg: Skip memcg_sock test if address family not supported 🔗 Waiman Long 1p
The patch adds a write(ctl_fd, &errno, sizeof(errno)) in tcp_server() when socket() fails, then checks for EAFNOSUPPORT in test_memcg_sock() to return KSFT_SKIP instead of KSFT_FAIL when IPv6 is not available on the system.
tests
On Wed, Mar 17 2026, Waiman Long wrote:
> selftest: memcg: Skip memcg_sock test if address family not supported

The overall approach is correct: pass errno back over the control pipe
and let the parent decide whether to skip.  I verified the pipe
protocol (write int in server, read int in parent), the existing
EADDRINUSE retry pattern that it follows, and that cg_destroy() is not
blocked because the server process has already called do_exit() and
been removed from the cgroup by the time goto cleanup runs.

A couple of things worth raising:

> diff --git a/tools/testing/selftests/cgroup/test_memcontrol.c b/...
[ ... ]
> +	if (sk < 0) {
> +		/* Pass back errno to the ctl_fd */
> +		write(ctl_fd, &errno, sizeof(errno));
> +		return ret;
> +	}

Passing &errno as the write buffer is consistent with the existing
bind() failure path just below, which already does
write(ctl_fd, &errno, sizeof(errno)).  No issue here.

> +		/* Skip if address family not supported by protocol */
> +		if (err == EAFNOSUPPORT) {
> +			ret = KSFT_SKIP;
> +			goto cleanup;
> +		}

The commit message says the test fails when IPv6 is "not configured to
support SOCK_STREAM".  In that case socket(AF_INET6, SOCK_STREAM, 0)
may return EPROTONOSUPPORT rather than EAFNOSUPPORT, depending on how
the kernel was configured.  Should EPROTONOSUPPORT also be treated as
a skip condition here, or is the intent limited to the case where the
AF_INET6 family itself is absent (CONFIG_IPV6=n)?

Also, when EAFNOSUPPORT causes goto cleanup inside the bind_retries
loop, there is no waitpid(pid) before cg_destroy().  The child has
already exited at that point (it returned after writing errno), so
cg_destroy() succeeds, and the zombie is reaped when the test binary
exits.  The same missing waitpid exists in the err != EADDRINUSE path
at the same loop level, so this is pre-existing behaviour rather than
a regression introduced by this patch.
Minor Issues mm: improve map count checks 🔗 "Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle)" 3p
This series fixes an overly conservative map count headroom in mremap() move operations, adds READ_ONCE() access to sysctl_max_map_count via a helper, and moves the map count check under the mmap write lock to eliminate a TOCTOU race. Patches 1 and 2 are correct; patch 3 introduces a minor behavioral regression by applying the early map count check unconditionally to mremap() paths that have no early destination unmaps.
include internal mmap mremap nommu tests vma
Lorenzo Stoakes (Oracle) <ljs@kernel.org>

mm: improve map count checks

Patches 1 and 2 look correct to me.

The headroom correction in patch 1 is well-justified.  After commit
659ace584e7a, __split_vma() explicitly bypasses the map_count check
(confirmed in mm/vma.c: "__split_vma() bypasses sysctl_max_map_count
checking"), so the unmap path can only produce at most a net +1 VMA
(split both ends, remove middle).  Combined with the +1 from copying
the VMA if no merge occurs, headroom of 2 is the right bound in
prep_move_vma().

The WRITE_ONCE claim in patch 2 is verified: proc_dointvec_minmax()
reaches proc_int_conv() with k_ptr_range_check=true, and that branch
unconditionally calls WRITE_ONCE(*k_ptr, tmp_k) regardless of whether
extra2 is set.  The READ_ONCE() in get_sysctl_max_map_count() pairs
correctly with that.

Patch 3 has one concern.

> diff --git a/mm/mremap.c b/mm/mremap.c
> --- a/mm/mremap.c
> +++ b/mm/mremap.c

[ ... ]

> +static bool __check_map_count_against_split(struct mm_struct *mm,
> +					    bool before_unmaps)
> +{
> +	const int sys_map_count = get_sysctl_max_map_count();
> +	int map_count = mm->map_count;
> +
> +	mmap_assert_write_locked(mm);

Good -- the assert correctly enforces the locking requirement.

[ ... ]

> +	if (!check_map_count_against_split_early()) {
> +		mmap_write_unlock(mm);
> +		return -ENOMEM;
> +	}
> +
> +	if (vrm_move_only(vrm)) {
> +		res = remap_move(vrm);
> +	} else {
> +		...
> +		res = vrm_implies_new_addr(vrm) ? mremap_to(vrm) : mremap_at(vrm);
> +	}

check_map_count_against_split_early() is now applied unconditionally
to all mremap() operations.  However, the mremap_at() code path
(!vrm_implies_new_addr, !vrm_move_only) does not perform any early
destination unmaps.

Consider:

  mremap(addr, old_len, new_len, MREMAP_MAYMOVE)  /* expand */

With neither MREMAP_FIXED nor MREMAP_DONTUNMAP set,
vrm_implies_new_addr() returns false, so mremap_at() is called.  If
the VMA can be expanded in-place via expand_vma_in_place(), no
additional VMA is created -- zero headroom is needed.

Yet check_map_count_against_split_early() (before_unmaps=true) rejects
this call when map_count + 4 > sysctl_max_map_count.  Before this
patch, check_mremap_params() returned 0 early for the
!vrm_implies_new_addr() case, so no map-count check was applied to
in-place expansions at all.  This is a behavioral regression: a process
at map_count == sys_max - 3 that previously succeeded with a simple
in-place expand will now receive -ENOMEM.

The same applies to the pure-shrink path through mremap_at(): shrink
uses __split_vma() internally which intentionally bypasses the
map_count limit, yet the unconditional early check can now reject it
before anything is attempted.

For the mremap_at() EXPAND path that falls back to move_vma(), the
existing check_map_count_against_split() inside prep_move_vma() already
handles the limit correctly with headroom of 2 -- no additional early
check is needed.

Would it be correct to gate check_map_count_against_split_early() on
only the paths that perform early destination unmaps?

  if (vrm_move_only(vrm) || vrm_implies_new_addr(vrm)) {
      if (!check_map_count_against_split_early()) {
          mmap_write_unlock(mm);
          return -ENOMEM;
      }
  }
4 patches
  • [PATCH 0/3] mm: improve map count checks
  • [PATCH 1/3] mm/mremap: correct invalid map count check
  • [PATCH 2/3] mm: abstract reading sysctl_max_map_count, and READ_ONCE()
  • [PATCH 3/3] mm/mremap: check map count under mmap write lock and abstract
Looks Good mm: migrate: transfer large_rmappable flag in folio_migrate_flags() 🔗 Usama Arif 1p
The patch fixes a use-after-free in the deferred split shrinker by transferring the large_rmappable flag during folio migration. Without this fix, a migrated folio can be added to the deferred split queue but escape cleanup at free time, leaving a stale queue entry that causes use-after-free when the shrinker walks the list.
migrate
From: <reviewer>
Subject: Re: [PATCH] mm: migrate: transfer large_rmappable flag in folio_migrate_flags()

On <date>, Usama Arif <usama.arif@linux.dev> wrote:

> folio_migrate_flags() transfers folio state from source to destination
> during migration, but does not transfer the large_rmappable flag.

Verified the bug and the fix. Here is what I checked:

alloc_migration_target() calls __folio_alloc() for large folios without
wrapping the result in page_rmappable_folio(), so the destination folio
indeed never gets large_rmappable set. Same for alloc_misplaced_dst_folio(),
which calls __folio_alloc_node() directly.

> diff --git a/mm/migrate.c b/mm/migrate.c
> --- a/mm/migrate.c
> +++ b/mm/migrate.c
> @@ -846,6 +846,9 @@ void folio_migrate_flags(struct folio *newfolio, struct folio *folio)
>  	folio_copy_owner(newfolio, folio);
>  	pgalloc_tag_swap(newfolio, folio);
>  
> +	if (folio_test_large_rmappable(folio))
> +		folio_set_large_rmappable(newfolio);
> +
>  	mem_cgroup_migrate(folio, newfolio);
>  }

The ordering is correct. In migrate_folio_move(), move_to_new_folio() ---
which calls folio_migrate_flags() --- runs before the
deferred_split_folio(dst, src_partially_mapped) call, so large_rmappable
is set on dst before it is enqueued.

I traced the full UAF path: deferred_split_folio() does not check
large_rmappable before adding to the queue, but folio_unqueue_deferred_split()
does:

  if (folio_order(folio) <= 1 || !folio_test_large_rmappable(folio))
      return false;

Without large_rmappable on dst, this early-return skips the dequeue,
leaving a stale entry. The shrinker then walks freed memory.

Also verified that __folio_migrate_mapping() calls
folio_unqueue_deferred_split() on the source folio (which has large_rmappable
set), so the source side is correctly cleaned up before migration completes.

Looks good to me.

Reviewed-by: <reviewer>

Looks Good binfmt_misc: restore write access before closing files opened by open_exec() v2+ 🔗 Robert Garcia 1p
bm_register_write() calls open_exec() which internally calls deny_write_access() on the interpreter file; when add_entry() fails, the error path was closing the file with filp_close() without first restoring write access. This patch fixes the leak by calling allow_write_access() before filp_close() in that error path.
Newer versions: v1
fs
From: Robert Garcia <rob_garcia@163.com>

binfmt_misc: restore write access before closing files opened by open_exec()

Verified the fix by cross-referencing open_exec() -> do_open_execat()
and the error path in bm_register_write().

> diff --git a/fs/binfmt_misc.c b/fs/binfmt_misc.c
> --- a/fs/binfmt_misc.c
> +++ b/fs/binfmt_misc.c

[ ... ]

> +		if (f) {
> +			allow_write_access(f);
>  			filp_close(f, NULL);
> +		}

Checked: open_exec() calls do_open_execat(), which in 5.15.y calls
deny_write_access() before returning the file. The matching
allow_write_access() must be called before releasing the file.
Without this fix, a failed add_entry() leaves write access
permanently denied on the interpreter file.

The choice of allow_write_access() over exe_file_allow_write_access()
is correct for 5.15.y: commit 0357ef03c94e introduced the latter API
after 5.15, so the older allow_write_access() is the right pairing
for this stable branch.

The error path runs after inode_unlock(), so no lock is held here.
kfree(e) is safe because e->interp_file = f was set before
add_entry() but add_entry() failure means e never reached any list.
No double-free risk. Cleanup symmetry with success path looks correct.
Looks Good binfmt_misc: restore write access before closing files opened by open_exec() 🔗 Robert Garcia 1p
bm_register_write() calls open_exec() which internally decrements i_writecount via deny_write_access(), but the error path after add_entry() failure was closing the file with filp_close() without first calling allow_write_access(), permanently leaking a negative i_writecount on the inode. The patch adds the missing allow_write_access() call before filp_close() in that error path.
fs
From: Zilin Guan <zilin@seu.edu.cn>

binfmt_misc: restore write access before closing files opened by open_exec()

Verified against fs/exec.c: do_open_execat() calls
exe_file_deny_write_access(), which in mm-new wraps deny_write_access()
with a FMODE_FSNOTIFY_HSM bypass. In 6.1.y, FMODE_FSNOTIFY_HSM does not
exist, so open_exec() unconditionally decrements i_writecount. The old
error path in bm_register_write() called filp_close() without the
symmetric allow_write_access(), leaving i_writecount permanently negative
on the inode.

> +	if (err) {
> +		if (f) {
> +			allow_write_access(f);
>  			filp_close(f, NULL);
> +		}

The choice of allow_write_access() rather than
exe_file_allow_write_access() is correct for 6.1.y. The exe_file_
variant and its FMODE_FSNOTIFY_HSM guard were introduced by commit
0357ef03c94e and are absent from the 6.1.y baseline. Since open_exec()
in 6.1.y always calls deny_write_access() unconditionally, pairing it
with allow_write_access() is the right call here.

Cross-referenced against mm-new: the same error path already carries
exe_file_allow_write_access(f), confirming the upstream intent and that
this backport gets the semantics right for the target kernel.

Looks good to me.

Minor Issues treewide: Use IS_ERR_OR_NULL over manual NULL check - refactor 🔗 Philipp Hahn 61p
Treewide Coccinelle-generated series converting manual IS_ERR() + NULL check combinations to IS_ERR_OR_NULL(), and removing incorrect likely()/unlikely() wrappers around it. The individual substitutions shown are all semantically equivalent, but the Coccinelle script has a documentation typo and patches 55-58 carry a disclosed semantic change worth explicit ack from affected maintainers.
arch drivers fs include kernel kmemleak lib net scripts security sound tests virt
From: Philipp Hahn <phahn-oss@avm.de>
Subject: [PATCH 00/61] treewide: Use IS_ERR_OR_NULL over manual NULL check

> +// SPDX-License-Identifier: GPL-2.0-only
> +///
> +/// Use IF_ERR_OR_NULL() instead of IS_ERR() plus a check for (not) NULL

Typo in the Coccinelle documentation comment: "IF_ERR_OR_NULL" should
be "IS_ERR_OR_NULL".

[ ... ]

> +@p2 depends on patch@
> +expression E;
> +@@
> +(
> +-	E == NULL || WARN_ON(IS_ERR(E))
> ++	WARN_ON(IS_ERR_OR_NULL(E))
> +|
> +-	E == NULL || WARN_ON_ONCE(IS_ERR(E))
> ++	WARN_ON_ONCE(IS_ERR_OR_NULL(E))
> +)

The cover letter calls out patches 55-58 as having a semantic change:
WARN_ON / WARN_ON_ONCE will now fire for NULL as well as for IS_ERR.
Before this change a NULL was silently tolerated; after it triggers a
warning. This needs an explicit ack from each affected subsystem
maintainer that NULL is also an unexpected/buggy condition at those
call sites, not a normal "not present" sentinel.

[ ... ]

diff --git a/fs/erofs/zdata.c b/fs/erofs/zdata.c

[ ... ]

> -		if (IS_ERR(page) || !page) {
> +		if (IS_ERR_OR_NULL(page)) {
>  			bvec->page = NULL;	/* clear the failure reason */
>  			err = page ? PTR_ERR(page) : -EIO;

Verified correct. IS_ERR_OR_NULL(page) is logically identical to
IS_ERR(page) || !page. Inside the block, the ternary "page ?
PTR_ERR(page) : -EIO" still works: IS_ERR pointers are non-zero
(truthy) so PTR_ERR is taken; NULL is zero (falsy) so -EIO is taken.
No functional change.

[ ... ]

diff --git a/fs/gfs2/glock.c b/fs/gfs2/glock.c

[ ... ]

> -		while ((gl = rhashtable_walk_next(&iter)) && !IS_ERR(gl)) {
> +		while (!IS_ERR_OR_NULL((gl = rhashtable_walk_next(&iter)))) {

The outer do-while retries when gl == ERR_PTR(-EAGAIN). I traced both
paths:
- rhashtable_walk_next returns ERR_PTR(-EAGAIN): the new condition is
  false (IS_ERR_OR_NULL true), gl is set to ERR_PTR(-EAGAIN), inner
  loop exits, outer do-while retries. Same as before.
- rhashtable_walk_next returns NULL (end of table): condition is false,
  gl = NULL, outer do-while sees NULL != ERR_PTR(-EAGAIN) and exits.
  Same as before.
The assignment-in-condition form preserves the gl value that the outer
loop depends on. Correct.

[ ... ]

diff --git a/fs/seq_file.c b/fs/seq_file.c

[ ... ]

> -		if (!p || IS_ERR(p))	// EOF or an error
> +		if (IS_ERR_OR_NULL(p))	// EOF or an error

Verified. PTR_ERR(NULL) = 0, so err = 0 correctly signals EOF when
p is NULL; the IS_ERR path still yields a negative errno. Both
occurrences in seq_read_iter are equivalent to the original.
m->op->stop(m, p) is called with p regardless (NULL or ERR), which
is the expected contract for ->stop().

[ ... ]

diff --git a/fs/btrfs/transaction.c b/fs/btrfs/transaction.c

[ ... ]

> -	if (unlikely(dir_item != NULL && !IS_ERR(dir_item))) {
> +	if (!IS_ERR_OR_NULL(dir_item)) {
>  		pending->error = -EEXIST;
>  		goto dir_item_existed;
>  	} else if (IS_ERR(dir_item)) {

The else-if clause still handles the error case correctly. When
dir_item is NULL: the new first condition is false, IS_ERR(NULL)
is also false (0 is not in the error range), so NULL falls through
identically to before. Verified in include/linux/err.h: IS_ERR_OR_NULL
uses unlikely(!ptr) internally, making the removed unlikely() wrapper
a no-op that checkpatch correctly flags.

Overall: all pattern substitutions in the patches shown are
semantically equivalent. The only substantive concern is the WARN_ON
semantic expansion in patches 55-58, which requires per-site ack that
NULL deserves the same warning as IS_ERR.

Note: patch 33/61 ("mm: Prefer IS_ERR_OR_NULL over manual NULL check")
was not included in the provided diff. From examining mm/, the only
IS_ERR + NULL combinations are in mm/kmemleak.c where they appear as
three-term conditions (kmemleak_enabled && ptr && !IS_ERR(ptr)) that
the author correctly excluded from the Coccinelle transform. If patch
33 touches other mm files, please send it separately for review.

Needs Discussion arm64/mm: contpte-sized exec folios for 16K and 64K pages 🔗 Usama Arif 4p
This series enables contpte-sized iTLB coalescing for executable file-backed mappings on arm64 16K and 64K pages by fixing exec_folio_order(), bypassing the mmap_miss heuristic for VM_EXEC readahead, aligning PIE load addresses to the folio boundary, and adding a folio-size alignment fallback in thp_get_unmapped_area_vmflags(). The series is mostly correct but patch 2 silently overrides THP readahead when VM_HUGEPAGE+VM_EXEC are both set on 4K/16K arm64, and patch 3 reduces ASLR entropy for all PIE binaries by a factor of up to 128 on 16K pages.
arch filemap fs huge_memory
Author: Usama Arif <usama.arif@linux.dev>

arm64/mm: contpte-sized exec folios for 16K and 64K pages

Overall the series is well-motivated and the benchmark numbers are
convincing.  I have two concerns worth discussing before merging.

---
[PATCH 1/4] arm64: request contpte-sized folios for exec memory

> -#define exec_folio_order() ilog2(SZ_64K >> PAGE_SHIFT)
> +#define exec_folio_order() ilog2(CONT_PTES)

Verified: CONT_PTES = 1 << CONFIG_ARM64_CONT_PTE_SHIFT.
For 4K pages (shift=4): ilog2(16)=4 (64K). Unchanged.
For 16K pages (shift=7): ilog2(128)=7 (2M). Correct new value.
For 64K pages (shift=5): ilog2(32)=5 (2M). Correct new value.
The old ilog2(SZ_64K >> PAGE_SHIFT) gave orders 2 and 0 for 16K/64K
respectively, so the fix is correct and the math checks out.

---
[PATCH 2/4] mm: bypass mmap_miss heuristic for VM_EXEC readahead

> +	if (vm_flags & VM_EXEC) {
> +		[ ... ]
> +		ra->order = exec_folio_order();
> +		ra->start = round_down(vmf->pgoff, 1UL << ra->order);
> +		ra->start = max(ra->start, start);
> +		ra_end = round_up(ra->start + ra->ra_pages, 1UL << ra->order);
> +		ra_end = min(ra_end, end);
> +		ra->size = ra_end - ra->start;
> +		ra->async_size = 0;
> +		goto do_readahead;
> +	}

Moving the VM_EXEC block above the mmap_miss check correctly fixes the
mmap_miss runaway described in the cover letter.  The VMA-boundary
clamping logic and the goto are correct.

However, the new VM_EXEC block now also precedes the
force_thp_readahead handling.  force_thp_readahead is set when:

    (vm_flags & VM_HUGEPAGE) && HPAGE_PMD_ORDER <= MAX_PAGECACHE_ORDER

With XA_CHUNK_SHIFT=6, MAX_PAGECACHE_ORDER=min(11, HPAGE_PMD_ORDER).
On arm64 4K pages HPAGE_PMD_ORDER=9, so force_thp_readahead can be
true.  On arm64 16K pages HPAGE_PMD_ORDER=11, same story.  (On 64K
pages HPAGE_PMD_ORDER=13 > MAX_PAGECACHE_ORDER=11, so
force_thp_readahead is always false there -- the primary target of
this series is not affected.)

For a file-backed exec VMA with madvise(MADV_HUGEPAGE) applied on
4K or 16K arm64, the pre-patch code reaches the force_thp_readahead
block and issues a PMD-order readahead window (HPAGE_PMD_NR * 2 pages
with PG_readahead markers).  Post-patch, the new VM_EXEC block fires
first and issues a single contpte-sized folio (order 4 or 7) with
async_size=0, silently bypassing THP readahead entirely.

Is this intentional?  The commit message does not mention this
interaction.  Replacing a 2x-PMD prefetch window with a single-folio
targeted read for exec+hugepage VMAs is a meaningful change in
readahead behavior on 4K and 16K configurations.

One option would be to guard the new VM_EXEC block:

    if (!force_thp_readahead && (vm_flags & VM_EXEC))

so that the existing THP readahead path is preserved for VMAs that
have explicitly requested hugepage treatment.

---
[PATCH 3/4] elf: align ET_DYN base to exec folio order for contpte mapping

> +			if (exec_folio_order())
> +				alignment = max(alignment,
> +					(unsigned long)PAGE_SIZE << exec_folio_order());

The placement (after maximum_alignment(), before the PIE handling
split) is correct for both the interpreter and static-PIE branches.
For static PIE (ld.so, no PT_INTERP), the new alignment exceeds
ELF_MIN_ALIGN=PAGE_SIZE, which correctly triggers the existing
preliminary-mmap alignment path.

For the interpreter (PIE program) branch, load_bias is computed as:

    load_bias = ELF_ET_DYN_BASE + arch_mmap_rnd();
    if (alignment)
        load_bias &= ~(alignment - 1);

With alignment bumped to 2M on 64K pages, the load address is
truncated to 2M granularity.  This divides the number of distinct
PIE load addresses by 32 (PAGE_SIZE=64K, folio=2M, ratio=32).
On 16K pages the folio is also 2M but PAGE_SIZE is 16K, so the
factor is 128.

This ASLR entropy reduction affects every PIE binary on the system,
not only those whose executable segments benefit from contpte mapping.
Has this tradeoff been reviewed from a security perspective?  It would
help to quantify the loss in bits in the commit message -- for example,
on a typical arm64 64K distro kernel with mmap_rnd_bits=18, effective
PIE load-address entropy drops from 18 to 13 bits.

---
[PATCH 4/4] mm: align file-backed mmap to exec folio order in
            thp_get_unmapped_area

> +	if (exec_folio_order()) {
> +		unsigned long folio_size = PAGE_SIZE << exec_folio_order();
> +
> +		ret = __thp_get_unmapped_area(filp, addr, len, off, flags,
> +					      folio_size, vm_flags);
> +		if (ret)
> +			return ret;
> +	}

The fallback is tried only after PMD_SIZE alignment fails (ret==0),
so it is purely additive.  __thp_get_unmapped_area() already handles
the 32-bit and in_compat_syscall() early-return cases, and the
overflow guards (len_pad, off_end) are inside that helper.  On
architectures where exec_folio_order() returns 0 (the generic
default) the block is dead.  Looks correct.

As the commit message notes, this aligns all file-backed mmaps, not
just exec ones.  The commit subject says "exec folio order" but the
change touches every mmap routed through thp_get_unmapped_area,
including read-only data segments.  Worth making that explicit in
the subject or first paragraph to avoid surprising reviewers of
future bisections.
5 patches
  • [PATCH 0/4] arm64/mm: contpte-sized exec folios for 16K and 64K pages
  • [PATCH 1/4] arm64: request contpte-sized folios for exec memory
  • [PATCH 2/4] mm: bypass mmap_miss heuristic for VM_EXEC readahead
  • [PATCH 3/4] elf: align ET_DYN base to exec folio order for contpte mapping
  • [PATCH 4/4] mm: align file-backed mmap to exec folio order in thp_get_unmapped_area
Minor Issues locking: contended_release tracepoint instrumentation 🔗 Dmitry Ilvokhin 2p
This series adds a contended_release tracepoint that fires on the lock-holder side when a contended lock is released, complementing the existing contention_begin/contention_end waiter-side tracepoints; it also refactors percpu_up_read()'s slowpath into a new __percpu_up_read() helper to avoid inlining the tracepoint call.
include kernel
Dmitry Ilvokhin <d@ilvokhin.com>

locking: Add contended_release tracepoint

I traced through all eight call sites against the current tree.  The
placement in mutex, semaphore, rwsem (up_read/up_write/downgrade),
rtmutex, and rwbase read-unlock all fire only when waiters are
confirmed present.  The __percpu_up_read() placement (between smp_mb()
and this_cpu_dec) is fine: the existing smp_mb() already orders the
critical section stores before the counter decrement; the tracepoint
call is a compiler barrier and does not weaken that ordering.  The
patch 1 extraction is correct: lockdep_assert_preemption_disabled()
matches the calling context (preempt_disable'd in percpu_up_read), and
the EXPORT_SYMBOL_GPL is consistent with Peter's request.

One site stands out:

> diff --git a/kernel/locking/percpu-rwsem.c b/kernel/locking/percpu-rwsem.c
> --- a/kernel/locking/percpu-rwsem.c
> +++ b/kernel/locking/percpu-rwsem.c
> @@ -263,6 +263,8 @@ void percpu_up_write(struct percpu_rw_semaphore *sem)
>  {
>  	rwsem_release(&sem->dep_map, _RET_IP_);
>
> +	trace_contended_release(sem);
> +
>  	/*
>  	 * Signal the writer is done, no fast path yet.

This fires on every percpu_up_write() call, even when sem->waiters is
empty.  Every other site guards with a confirmed-waiters check:

  - mutex:    inside if (waiter)
  - semaphore: inside if (!wake_q_empty(&wake_q))
  - rwsem:    inside if (unlikely(tmp & RWSEM_FLAG_WAITERS))
  - rtmutex:  after while (!rt_mutex_has_waiters(lock)) exits
  - rwbase write unlock:

> +	if (trace_contended_release_enabled() && rt_mutex_has_waiters(rtm))
> +		trace_contended_release(rwb);

The cover letter says percpu_up_write "always wakes via __wake_up()",
but __wake_up() with an empty sem->waiters is a no-op -- there need
not be any waiters.  A write lock can be acquired and released without
contention even while sem->block is set.  The result is that
trace_contended_release fires on every write-side unlock, making the
event misleading for tooling trying to identify genuinely contended
release events.

An analogous fix using the same pattern as rwbase_write_unlock would
be:

  if (trace_contended_release_enabled() && waitqueue_active(&sem->waiters))
          trace_contended_release(sem);

This check is safe before atomic_set_release(&sem->block, 0): while
sem->block is still 1 no new waiters can drain off sem->waiters, so
the read of waitqueue_active() is stable.

Could the placement of trace_contended_release(sem) in
percpu_up_write() be moved inside such a guard to match all other
call sites?

  • [PATCH v2 1/2] locking/percpu-rwsem: Extract __percpu_up_read()
  • [PATCH v2 2/2] locking: Add contended_release tracepoint
Needs Work mm/damon: support addr_unit on default monitoring targets for modules 🔗 SeongJae Park 5p
This series extends DAMON's addr_unit support to the default monitoring target path used by DAMON_RECLAIM and DAMON_LRU_SORT, fixing a minor end-address off-by-one bug along the way. Patch 3 contains a concrete bug: addr_unit is passed as the nr_ranges argument to damon_set_regions(), causing out-of-bounds access when addr_unit > 1.
damon/core damon/lru_sort damon/reclaim damon/stat include
SeongJae Park <sj@kernel.org>

mm/damon: support addr_unit on default monitoring targets for modules

Patches 1, 2, 4, and 5 look correct.  There is one concrete bug in
patch 3 and one minor logic issue in patch 2 worth considering.

--- [PATCH 2/5] mm/damon/core: support addr_unit on damon_find_biggest_system_ram() ---

> +	walk_system_ram_res(0, -1, &res, walk_system_ram);
> +	if (res.end < res.start)
> +		return false;

The previous code used 'struct damon_addr_range arg = {}' with the
check 'arg.end <= arg.start', which correctly returned false when
no System RAM resource was found (both fields zero after
zero-initialization).  The new check 'res.end < res.start' does not
catch that case: a zero-initialized 'struct resource' has start=0
and end=0, so '0 < 0' is false and the function falls through to
compute *start=0, *end=1 (or 0 when addr_unit>1), returning true
when it should return false.

In practice a running kernel always has at least one System RAM
resource so this path cannot be reached, but the logic is
inconsistent with the old behaviour.  A check such as tracking
whether walk_system_ram was ever invoked would restore the original
semantics.

--- [PATCH 3/5] mm/damon/core: receive addr_unit on damon_set_region_biggest_system_ram_default() ---

> -	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, 1, min_region_sz);
> +	return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, addr_unit, min_region_sz);

This is a bug.  The third parameter of damon_set_regions() is
nr_ranges -- the number of elements in the 'ranges' array:

    int damon_set_regions(struct damon_target *t,
            struct damon_addr_range *ranges,
            unsigned int nr_ranges,
            unsigned long min_region_sz)

'addr_range' is a single 'struct damon_addr_range' declared on the
stack, not an array of addr_unit elements.  When addr_unit > 1,
passing it as nr_ranges causes damon_set_regions() to iterate and
dereference 'ranges[1]' through 'ranges[addr_unit-1]' inside both
the region-removal loop and the region-addition loop, reading beyond
the single valid element -- a stack out-of-bounds access.

The addr_unit conversion is already applied correctly upstream in
damon_find_biggest_system_ram(), where res.start and res.end+1 are
each divided by addr_unit via damon_res_to_core_addr() before being
stored in *start and *end.  By the time damon_set_regions() is
called, addr_range already holds the correctly scaled core
addresses.  The nr_ranges argument should remain 1:

    return damon_set_regions(t, &addr_range, 1, min_region_sz);

Patches 4 and 5 (removing the 'if (!monitor_region_start &&
!monitor_region_end) addr_unit = 1' resets in reclaim.c and
lru_sort.c) are correct and consistent with the updated behaviour
of damon_find_biggest_system_ram() now that it honours addr_unit.

  • [PATCH 2/5] mm/damon/core: support addr_unit on damon_find_biggest_system_ram()
  • [PATCH 3/5] mm/damon/core: receive addr_unit on damon_set_region_biggest_system_ram_default()

  • [PATCH 5/5] mm/damon/lru_sort: respect addr_unit on default monitoring region setup
Needs Work mm/damon: Support hot application detections 🔗 <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com> 4p
This four-patch RFC series introduces DAMON_HOT_HUGEPAGE, a new kernel module that monitors user-specified PIDs via virtual-address DAMON, detects hot regions, and collapses them synchronously into huge pages via a new DAMOS_COLLAPSE action backed by MADV_COLLAPSE. Patch 1 is a clean refactoring; patches 2-3 have a mutex initialization bug, a Kconfig gap, watermark/documentation mismatches, and a stale docs section describing removed v1 behavior.
damon/Kconfig damon/Makefile damon/hugepage damon/lru_sort damon/modules-common damon/reclaim damon/vaddr docs include
Asier Gutierrez <gutierrez.asier@huawei-partners.com>

mm/damon: Support hot application detections [RFC PATCH v2 0/4]

[ Patch 1/4 - modules-common refactoring ]

Patch 1 is a clean refactor.  Both existing callers in reclaim.c and
lru_sort.c pass DAMON_OPS_PADDR, so behavior is unchanged.  The error
path (damon_destroy_ctx on damon_select_ops failure) is preserved
identically.  No issues.

[ Patch 2/4 - DAMOS_COLLAPSE action ]

> diff --git a/include/linux/damon.h b/include/linux/damon.h
> @@ -142,6 +142,7 @@ enum damos_action {
>  	DAMOS_MIGRATE_HOT,
>  	DAMOS_MIGRATE_COLD,
> +	DAMOS_COLLAPSE,
>  	DAMOS_STAT,		/* Do nothing but only record the stat */
>  	NR_DAMOS_ACTIONS,
>  };

All kernel-internal accesses use the enum symbol, so shifting DAMOS_STAT
from 9 to 10 is fine.  However, every other damos_action value is
registered in damos_sysfs_action_names[] in sysfs-schemes.c so users
can select it via the sysfs action knob.  DAMOS_COLLAPSE is not added
there.  Is the omission intentional?  If DAMOS_COLLAPSE is meant to be
a general-purpose action (like DAMOS_HUGEPAGE) and not purely
module-private, it should get an entry alongside the others.

> diff --git a/mm/damon/vaddr.c b/mm/damon/vaddr.c
> +	case DAMOS_COLLAPSE:
> +		madv_action = MADV_COLLAPSE;
> +		break;

This routes to damos_madvise() -> do_madvise(..., MADV_COLLAPSE).
That path is gated in madvise.c:

    #ifdef CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE
    case MADV_HUGEPAGE:
    case MADV_NOHUGEPAGE:
    case MADV_COLLAPSE:
    #endif

so madvise_behavior_valid() rejects MADV_COLLAPSE when
CONFIG_TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE is not set, and damos_madvise() silently
returns 0.  The new Kconfig entry only says:

> +config DAMON_HOT_HUGEPAGE
> +	bool "Build DAMON-based collapse of hot regions (DAMON_HOT_HUGEPAGE)"
> +	depends on DAMON_VADDR

Should this also say "depends on TRANSPARENT_HUGEPAGE"?  Without that
dependency the module builds and runs on a THP-less kernel, but
DAMOS_COLLAPSE never applies anything and the user gets no indication
of why.

[ Patch 3/4 - hugepage.c new module ]

> +struct mutex enable_disable_lock;

This global mutex is zero-initialized (BSS), not properly initialized.
DEFINE_MUTEX() (which expands to __MUTEX_INITIALIZER including
LIST_HEAD_INIT on wait_list) is required for global mutexes.  A
BSS-zero-initialized wait_list has .next = .prev = NULL instead of
pointing to the list head itself.  If mutex_lock() ever blocks because
two threads race on enable/disable, __mutex_lock_slowpath() calls
list_add() on that NULL-pointer list_head and panics.  Please use
DEFINE_MUTEX(enable_disable_lock).

> +static struct damos_watermarks damon_hugepage_wmarks = {
> +	.metric = DAMOS_WMARK_FREE_MEM_RATE,
> +	.interval = 5000000, /* 5 seconds */
> +	.high = 900, /* 90 percent */
> +	.mid = 800, /* 80 percent */
> +	.low = 50, /* 5 percent */
> +};

The documentation for this module (patch 4) says the defaults are:

    wmarks_high: "200 (20%) by default"
    wmarks_mid:  "150 (15%) by default"

The code and docs disagree on the watermark defaults.  Which is
correct?  With high=900 the scheme is inactive only when free memory
exceeds 90%, meaning it runs on nearly any loaded system.  With the
documented high=200 it would be suppressed on lightly-loaded systems
with >20% free memory, which seems wrong for a THP-promotion use case.
The code value (900) is probably closer to the right intent, but the
documentation must be updated to match.

> +static struct damos_quota damon_hugepage_quota = {
> +	/* use up to 10 ms time, reclaim up to 128 MiB per 1 sec by default */
> +	.ms = 10,
> +	.sz = 0,

The comment says "reclaim up to 128 MiB" but .sz = 0 (no size quota)
and this is a collapse module, not reclaim.  This is a copy-paste from
damon_reclaim_quota that was not updated.

[ Patch 4/4 - Documentation ]

The "How It Works?" section describes the v1 behavior that was removed
based on SeongJae Park's feedback:

    "The monitor thread will calculate the moving average of the sum of
     utimes of all threads ... Then, pick the top three and launch a
     damon process to monitor the hot regions in those tasks."
    "If a task turns cold, the monitor thread will detect it (it will
     not fall in the top three hot tasks), and stop the damon thread."

But v2 removes automatic task selection entirely -- the user provides
PIDs via the monitored_pids parameter.  The "How It Works?" section
needs to be rewritten to describe the actual v2 behavior.

Additionally, the Interface section references the module as
"damon_dynamic_hotpages" (old name) in the sysfs path:

    /sys/module/damon_dynamic_hotpages/parameters/<parameter>

but the module file is now mm/damon/hugepage.c.  Please verify the
correct module name and update the path accordingly.

  • [RFC PATCH v2 1/4] mm/damon: Generic context creation for modules
  • [RFC PATCH v2 2/4] mm/damon: Support for synchrounous huge pages collapse
  • [RFC PATCH v2 3/4] mm/damon: New module with hot application detection
  • [RFC PATCH v2 4/4] DAMON_HOT_HUGEPAGE documentation
Minor Issues mm: prevent droppable mappings from being locked 🔗 Anthony Yznaga 2p
The patch introduces vma_supports_mlock() to consolidate VMA lockability checks and uses it in both mlock_fixup() and __mmap_complete() to fix droppable mappings being silently locked under MCL_FUTURE. The selftest patch verifies both mlock() and mlockall(MCL_FUTURE) paths.
include internal mlock tests vma
Anthony Yznaga <anthony.yznaga@oracle.com>

mm: prevent droppable mappings from being locked

The kernel changes are correct. One minor test issue noted below.

> diff --git a/mm/internal.h b/mm/internal.h
> +static inline bool vma_supports_mlock(const struct vm_area_struct *vma)
> +{
> +	if (vma->vm_flags & (VM_SPECIAL | VM_DROPPABLE))
> +		return false;
> +	if (vma_is_dax(vma) || is_vm_hugetlb_page(vma))
> +		return false;
> +	return vma != get_gate_vma(current->mm);
> +}

Verified the gate-VMA check uses current->mm rather than a
caller-supplied mm.  This is safe because the only caller of
__mmap_complete() is __mmap_region(), which opens with
"struct mm_struct *mm = current->mm" and stores that into
map->mm, so both are identical at the call site.

> diff --git a/mm/mlock.c b/mm/mlock.c
> -	if (newflags == oldflags || (oldflags & VM_SPECIAL) ||
> -	    is_vm_hugetlb_page(vma) || vma == get_gate_vma(current->mm) ||
> -	    vma_is_dax(vma) || vma_is_secretmem(vma) || (oldflags & VM_DROPPABLE))
> +	if (newflags == oldflags || vma_is_secretmem(vma) ||
> +	    !vma_supports_mlock(vma))

All conditions from the old check are accounted for: VM_SPECIAL,
hugetlb, gate VMA, DAX, and VM_DROPPABLE are captured inside
vma_supports_mlock(); secretmem is kept as a separate predicate,
which is correct since it must block both lock and unlock regardless
of the other conditions.  No behaviour change for any pre-existing
VMA type.

> diff --git a/mm/vma.c b/mm/vma.c
> -		if ((vm_flags & VM_SPECIAL) || vma_is_dax(vma) ||
> -				is_vm_hugetlb_page(vma) ||
> -				vma == get_gate_vma(mm))
> +		if (!vma_supports_mlock(vma))

This is the actual bug fix: VM_DROPPABLE was absent from the
__mmap_complete() filter, allowing droppable VMAs to carry VM_LOCKED
when MCL_FUTURE was active.  The new check covers every condition the
old code checked plus VM_DROPPABLE.  Also verified: secretmem is not
regressed here because secretmem does not set VM_SPECIAL but does set
VM_LOCKED explicitly in secretmem_mmap_prepare(), and the
vma_supports_mlock() path correctly counts it in locked_vm, which is
unchanged from the old behaviour.

[ ... ]

> +static void test_mlockall_future_droppable(void)
> +{
> +	char *map;
> +	unsigned long page_size = getpagesize();
> +
> +	if (mlockall(MCL_CURRENT | MCL_FUTURE))
> +		ksft_exit_fail_msg(...);
> +
> +	map = mmap(NULL, 2 * page_size, PROT_READ | PROT_WRITE,
> +		   MAP_ANONYMOUS | MAP_DROPPABLE, -1, 0);
> +
> +	ksft_test_result(!unlock_lock_check(map, false), ...);

The mmap() return value is not checked against MAP_FAILED before
being passed to unlock_lock_check().  If mmap() fails (e.g. on a
kernel built without MAP_DROPPABLE support), map == (char *)-1.
is_vmflag_set() will search /proc/self/smaps for the address
0xffffffffffffffff, find nothing, return 0, and the test silently
passes having verified nothing.

The companion function test_mlock_droppable() correctly guards with:

  if (map == MAP_FAILED)
          ksft_exit_fail_msg("mmap error: %s", strerror(errno));

Please add the same check here.

Minor Issues kasan: x86: arm64: KASAN tag-based mode for x86 🔗 Maciej Wieczor-Retman 5p
This series adds KASAN software tag-based mode for x86 using LAM bits [60:57], including an arithmetic-shift kasan_mem_to_shadow() change, arch-specific 4-bit tag constants, x86 arch tag helpers, a generic KASAN-aware page_to_virt(), and tag-reset fixes in execmem/vmalloc to prevent tagged pointers from corrupting maple-tree range arithmetic.
arch docs execmem include kasan/report scripts vmalloc
Author: Maciej Wieczor-Retman <m.wieczorretman@pm.me>

kasan: x86: arm64: KASAN tag-based mode for x86 (patches 01,02,04,06,07)

I read the full implementations of every modified function and traced
kasan_mem_to_shadow(), kasan_shadow_to_mem(), vm_reset_perms(),
execmem_vmalloc(), and page_to_virt() against the tree.  The overall
design is correct.  A few points below.

--- [PATCH v11 01/15] kasan: sw_tags: Use arithmetic shift ---

> -static inline void *kasan_mem_to_shadow(const void *addr)
> -{
> -	return (void *)((unsigned long)addr >> KASAN_SHADOW_SCALE_SHIFT)
> -		+ KASAN_SHADOW_OFFSET;
> -}

Verified: with the arithmetic (signed) right-shift the inverse
kasan_shadow_to_mem() formula (shadow - offset) << shift still holds
because the change is only in what KASAN_SHADOW_OFFSET denotes
(KASAN_SHADOW_END vs. the old bias).  The generic kasan_shadow_to_mem()
in mm/kasan/kasan.h is updated in tandem.  No issue.

--- [PATCH v11 02/15] kasan: arm64: x86: Make special tags arch specific ---

> +++ b/arch/arm64/include/asm/kasan-tags.h
> +#define KASAN_TAG_KERNEL	0xFF /* native kernel pointers tag */
> +#ifdef CONFIG_KASAN_HW_TAGS
> +#define KASAN_TAG_MIN		0xF0 /* minimum value for random tags */
> +#define KASAN_TAG_WIDTH		4
> +#else
> +#define KASAN_TAG_WIDTH		8
> +#endif

Verified: for arm64 HW_TAGS all random tags live in [0xF0, 0xFF], so
XOR-with-0xFF maps them to [0x00, 0x0F], which fits in 4 page->flags
bits.  The round-trip is lossless.  OK.

The mm.h hunk for this patch (6 +++---) must replace the hardcoded 0xff
in page_kasan_tag() and page_kasan_tag_set() with KASAN_TAG_KERNEL.
That replacement is essential for x86 where KASAN_TAG_KERNEL=0xF: a
zeroed page slot XOR'd with 0xff yields 0xFF, but the expected kernel
tag on x86 is 0xF.  Without the change every tag comparison for
uninitialized pages would be wrong.  Could you confirm that hunk is
present?  It was not visible in the provided diff.

--- [PATCH v11 04/15] x86/kasan: Add arch specific kasan functions ---

> +#define __tag_reset(addr)		(sign_extend64((u64)(addr), 56))

Verified: bit 56 is always 1 in a kernel address and is never touched
by a tag stored in bits [60:57].  sign_extend64(addr, 56) copies bit 56
to all of [63:57], restoring the canonical form for both 4-level
(canonical from bit 47) and 5-level (canonical from bit 56) paging.
OK.

> +static inline void *__tag_set(const void *__addr, u8 tag)
> +{
> +	u64 addr = (u64)__addr;
> +	addr &= ~__tag_shifted(KASAN_TAG_BITS_MASK);
> +	addr |= __tag_shifted(tag & KASAN_TAG_BITS_MASK);

When CONFIG_KASAN_SW_TAGS is not set, KASAN_TAG_WIDTH defaults to 0 so
KASAN_TAG_BITS_MASK == 0, __tag_shifted(0) == 0, and __tag_set becomes
a no-op.  OK.

--- [PATCH v11 06/15] mm: Make page_to_virt() KASAN aware ---

> +#define page_to_virt(x) ({						\
> +	void *__addr = __va(PFN_PHYS(page_to_pfn((struct page *)x)));	\
> +	kasan_set_tag(__addr, page_kasan_tag(x));			\
> +})

The cast (struct page *)x silently discards const and accepts any
pointer type without a diagnostic.  The removed arm64 debug version
used __typeof__(x) __page = x, which preserved the type.  Could you
use __typeof__ here to restore the type check?  For example:

  __typeof__(x) __page = (x);
  void *__addr = __va(PFN_PHYS(page_to_pfn(__page)));
  kasan_set_tag(__addr, page_kasan_tag(__page));

> diff --git a/arch/arm64/include/asm/memory.h b/arch/arm64/include/asm/memory.h
> -#if defined(CONFIG_DEBUG_VIRTUAL)
> -#define page_to_virt(x)	({					\
> -	__typeof__(x) __page = x;				\
> -	void *__addr = __va(page_to_phys(__page));		\
> -	(void *)__tag_set((const void *)__addr,			\
> -			  page_kasan_tag(__page));		\
> -})
>  #define virt_to_page(x)		pfn_to_page(virt_to_pfn(x))

After this removal, arm64 + CONFIG_DEBUG_VIRTUAL falls through to the
new generic page_to_virt().  The generic path uses
PFN_PHYS(page_to_pfn()) rather than page_to_phys().  On arm64 these
are equivalent, so there is no functional regression.  Intentional?

--- [PATCH v11 07/15] mm/execmem: Untag addresses ---

> +	/*
> +	 * Resetting the tag here is necessary to avoid the tagged address
> +	 * ending up in the maple tree structure. There it's linear address
> +	 * can be incorrectly compared with other addresses which can result in

Nit: "it's" should be "its" (possessive, not contraction).

> -	return p;
> +	return kasan_reset_tag(p);

Verified: __vmalloc_node_range() returns a SW_TAGS-tagged pointer.
Without this reset, execmem_cache_populate() passes a tagged address
to execmem_cache_add_locked() which converts it to an unsigned long
and uses it as a maple-tree key.  A later mas_walk() with an untagged
index misses the entry and returns a wrong address.  Fix is correct.

Note: for the !use_cache path, execmem_alloc() calls kasan_reset_tag()
again on the return value of execmem_vmalloc().  Double reset is
idempotent but redundant; the call in execmem_alloc() could now be
dropped for that path, though leaving it is harmless.

> diff --git a/mm/vmalloc.c b/mm/vmalloc.c
> +		unsigned long addr =
> +		    (unsigned long)kasan_reset_tag(page_address(area->pages[i]));

Verified: on x86, page_address() calls lowmem_page_address() ->
page_to_virt(), which after patch 06 applies the per-page KASAN tag.
Different pages can have different random tags, so without the reset
min()/max() would compare addresses with mismatched high bits and
compute a wrong [start, end) range for _vm_unmap_aliases().  Fix is
correct.

Looks Good mm/userfaultfd: fix hugetlb fault mutex hash calculation 🔗 Jianhui Zhou 1p
The patch fixes a unit mismatch in mfill_atomic_hugetlb() where linear_page_index() (which returns PAGE_SIZE units) was passed to hugetlb_fault_mutex_hash() which expects huge-page units, potentially hashing different threads working on the same huge page to different mutexes. The fix introduces hugetlb_linear_page_index() which is algebraically identical to the existing static vma_hugecache_offset().

Jianhui Zhou <jianhuizzzzz@gmail.com>

mm/userfaultfd: fix hugetlb fault mutex hash calculation

Verified the bug and the fix by reading linear_page_index(),
vma_hugecache_offset(), hugetlb_fault_mutex_hash(), and the
mfill_atomic_hugetlb() loop.

> diff --git a/include/linux/hugetlb.h b/include/linux/hugetlb.h
> +static inline pgoff_t hugetlb_linear_page_index(struct vm_area_struct *vma,
> +		unsigned long address)
> +{
> +	struct hstate *h = hstate_vma(vma);
> +
> +	return ((address - vma->vm_start) >> huge_page_shift(h)) +
> +		(vma->vm_pgoff >> huge_page_order(h));
> +}

This is algebraically identical to the static vma_hugecache_offset() in
mm/hugetlb.c, confirming it produces huge-page-granularity offsets.
All other callers of hugetlb_fault_mutex_hash() already pass an idx
computed via vma_hugecache_offset() or vmf->pgoff (set from
vma_hugecache_offset() in the fault path), so the new function is
consistent with existing practice.

> diff --git a/mm/userfaultfd.c b/mm/userfaultfd.c
> -		idx = linear_page_index(dst_vma, dst_addr);
> +		idx = hugetlb_linear_page_index(dst_vma, dst_addr);

dst_addr is guaranteed huge-page-aligned at entry (checked via
dst_start & (vma_hpagesize - 1) == 0) and the loop advances it by
vma_hpagesize, so the shift in hugetlb_linear_page_index() has no
rounding ambiguity.

Looks good to me.
Looks Good kthread, exit: clean up kernel thread exit paths 🔗 Christian Brauner 2p
This two-patch series removes the kthread_exit() macro alias for do_exit() and then renames do_exit() to task_exit() tree-wide to clarify it is a public API rather than a private helper.
docs fs hugetlb include io_uring kernel lib security tests tools
From: Christian Brauner <brauner@kernel.org>
Subject: [PATCH v2 0/2] kthread, exit: clean up kernel thread exit paths

Verified both patches against the source tree. No regressions found.

--- [PATCH v2 1/2] kthread: remove kthread_exit() ---

> -#define kthread_exit(result) do_exit(result)

kthread_exit() was always a macro that expanded inline to do_exit(), so
no kthread_exit symbol was ever emitted in object files. The removal of
NORETURN(kthread_exit) from tools/objtool/noreturns.h is therefore
correct -- objtool never sees that symbol in any binary, making the
entry spurious from the start.

> -NORETURN(kthread_exit)

Confirmed: all direct call sites are covered. kthread_complete_and_exit(),
kthread() (two exit paths: the !done early-exit and the threadfn()
return), and __module_put_and_kthread_exit() are all updated to call
do_exit() directly. The module_put_and_kthread_exit() macro in
include/linux/module.h for non-modular builds is updated in lock-step.
No remaining callers of the kthread_exit() macro were found outside the
patch.

--- [PATCH v2 2/2] tree-wide: rename do_exit() to task_exit() ---

> -void do_exit(long error_code) __noreturn;
> +void task_exit(long error_code) __noreturn;

All in-kernel call sites verified against the source tree:

- kernel/exit.c: definition, EXPORT_SYMBOL, and the three internal
  callers in make_task_dead(), sys_exit(), and do_group_exit() are all
  updated.
- kernel/kthread.c: the four do_exit() calls introduced by patch 1 are
  renamed, along with the kthread_stop() doc comment.
- kernel/bpf/verifier.c: the BTF_ID(func, do_exit) reference is
  correctly updated to BTF_ID(func, task_exit) to match the renamed
  exported symbol.
- All remaining callers (kernel/pid_namespace.c, kernel/reboot.c,
  kernel/seccomp.c, kernel/vhost_task.c, kernel/umh.c, io_uring/,
  security/tomoyo/gc.c, mm/hugetlb.c, fs/cachefiles/namei.c) are
  covered by the diffstat.

Two files in tools/ (virtio/ringtest/main.c and
scripts/kconfig/nconf.c) contain their own unrelated local do_exit
symbol (a bool variable and a static function, respectively). These are
userspace tools that do not reference the kernel function and are
correctly left untouched.

Looks good to me.

Minor Issues selftest: memcg: Skp memcg_sock test if address family not supported 🔗 Waiman Long 1p
The patch modifies test_memcg_sock to skip instead of fail when socket(AF_INET6, SOCK_STREAM, 0) returns EAFNOSUPPORT, by piping errno from the server child process back to the parent via the existing control fd.
tests
Waiman Long <longman@redhat.com>

selftest: memcg: Skip memcg_sock test if address family not supported

The approach of piping errno through ctl_fd is already established in
the code for the bind() failure path, and the placement of the
EAFNOSUPPORT check before the !err success check is correct.

> @@ -1280,8 +1280,11 @@ static int tcp_server(const char *cgroup, void *arg)
>  	saddr.sin6_port = htons(srv_args->port);
>  
>  	sk = socket(AF_INET6, SOCK_STREAM, 0);
> -	if (sk < 0)
> +	if (sk < 0) {
> +		/* Pass back errno to the ctl_fd */
> +		write(ctl_fd, &errno, sizeof(errno));
>  		return ret;
> +	}

> @@ -1412,6 +1415,12 @@ static int test_memcg_sock(const char *root)
>  		close(args.ctl[0]);
>  
> +		/* Skip if address family not supported by protocol */
> +		if (err == EAFNOSUPPORT) {
> +			ret = KSFT_SKIP;
> +			goto cleanup;
> +		}

When err == EAFNOSUPPORT, we goto cleanup with pid unwaited.  The
server child has already exited (it returned after writing errno), so
it becomes a zombie until the parent exits.  The same omission already
exists in the pre-existing "err != EADDRINUSE" path at the same goto,
so this is not a new regression, and cg_destroy() should still succeed
since cgroup_exit() unlinks the task from the cgroup before it becomes
a zombie.  Would it still make sense to add a waitpid(pid, NULL, 0)
here for symmetry with the EADDRINUSE retry path?

Also, the commit message mentions "not configured to support
SOCK_STREAM" as a motivation, but socket() returns EPROTONOSUPPORT in
that case, not EAFNOSUPPORT.  Should EPROTONOSUPPORT also trigger a
skip, or is EAFNOSUPPORT the only errno seen in practice on the
systems this targets?
Looks Good fix kmem over-charging for embedded obj_exts array 🔗 ranxiaokai627@163.com 2p
Two-patch series that avoids over-charging kmem for objects whose slabobj_ext array is stored in slab leftover space or embedded inside the object, by moving obj_exts_in_slab() to slab.h and using it from obj_full_size() in memcontrol.c.
memcontrol slab slub
From: Ran Xiaokai <ran.xiaokai@zte.com.cn>

mm/slab: move obj_exts_in_slab() definition to slab.h
memcg: fix kmem over-charging for embedded obj_exts array

The series looks correct. Notes on what was verified below.

> diff --git a/mm/slab.h b/mm/slab.h
> +static inline bool obj_exts_in_slab(struct kmem_cache *s, struct slab *slab)
> +{
> +	unsigned long obj_exts;
> +	unsigned long start;
> +	unsigned long end;
> +
> +	obj_exts = slab_obj_exts(slab);
> +	if (!obj_exts)
> +		return false;
> +
> +	start = (unsigned long)slab_address(slab);
> +	end = start + slab_size(slab);
> +	return (obj_exts >= start) && (obj_exts < end);
> +}

Verified: slab_obj_exts(), slab_address(), and slab_size() are all
defined in slab.h before this point, so the inline is available to
memcontrol.c which includes "slab.h". The !CONFIG_SLAB_OBJ_EXT stub
returning false is also in the right place.

[ ... ]

> diff --git a/mm/memcontrol.c b/mm/memcontrol.c
> -static inline size_t obj_full_size(struct kmem_cache *s)
> +static inline size_t obj_full_size(struct kmem_cache *s, struct slab *slab)
>  {
> +	if (obj_exts_in_slab(s, slab)) {
> +		/*
> +		 * If obj_exts array uses slab leftover space or is embedded
> +		 * in object, no extra space is allocated, just charge the
> +		 * object size.
> +		 */
> +		return s->size;
> +	}

Verified obj_exts_in_slab() covers both in-slab cases: leftover
space (obj_exts pointer lands after all objects, within slab range)
and embedded-in-object (obj_exts pointer lands inside the first
object's body, still within slab range). Both fall in
[slab_address(slab), slab_address(slab) + slab_size(slab)).
Kmalloc'd obj_exts always land outside that range, so the condition
correctly distinguishes the two situations.

Verified charge/uncharge symmetry: a slab's obj_exts placement is
fixed at creation time by alloc_slab_obj_exts_early() for in-slab
cases, or by alloc_slab_obj_exts() for the kmalloc path. Every
call site that might invoke alloc_slab_obj_exts() guards with
!slab_obj_exts(slab), so an in-slab assignment is never overwritten
by a kmalloc'd one. The placement cannot change between
post_alloc_hook (charge) and free_hook (uncharge).

> -	size_t obj_size = obj_full_size(s);
> +	size_t obj_size = obj_full_size(s, slab);

In __memcg_slab_free_hook, slab->obj_exts is still valid at this
point: the caller memcg_slab_free_hook() captures the pointer with
slab_obj_exts(), then calls get_slab_obj_exts() before invoking
__memcg_slab_free_hook(), and only calls put_slab_obj_exts() after
it returns. So obj_exts_in_slab() cannot observe a zeroed
slab->obj_exts here.

Reviewed-by: <reviewer>

  • [PATCH 2/2] memcg: fix kmem over-charging for embedded obj_exts array
Minor Issues cgroup: improve cgroup_file_notify() scalability 🔗 Shakeel Butt 3p
This three-patch series reduces cgroup_file_notify() lock contention by moving kernfs_notify() outside the critical section, adding lockless fast-path NULL and rate-limit checks, and replacing the global cgroup_file_kn_lock with a per-cgroup_file spinlock. The logic is correct overall but patch 3 silently drops a WRITE_ONCE that patch 2 introduced, creating an asymmetry with the READ_ONCE in the lockless fast-path.
include kernel
Shakeel Butt <shakeel.butt@linux.dev>

cgroup: improve cgroup_file_notify() scalability

Verified: kernfs_get()/kernfs_put() symmetry (both are NULL-safe per
fs/kernfs/dir.c, so cgroup_file_show() is safe), irq-context
correctness of the per-file lock (notify uses irqsave, rm_file and
file_show use spin_lock_irq from process context -- fine), and the
timer callback path (cgroup_file_notify_timer -> cgroup_file_notify
re-enters the same function; the lockless fast-path handles this
correctly because at timer-fire time notified_at has aged past the
interval so time_in_range is false and it falls through to the lock).

[ patch 1/3 looks good ]

[ patch 2/3: lockless fast-path ]

> @@ -1749,7 +1749,7 @@ static void cgroup_rm_file(...)
>  		spin_lock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);
> -		cfile->kn = NULL;
> +		WRITE_ONCE(cfile->kn, NULL);
>  		spin_unlock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);
> ...
> @@ -4429,7 +4429,7 @@ static int cgroup_add_file(...)
>  		spin_lock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);
> -		cfile->kn = kn;
> +		WRITE_ONCE(cfile->kn, kn);
>  		spin_unlock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);

Good -- both write sites are annotated WRITE_ONCE to pair with the
new READ_ONCE(cfile->kn) in the fast-path.

[ patch 3/3: per-cgroup_file lock ]

> @@ -4421,10 +4421,8 @@ static int cgroup_add_file(...)
>  		timer_setup(&cfile->notify_timer, cgroup_file_notify_timer, 0);
> -		spin_lock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);
> -		WRITE_ONCE(cfile->kn, kn);
> -		spin_unlock_irq(&cgroup_file_kn_lock);
> +		spin_lock_init(&cfile->lock);
> +		cfile->kn = kn;

Patch 3 drops the WRITE_ONCE that patch 2 just introduced for
cgroup_add_file().  The commit message argues no concurrent accessors
exist at init time, which is logically correct: cgroup_add_file() is
called under cgroup_mutex, spin_lock_init() is called before the
assignment, and the kernfs node is not visible to any reader until
after kernfs_activate() completes later in cgroup_apply_cftypes().

However, cgroup_file_notify() now reads cfile->kn with READ_ONCE()
in its lockless fast-path, and cgroup_rm_file() still writes
cfile->kn with WRITE_ONCE().  The plain store in cgroup_add_file()
is asymmetric with both of those annotations, and KCSAN would flag
it as an uninstrumented store racing against the READ_ONCE -- even
though the race is impossible in practice.  Could the WRITE_ONCE be
kept here for annotation consistency?

> +	if (time_in_range(jiffies, last, next)) {
> +		timer_reduce(&cfile->notify_timer, next);
> +		if (timer_pending(&cfile->notify_timer))
> +			return;
> +	}
> +
> +	spin_lock_irqsave(&cfile->lock, flags);
> +	if (cfile->kn) {
> +		kn = cfile->kn;
> +		kernfs_get(kn);
> +		WRITE_ONCE(cfile->notified_at, jiffies);
> +	}
> +	spin_unlock_irqrestore(&cfile->lock, flags);

The locked critical section no longer re-checks the rate-limit
interval, so multiple threads that each race past the lockless check
can each acquire cfile->lock in turn and each call kernfs_notify().
The commit message acknowledges this (stale reads lead only to
unnecessary lock acquisition, never to a missed notification).
For the memcg hot-path use case extra notifications are harmless,
so the trade-off is acceptable.

  • [PATCH v2 3/3] cgroup: replace global cgroup_file_kn_lock with per-cgroup_file lock
